PREFACE
   This code of the City of Three Forks, as supplemented, contains ordinances
up to and including Ordinance 406-2025, passed August 12, 2025. Ordinances of
the City adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of this code to
the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith. Consult the
City office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision of the code
has been amended, superseded or repealed.
      American Legal Publishing
      Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not affect the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
ADOPTING ORDINANCE
ORDINANCE NO. 264-2001
   AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING
   THE CITY OF THREE FORKS, MONTANA MUNICIPAL CODE
BE IT ORDAINED by the Mayor and City Council of the City of Three Forks,
Montana, as follows:
   Section 1: From and after the date of passage of this ordinance, the City
Code of the City of Three Forks, Montana prepared by Sterling Codifiers, Inc.
containing the compilation of all ordinances of a general nature together with
the changes made to said ordinances, under the direction of the governing body
of the City, shall be accepted in all courts without question as the official
code and law of the City as enacted by the Mayor and City Council.
   Section 2: There is hereby adopted, as a method of perpetual codification,
the loose-leaf type of binding together with the continuous supplement service,
provided by Sterling Codifiers, Inc., whereby each newly adopted ordinance of a
general and permanent nature amending, altering, adding or deleting provisions
of the official City Code is identified by the proper catchline and is inserted
in the proper place in each of the official copies, one copy of which shall be
maintained in the office of the City Clerk, certified as to correctness and
available for inspection at any and all times that said office is regularly
open.
   Section 3: All ordinances of a general nature included in this official City
Code shall be considered as a continuation of said ordinance provision and the
fact that some provisions have been deliberately eliminated by the governing
body shall not serve to cause any interruption in the continuous effectiveness
of ordinances included in said official City Code. All ordinances of a special
nature, such as tax levy ordinances, bond ordinances, franchises, vacating
ordinances and annexation ordinances shall continue in full force and effect
unless specifically repealed or amended by a provision of the City Code. Such
ordinances are not intended to be included in the official City Code.
   Section 4: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or corporation to
change or amend by additions or deletions, any part or portion of such Code, or
to insert or delete pages or portions thereof, or to alter or tamper with such
Code in any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the City to be
misrepresented thereby.
   Section 5: All ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith, are,
to the extent of such conflict, hereby repealed.
   Section 6: This ordinance and the Code adopted by the same shall be recorded
and shall be in full force and effect from and after its passage, approval and
publication in pamphlet form as provided by law.
PASSED this 12th day of September, 2000.
APPROVED this 12th day of September, 2000.

TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATION
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL CITY CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
Upon the adoption by the City Council, this City Code is hereby declared to be
and shall hereafter constitute the Official City Code of Three Forks. This City
Code of ordinances shall be known and cited as the THREE FORKS CITY CODE and is
hereby published by authority of the City Council and shall be supplemented to
incorporate the most recent legislation of the City as provided in Section
1-1-3 of this Chapter. Any reference to the number of any section contained
herein shall be understood to refer to the position of the same number, its
appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general penalty clause
relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when reference is made to
this City Code by title in any legal documents. (2000 Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
The City Code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be received
without further proof in all courts and in administrative tribunals of this
State as the ordinances of the City of general and permanent effect, except the
excluded ordinances enumerated in Section
 1-2-1 of this Title. (2000 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
Any ordinance amending the City Code shall set forth the title, chapter and
section number of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall
constitute sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to
the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this City Code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifiers, and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of this City Code. Each such replacement page
shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of
the City Code. (2000 Code)
1-1-4: CODE ALTERATIONS:
It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or deface
in any way any section or any page of this City Code in such a manner that the
meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement pages may
be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized by the
City Council. The City Clerk shall see that the replacement pages are properly
inserted in the official copies maintained in the office of the Clerk. Any
person having custody of a copy of the City Code shall make every effort to
maintain said Code current as to the most recent ordinances passed. Such person
shall see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such are
delivered or made available to such person through the office of the City
Clerk. Said Code books, while in actual possession of officials and other
interested persons, shall be and remain the property of the City and shall be
returned to the office of the City Clerk when directed so to do by order of the
City Council. (2000 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal Of General Ordinances; Exceptions
1-2-2: Public Ways And Public Utility Ordinances
1-2-3: Scope And Applicability Of Provisions
1-2-4: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES; EXCEPTIONS:
All general ordinances of the City passed prior to the adoption of this City
Code are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this City Code or are
by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances; appropriation
ordinances; ordinances relating to boundaries and annexations; franchise
ordinances and other ordinances granting special rights to persons or
corporations; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; ordinances
establishing, naming or vacating streets, alleys or other public places;
improvement ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections;
ordinances relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the
City; and all special ordinances. (2000 Code)
1-2-2: PUBLIC WAYS AND PUBLIC UTILITY ORDINANCES:
No ordinance relating to railroad crossings with streets and other public ways,
or relating to the conduct, duties, service or rates of public utilities shall
be repealed by virtue of the adoption of this City Code or by virtue of the
preceding Section, excepting as the City Code may contain provisions for such
matters, in which case, this City Code shall be considered as amending such
ordinance or ordinances in respect to such provisions only. (2000 Code)
1-2-3: SCOPE AND APPLICABILITY OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Effect On Past Actions And Obligations:
      1.   Neither the adoption of this Code nor the consequent repeal or
amendment of any ordinance or part or portion of any ordinance of the City
shall in any manner affect the prosecution for violations of ordinances, which
violations were committed prior to the effective date hereof, nor be construed
as a waiver of any license, fee, or penalty due and unpaid under such
ordinance, or affect the validity of any bond or cash deposit required to be
posted, filed, or deposited pursuant to any such ordinance.
      2.   The repeal provided for in Section
1-2-1 of this Chapter shall not affect any ordinance or resolution promising or
guaranteeing the payment of money to or by the City or any evidence of the
City's indebtedness, or any contract or obligation assumed by the City. Such
repeal shall not affect the annual tax levy; nor shall it affect any right or
franchise conferred by ordinance or resolution on any person or corporation;
nor shall it affect any ordinance relating to the salaries of the City officers
and employees. (1977 Code § 1.02.040)
   B.   Extend To All Repeals: This Section shall extend to all repeals, either
by express words or implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making
any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   C.   Currently Pending Actions: Nothing contained in this Chapter shall be
construed as abating any action now pending under or by virtue of any general
ordinance of the City herein repealed, and the provisions of all general
ordinances contained in this Code shall be deemed to be continuing provisions
and not a new enactment of the same provisions; nor shall this Chapter be
deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying or altering any penalty accrued or
to accrue, or as affecting the liability of any person, firm or corporation, or
as waiving any right of the City under any ordinance or provision thereof in
force at the time of the adoption of this City Code. (2000 Code)
1-2-4: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase
of this City Code, or any part hereof or any portion adopted by reference or
any codes or portions of codes adopted herein is for any reason held to be
unconstitutional or invalid or ineffective by any court of competent
jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity or effectiveness of
the remaining portions of this Code, or any part hereof or any portion adopted
by reference or any codes or portions of codes adopted herein. The City Council
hereby declares that it would have passed each section, subsection,
subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the
fact that any one or more sections, subsections, subdivisions, paragraphs,
sentences, clauses or phrases be declared unconstitutional, invalid or
ineffective. (2000 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Construction Of Words
1-3-2: Definitions, General
1-3-3: Catchlines
1-3-1: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
   A.   Whenever any word in any section of this City Code importing the plural
number is used in describing or referring to any matters, parties or persons,
any single matter, party or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used. When any subject matter, party or
person is referred to in this City Code by words importing the singular number
only, or a particular gender, several matters, parties or persons and the
opposite gender and bodies corporate shall be deemed to be included; provided,
that these rules of construction shall not be applied to any section of this
City Code which contains any express provision excluding such construction or
where the subject matter or context may be repugnant thereto.
   B.   The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the City has been
changed in the content of this City Code to "Title", "Chapter", "Section" and/
or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and clarification
purposes only. Such change to the City's ordinances is not meant to amend
passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (2000 Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
Whenever the following words or terms are used in this Code, they shall have
such meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
   AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another with authority conferred, either
expressly or by implication.
   CITY: The City of Three Forks, County of Gallatin, State of Montana.
   CODE: The City Code of the City of Three Forks.
   COUNCIL: Unless otherwise indicated, the Council of the City of Three Forks.
   COUNTY: The County of Gallatin, State of Montana.
   EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a City employee by
title only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the
City of Three Forks".
   FISCAL YEAR: The fiscal year of the City shall commence on July 1 of each
year.
   GENDER: A word importing either the masculine or feminine gender only shall
extend and be applied to the other gender and to persons.
   LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business,
profession or occupation.
   MCA: Abbreviation for Montana Code Annotated.
   NUISANCE: Anything offensive to the sensibilities of reasonable persons, or
any act or activity creating a hazard which threatens the health and welfare of
inhabitants of the City, or any activity which by its perpetuation can
reasonably be said to have a detrimental effect on the property of a person or
persons within the community.
   OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
   OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this Code or the omission of
any act required by the provisions of this Code.
   OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a City officer by title
only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of the City of
Three Forks".
   OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or
profession.
   OWNER: As applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
   PERSON: Any public or private corporation, firm, partnership, association,
organization, government or any other group acting as a unit, as well as a
natural person.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods,
chattels, effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by
which any pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created,
acknowledged, transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and
every right or interest therein.
   RETAILER: Unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to
relate to the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things direct to the
consumer.
   RIGHT OF WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of the roadway or other
property.
   STATE: The State of Montana.
   STREET: Shall include alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public
squares, public places and sidewalks.
   TENANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land, whether alone or with
others.
   WHOLESALER: The terms "wholesaler" and "wholesale dealer" as used in this
Code, unless otherwise specifically defined, shall be understood to relate to
the sale of goods, merchandise, articles or things to persons who purchase for
the purpose of resale.
   WRITTEN, IN WRITING: May include printing and any other mode of representing
words and letters, but when the written signature of any person is required by
law to any official or public writing or bond, it shall be in the proper
handwriting of such person, or in case such person is unable to write, by such
person's proper mark. (2000 Code)
1-3-3: CATCHLINES:
The catchlines of the several sections of the City Code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when
any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or reenacted. (2000
Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers
1-4-4: Execution Of Sentences
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY 1 :
Unless specifically provided elsewhere in this code or state statute, any
person found to have been in violation of any of the terms and provisions of
this code shall be sentenced to a fine in an amount not to exceed five hundred
dollars ($500.00), six (6) months' imprisonment, and/or ordered to provide
community service or any combination of fine, imprisonment and community
service not to exceed the limits set herein. Each day that a violation
continues shall be deemed to be a separate offense. The city court may impose a
court fee in the amount established by the city council for each violation of
the city code. (Ord. 357-15, 4-14-2015)
 
Notes
1 1. MCA §§ 7-5-109, 7-5-4207.
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   Application Of Penalty: The penalty provided in this chapter shall be
applicable to every section of this code the same as though it were a part of
each and every separate section.
   B.   Acts Punishable Under Different Sections: In all cases where the same
offense is made punishable or is created by different clauses or sections of
this code, the prosecuting officer may elect under which to proceed, but not
more than one recovery shall be had against the same person for the same
offense; provided, that the revocation of a license or permit shall not be
considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar any other penalty being enforced.
   C.   Breach Of Provisions: Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to
do any act constitutes a breach of any section or provision of this code and
there shall be no fine or penalty specifically declared for such breach, the
provisions of this chapter shall apply. (2000 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS:
No provision of this code designating the duties of any officer or employee
shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee liable for any fine
or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty, unless the intention of
the city council to impose such fine or penalty on such officer or employee is
specifically and clearly expressed in the section creating the duty. (2000
Code)
1-4-4: EXECUTION OF SENTENCES:
   A.   Officer Of Jurisdiction: If any person shall plead guilty or shall be
convicted of a breach, infraction or violation of any ordinance now or
hereafter enacted or in force in the city, the judgment must be executed by a
police officer of the city. (1977 Code § 9.08.010; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-
10, 11-10-2009)
   B.   Judgment Of Imprisonment: When a judgment of imprisonment is entered, a
certified copy thereof must be delivered to the city judge, which is a
sufficient warrant for its execution.
   C.   Imposition Of Fine: If a judgment is rendered imposing a fine only,
without imprisonment for nonpayment, and the defendant is not detained for any
other legal cause, he must be discharged as soon as the judgment is given.
   D.   Imprisonment For Satisfaction Of Fine:
      1.   A judgment that the defendant pay a fine may also direct that he be
imprisoned until the fine be satisfied, in the proportion of one day's
imprisonment for the daily rate of credit for incarceration established
annually by the Gallatin County commissioners.
      2.   When such a judgment is rendered, the defendant must be held in
custody for the time specified in the judgment, unless the fine is sooner paid.
   E.   Payment To Judge: Any officer charged with the collection of fines,
under the provisions of this section, must return the execution to the judge
within thirty (30) days from its delivery to him and pay over to the judge the
money collected therefrom, deducting his fees for the collection.
   F.   Receipt For Fines Collected: All fines imposed and collected by a city
court must be paid to the city treasurer within thirty (30) days after the
receipt of the same, and the city judge must take duplicate receipts therefor,
one of which he must deposit with the city clerk. (1977 Code § 9.08.010; amd.
2000 Code)
CHAPTER 5
OFFICIAL AND CORPORATE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
1-5-1: Corporate Seal
1-5-1: CORPORATE SEAL:
   A.   Form: The Corporate Seal of the City shall be circular in form with the
words "City of Three Forks, Montana", on the upper part of the outer circle,
and the words "County of Gallatin", on the lower part of said circle; and on
the upper part of the smaller and interior circle the word "Incorporated", on
the lower part of said circle the figures "1910", and in the center of said
interior circle the word "Seal" in large letters. (1977 Code § 2.04.010)
   B.   Authentication Of Documents: The Corporate Seal shall be used to
authenticate all ordinances, and resolutions having the force and effect of an
ordinance, all contracts entered into by the City, on the part of the City
Council or authorized by the City Council, on all warrants drawn on the City
Clerk, and on all acts on the part of the City Council or City officers duly
authorized by the City Council whereby the City is intended to be bound. (1977
Code § 2.04.020)
CHAPTER 6
MAYOR AND CITY COUNCIL
SECTION:
1-6-1: Elections; Terms Of Office
1-6-2: Composition; Membership
1-6-3: Qualifications Of Mayor And Council
1-6-4: Salaries
1-6-5: Meetings; Place And Time
1-6-6: Notice Of Public Meetings
1-6-7: Rules And Order Of Business
1-6-8: Powers And Duties
1-6-9: Ordinance Enactment And Passage
1-6-10: Special Committees
1-6-11: Contract For Work And Labor
1-6-12: Absence Of Mayor
1-6-1: ELECTIONS; TERMS OF OFFICE 1 :
On the first Tuesday after the first Monday in November of every odd numbered
year, a city election shall be held, at which the qualified electors of the
city shall elect the officers of the city whose term of office will expire,
with council members to be voted for who represent the city at large; the mayor
to hold office for a term of four (4) years, and until the qualification of
his/her successor; and each council member so elected to hold office for a term
of four (4) years, and until the qualification of his/her successor. (Ord. 369-
2016, 10-11-2016)
 
Notes
1 1. MCA § 13-1-104.
1-6-2: COMPOSITION; MEMBERSHIP:
The city council shall be composed of the mayor and six (6) council members at
large of the city limits, who, upon receiving notice of their election, shall,
before entering upon their duties, severally, take and subscribe to an oath or
affirmation before some officer authorized to administer the same, which a copy
shall be filed in the office of the city clerk and the original sent to the
county clerk and recorder, that he/she will support the constitution of the
United States, the constitution of the state, and will discharge the duties
required of him/her by law. The council shall, within three (3) weeks after a
vacancy occurs in the city council, fill that vacancy through the appropriate
appointment procedures as authorized by the laws of the state. (Ord. 369-2016,
10-11-2016)
1-6-3: QUALIFICATIONS OF MAYOR AND COUNCIL:
   A.   Mayor: No person is eligible for the office of mayor unless he/she:
      1.   Is at least eighteen (18) years old;
      2.   A citizen of Montana and a qualified elector pursuant to article IV,
section 2 of the Montana constitution.
   B.   Council Member: No person is eligible for the office of council unless
he/she:
      1.   Is at least eighteen (18) years old;
      2.   A citizen of Montana and a qualified elector pursuant to article IV,
section 2 of the Montana constitution. (Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
1-6-4: SALARIES:
   A.   Mayor: The annual salary which shall be allowed and paid to the mayor
shall be set and paid annually by the city council. (1977 Code § 2.44.010)
   B.   Council Members: The city council members shall each be allowed and
paid the amount set annually by the council, per diem for each day of session
of the city council; provided, however, that no council member shall be paid
for more than two (2) days' service during any one month. (1977 Code §
2.44.020)
1-6-5: MEETINGS; PLACE AND TIME:
   A.   Council Meeting Place:
      1.   Meeting Place Designated: In the interest of economy, and for the
purpose of concentrating the business of the city, the city office at 206 Main
Street is hereby designated and established as the place for holding all
meetings of the city council, or at such other location as the council may
determine based on the city's needs by resolution.
   B.   Regular Meetings:
      1.   The City Council shall hold regular meetings on the second Tuesday
of each month, and on the fourth Tuesday of each month as needed. Each regular
meeting shall be set via resolution of the City Council.
      2.   The city council may adjourn any regular meeting to any specified
time, and may adjourn any meeting from time to time, and such adjourned regular
meeting, for the purpose of the passage of any ordinance, or the transaction of
any business required by law or ordinance to be transacted at a regular meeting
of said council, shall be considered a regular meeting.
   C.   Special Meetings: The city council may hold special meetings at the
call of the mayor, and it shall be the duty of the mayor to call a special
meeting of the city council whenever in his/her judgment a special meeting
shall be necessary, or whenever the mayor shall be requested to do so by the
written request of three (3) council members. Such special meeting shall be
called by a written notice from the mayor, to be served upon each council
member by any such means.
   D.   Open Meetings: All meetings of the city council shall be open to the
public, except as provided in section 2-3-203, Montana Code Annotated. (Ord.
369-2016, 10-11-2016; Ord. 396-2022, 7-12-2022)
1-6-6: NOTICE OF PUBLIC MEETINGS:
   A.   Public notice will be provided on the windows of city hall located at
206 Main Street, Three Forks, Montana, on the public bulletin boards at three
(3) banks in Three Forks located at 120 South Montana Street, 320 South Main
Street, and 2 North Railway Avenue, on the city of Three Forks website, and in
a newspaper of general circulation if deemed necessary to ensure public
participation which has complied with section 7-1-4127, Montana Code Annotated.
(Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
1-6-7: RULES AND ORDER OF BUSINESS:
   A.   Quorum: A majority of council members elected in the city, with the
presiding officer, shall constitute a quorum to do business; but a smaller
number when present may compel the attendance of the absent member(s) by
sending law enforcement to require their attendance. If any absent member shall
refuse or neglect to attend a session of the council when notified as herein
mentioned, the council may, by a majority vote, pass and adopt a resolution
prescribing such punishment as may seem just and reasonable, up to and
including removal from office as defined in section 2.08 of the city charter;
provided if said delinquent member at a succeeding meeting of the council
renders an excuse which shall be satisfactory to the council, he/she shall be
released from said fine.
   B.   Roll Call; Order Of Business: At the hour appointed for the meeting,
the council shall be called to order by the mayor, or in his absence by the
president of the council, or in the absence of both, by any council member
present. The roll of members elected shall first be called to determine if a
quorum is present. If the roll call shows a quorum not present, the clerk must
announce and the members present may adjourn to such time as the urgency of
business shall require or a majority may be had; but if the roll call shows a
quorum present the council may proceed with business. (Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-
2016)
1-6-8: POWERS AND DUTIES:
   A.   General: The council shall ensure the record of its proceedings are
open to the public; shall determine its own rules of action; shall protect
itself from indignities and interruptions from bystanders and spectators, and
it shall be unlawful for any person, not a member of the council, to
participate in its deliberations, or to address the council, except upon
special permission granted by the council. (Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
   B.   Passage Of Ordinances And Resolutions: The council shall have power to
pass all needful ordinances and resolutions for the promotion of the public
interest and good government of the city, and from time to time adopt such
rules and bylaws for its own regulation and procedure as may be deemed
necessary. (1977 Code § 2.16.040; amd. Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
1-6-9: ORDINANCE ENACTMENT AND PASSAGE:
   A.   Proposed Ordinance Presentation: Ordinance proposals and amendments to
existing ordinances typically start at the ordinance committee level, but may
be presented to the city council by any city staff member or member of the
general public. At the ordinance committee level discussion takes place on how
to word the proposed ordinance or amendment to existing ordinance. Every
proposed ordinance shall be read in its entirety to the city council at the
publicly noticed meeting it is scheduled for. The ordinance committee may take
the first reading of the ordinance back to further consider, revise and/or make
recommendation.
   B.   Ordinance Committee Recommendations: Every proposed ordinance referred
to the ordinance committee may be reported back to the city council at the next
regular meeting of said council with such recommendation of passage and
approval, or changes to be made as may seem right and proper, just and
equitable. The recommendations of the ordinance committee shall be presented in
the revised ordinance.
   C.   Council Actions On Recommendations: The council shall consider the
recommendations of the ordinance committee, on any ordinance referred to it,
and pass any ordinance, or adopt and approve the changes as may be recommended,
or refer it back to the ordinance committee as may be required, and when
returned to the council by the ordinance committee, and before placed upon its
final passage, shall be read at length, then put upon its final passage.
   D.   Mayor; Veto Powers: Refer to section 7-5-4205, Montana Code Annotated.
      1.   Ordinance Appropriating Money: Any ordinance appropriating money
shall be subject to the veto of the mayor, and the mayor may veto any one item
or several items in such ordinance, and if such item or items be not passed
over his veto, such item or items shall be stricken out and shall not be paid
by the city treasurer. (1977 Code § 2.16.100)
   E.   Repeal Of Ordinance: Whenever any ordinance, or part of an ordinance,
shall be repealed or modified by a subsequent ordinance, the ordinance or part
of an ordinance thus repealed or modified shall continue in force until the
repealing ordinance shall go into effect, or until such time as may be
specially designated in said repealing ordinance. (1977 Code § 1.04.060)
   F.   Style Of Ordinance: The style of the ordinances of the city shall be
"Be it Ordained by the Three Forks City Council"; and all ordinances shall be
signed by the mayor, president of the council or the presiding officer
thereof,and attested by the city clerk with the seal of incorporation of the
city affixed thereon, and shall be posted, unless the council shall direct said
ordinances to be published once in a newspaper designated by the city. (Ord.
369-2016, 10-11-2016; amd. Ord. 383-2019; 9-10-2019)
1-6-10: SPECIAL COMMITTEES:
The mayor shall designate and appoint such standing and special committees as
may be from time to time provided by the rules and orders of the council, as
provided in section 3.08 of the city charter. (Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
1-6-11: CONTRACT FOR WORK AND LABOR:
All contracts for work and labor, or for supplies, or materials, shall be
authorized and approved in compliance with state law. (1977 Code § 2.16.090;
amd. Ord. 369-2016, 10-11-2016)
1-6-12: ABSENCE OF MAYOR:
In the absence of the mayor, the president of the city council, or in his
absence the vice president of the council, if there shall be such an officer,
shall perform all the duties and functions of the mayor as may be required by
the ordinances of the city, and part 4, title 3 of the political code of the
state of Montana. (1977 Code § 2.16.120)
CHAPTER 7
CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-7-1: Appointments By Mayor
1-7-2: Salaries
1-7-3: City Judge
1-7-1: APPOINTMENTS BY MAYOR:
   A.   City Clerk 1 ; Police Officers: The mayor shall nominate and, by and
with the consent of the council, appoint one city clerk, and one or more police
officers. (1977 Code § 2.02.010; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
   B.   City Judge:
      1.   Appointment: The mayor shall appoint a city judge. (1977 Code §
2.02.020; amd. 2000 Code)
      2.   Maintain Courtroom: Said city judge must keep and maintain at all
times during his term of office, at a certain place, and within the limits of
the city, a courtroom, which shall be open at times designated by the judge.
The criminal jurisdiction of said judge shall be as provided by the Montana
statutes governing city courts. (1977 Code § 2.02.030; amd. 2000 Code)
   C.   Street Superintendent: Annually the mayor shall appoint the street
superintendent of the city. (1977 Code § 2.32.010; amd. 2000 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also article A of this chapter.
1-7-2: SALARIES:
The salaries of the appointed city officials shall be reviewed and set annually
by the city council. (2000 Code)
1-7-3: CITY JUDGE:
The city judge shall, before entering upon the duties of the office, take the
oath required by law and file the same with the city clerk, for the faithful
performance of the duties of the office as required by law and the ordinances
of the city, and that the city judge will pay over all monies which shall come
into the city court's hands to the person entitled to receive the same, and at
the expiration of the city judge's term of office to surrender to and deposit
with the city judge's successor in office all records and files of the office
of the city judge. (Ord. 350-15, 2-24-2015)
ARTICLE A. CITY CLERK AND CITY TREASURER
SECTION:
1-7A-1: Combining Offices
1-7A-2: Bond Required
1-7A-3: Discharge Duties Of City Clerk
1-7A-4: Collection Of Special Assessments
1-7A-5: Payment Of Special Improvement Assessments
1-7A-6: Delinquent Tax
1-7A-1: COMBINING OFFICES:
The offices of city clerk and/or city treasurer may be combined and one person
may hold both offices, at the discretion of the mayor, subject to the approval
and consent of the council. (1977 Code § 2.42.010)
1-7A-2: BOND REQUIRED:
Bonds shall be posted for the position as required by the city council, and
shall be paid for by the city. (1977 Code § 2.42.030)
1-7A-3: DISCHARGE DUTIES OF CITY CLERK:
   A.   Authorization: The city clerk is hereby empowered, authorized and
required to discharge all of the duties and exercise all of the powers and
authority of the city clerk. In absence of the city clerk or at the direction
of the city clerk, the deputy city clerk shall perform the enumerated duties.
   B.   Duties Enumerated:
      1.   To attend all meetings of the council, to record and sign the
proceedings thereof and all ordinances, bylaws, resolutions and contracts
passed, adopted or entered into, and to sign, number and keep a record of all
licenses, commissions or permits granted or authorized by the council.
      2.   To enter in a book all ordinances, resolutions and bylaws passed and
adopted by the council. Such book is called "the ordinance book".
      3.   To enter in a book kept for that purpose the date, amount and person
in whose favor and for what purpose warrants are drawn. Such book is called
"the finance book".
      4.   To countersign and cause to be published or posted as provided by
law, all ordinances, bylaws or resolutions passed and adopted by the council.
      5.   To make and certify copies of all records, books and papers in his/
her possession, on the payment of like fees as are allowed county clerks; which
fees must be paid into the city treasury.
      6.   To file and keep all records, books, papers or property belonging to
the city, and to deliver the same to his/her successor when qualified.
      7.   To give notice of all elections as required by law, and to notify
all persons of their election or appointment to office.
      8.   To make and keep a complete index of the journal, ordinance book,
finance book, and all other books and papers on file in his/her office.
      9.   To perform such duties in and about the assessment, levy and
collection of taxes and assessments as may be prescribed by law or ordinances.
      10.   To take and administer oaths, but must not charge or receive any
fees therefor.
      11.   To perform such other and further duties as the council and/or
mayor may prescribe, which then might be performed or exercised by the city
clerk.
   C.   Signing Of Warrants And Other Documents: The city clerk shall be
required to sign any warrant, contract or other document or paper of any kind,
or to attest the minutes of the city council. In absence of the city clerk, the
deputy clerk is hereby authorized and required to attach thereto the official
signature as ex officio city clerk. (Ord. 351-15, 2-24-2015)
1-7A-4: COLLECTION OF SPECIAL ASSESSMENTS:
   A.   City Treasurer: The city treasurer may collect special assessments,
when: any city whose taxes for general, municipal and administrative purposes
are certified to and collected by the county treasurer, in accordance with the
provisions of sections 7-6-4407 and 7-6-4423, Montana Code Annotated, may,
nevertheless, provide by ordinance for the collection by its city or treasurer
of all special assessments and taxes levied and assessed in accordance with any
of the provisions of this act in the same manner and at the same time as said
taxes for general, municipal and administrative purposes are collected by the
county treasurer and all of the provisions of section 7-6-4423, Montana Code
Annotated shall apply to the collection of such special taxes and assessments
in the same manner as such provisions apply to the collection of other city
taxes. When the payment of any one installment of any special assessment
becomes delinquent, all payments of subsequent installments shall, at the
option of the city council, by appropriate resolution, duly adopted, become
delinquent, and such delinquent special assessments shall be certified to the
county clerk of the county in which such city is situated, and the county
treasurer must collect such delinquent special assessments and taxes in the
same manner and at the same time as said taxes for general, municipal and
administrative purposes are collected by him/her and in case the same are not
paid, the whole property shall be sold, the same as other property is sold for
taxes.
   B.   City Clerk: The city clerk shall collect all special assessments and
taxes levied and assessed by the city in accordance with any of the provisions,
by state law, in the same manner and at the same time as taxes for general,
municipal and administrative purposes are collected by the county treasurer.
(Ord. 351-15, 2-24-2015)
1-7A-5: PAYMENT OF SPECIAL IMPROVEMENT ASSESSMENTS:
Special assessments, or installments of special assessments, made for special
improvements in cities, duly and regularly made and levied by resolution,
according to law, shall be payable on or before five o'clock (5:00) P.M. on
November 30 and May 31 of each year, and in the event the same are not paid on
or before said date, the same shall be subject to the same interest and penalty
for nonpayment as are or may hereafter be provided by the laws of the state for
other delinquent taxes. (Ord. 351-15, 2-24-2015)
1-7A-6: DELINQUENT TAX:
   A.   Delinquent Tax Or Assessment: Whenever, in a city whose treasurer
collects its own taxes or special assessments, or both thereof, any such taxes
or assessments shall become delinquent, no tax sale shall be held by such city
treasurer therefore, but such city treasurer must, within ten (10) days after
the date the same become delinquent, certify all such delinquent taxes and
assessments to the county treasurer of the county in which the city is
situated. Such certificate shall contain the description of each lot or parcel
of land on which any tax or assessment has become delinquent, the name and
address of the person to whom assessed, the date when the same became
delinquent, the amount of the delinquent tax or assessment, the penalty to be
added thereto, and the total amount of such delinquent tax or assessment with
penalty added.
   B.   Installments: If any special assessment is payable in installments and
any installment thereof becomes delinquent, the amount of such delinquent
installment shall be included in such certificate; provided, however, that if
the city council, by the adoption of an appropriate resolution, shall declare
the whole of the assessment remaining unpaid to be delinquent, as provided in
section 7-12-4181 (7-12-4183), Montana Code Annotated, then the whole of the
assessment remaining unpaid shall be included in such certificate. (Ord. 351-
15, 2-24-2015)
ARTICLE B. CITY ATTORNEY
SECTION:
1-7B-1: Office Created; Term; Duties
1-7B-2: Salary Or Retainer Fee
1-7B-1: OFFICE CREATED; TERM; DUTIES:
   A.   Creation; Term: There is hereby created in and for the city, the office
of city attorney whose term of office shall be for the period of two (2) years
running from July 1 to June 30 to coincide with the city's annual budget, and
until his/her successor shall be duly appointed and qualified. (Ord. 335-13, 9-
10-2013)
   B.   Duties: It shall be the duty of the city attorney:
      1.   Attend Court; Prosecutions For The City: To attend before the city
court and other courts, and prosecute on behalf of the city, and to attend all
suits, matters and things in which the city may be legally interested. In no
case must the city attorney defend or act as an attorney for the defendant in a
criminal action or proceeding.
      2.   Render Advice: To give his/her advice or opinion in writing when
required by the mayor or council, and to do all such things touching his/her
office as the council may require, or any ordinance may prescribe.
      3.   Draw Contracts: To draw for the use of the council and/or mayor any
contract, resolution or ordinance.
      4.   City Attorney: The city attorney is hereby empowered, authorized and
required to discharge all of the duties and exercise all of the powers and
authority of the city clerk whenever said clerk is absent from the city, and
whenever said clerk is unable or unwilling to discharge the duties of his/her
office.
      5.   Other Duties: To perform such other and further duties as the
council and/or mayor may prescribe. (Ord. 352-15, 2-24-2015)
   C.   Employ Additional Attorneys: The council may employ other or additional
attorneys or counsel in special cases, and provide for the payment for their
services. (1977 Code § 2.20.010; amd. 2000 Code)
1-7B-2: SALARY OR RETAINER FEE:
The salary or retainer fee of the herein named officer shall be reviewed and
set annually by the city council. (1977 Code § 2.20.020)
   1-7C ()CHAPTER 7
   CITY OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
ARTICLE C. CITY ENGINEER
SECTION:
1-7C-1: Appointment; Term
1-7C-2: Qualifications; Oath
1-7C-3: Compensation
1-7C-4: Duties
1-7C-5: Deliver Books And Property To Successor
1-7C-6: Interfering With Work Of Engineer
1-7C-1: APPOINTMENT; TERM:
The City Council may create the office of City Engineer, or may contract for
engineering services in and for the City. The office of City Engineer shall be
appointed by the Mayor, with the approval of the Council, and shall hold his
office until his successor is appointed and qualified. (1977 Code § 2.26.010;
amd. 2000 Code)
1-7C-2: QUALIFICATIONS; OATH:
The person appointed to the office of City Engineer shall be a suitable and
competent person and shall possess a practical knowledge of surveying and civil
engineering. He shall, in addition to the oath prescribed for City officers,
take an oath that he is not and will not, during his continuance in office,
either directly or indirectly, be interested in any contract with the City for
any work or material furnished. (1977 Code § 2.26.020)
1-7C-3: COMPENSATION:
The City Engineer shall receive for performing such duties as may be required
of him, such fair and reasonable compensation as may be agreed upon between the
City Council and himself from time to time. (1977 Code § 2.26.080)
1-7C-4: DUTIES:
   A.   Engineering And Surveying:
      1.   It shall be the duty of the City Engineer to do and perform within
the City all engineering and surveying; to locate and establish the lines and
grades of all streets, avenues, alleys, sidewalks, gutters, sewers, waterworks,
or other public works or appurtenances, under the order of the City Council and
subject to its approval; to prepare and preserve, in his office, plans, maps or
profiles of the same, and keep them subject to inspection at all reasonable
times; to make estimates and furnish specifications for any of said work
whenever required to do so by the City Council; to inspect the work of grading
streets, construction of gutters and sewers, and of laying down sidewalks. He
shall have the general supervision of all contract or other work and see that
it is performed in a workmanlike manner and in accordance with the authorized
plans, and in conformity with the terms of the contract and specifications when
directed by the City Council, and perform such other duties as may, from time
to time, be prescribed by ordinance, resolution or order of the City Council.
(1977 Code § 2.26.040)
      2.   All surveys, notes of surveys, field notes, maps or profiles, plans
and estimates made by him or others in his employ for the City shall be the
property of the City, and shall be carefully preserved in his office and open
to the inspection of all persons interested. He shall also make a certified
copy of all surveys, notes of surveys, field notes, maps or profiles, plans and
estimates and file the same in the office of the City Clerk. (1977 Code §
2.26.050)
   B.   Suggestion Of Materials: The City Engineer shall inform and suggest to
the City Council the kind and quality of material to be used in all public
works, the necessary means to ensure permanent stability of the work, and at
all times aid the City Council with his professional knowledge and skill. (1977
Code § 2.26.060)
   C.   Prepare And Certify Assessment Lists: He shall prepare and certify to
the City Council all assessment lists for improvements which are chargeable to
the abutting property, and shall, at the end of each fiscal year, make an
annual report to the City Council of the work of his office, showing extent and
cost of all work and improvements done by him, or over which he has had
supervision. (1977 Code § 2.26.070)
1-7C-5: DELIVER BOOKS AND PROPERTY TO SUCCESSOR:
The City Engineer shall, at the expiration of his term of office, turn over and
deliver to his successor in office, all books, papers, profiles, maps,
estimates and other property of any kind whatsoever in his hands, or belonging
to the City, taking therefor duplicate receipts, in which receipts all books,
papers, plans, maps, profiles and estimates and other property shall be
specifically numbered, one of which receipts shall be transmitted to the City
Council within five (5) days after the expiration of his term of office. (1977
Code § 2.26.090)
1-7C-6: INTERFERING WITH WORK OF ENGINEER:
If any person shall interrupt or molest the City Engineer while engaged in his
official duty, by driving a vehicle of any kind against the person or surveying
instruments or other professional apparatus of said City Engineer or any of his
assistants, or by wilfully moving or displacing any stake or other landmark
fixed or determined by him or his assistants, or by wilfully causing or
offering them any kind of bodily injury or hindrance, such person so offending
shall be subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1977 Code § 2.26.100; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 8
MUNICIPAL ELECTIONS
SECTION:
1-8-1: Registration Of Electors
1-8-1: REGISTRATION OF ELECTORS:
   A.   Requirement: The city council wholly provides by this subsection for
the registration of electors in the city, and may prohibit any person from
voting at any election unless he has been registered, but such subsection must
not be in conflict with the general law providing for the registration of
electors, and must not change the qualifications of electors except as allowed
by the state. However, when an area is annexed by the city after the date for
registration has expired, opportunity must be provided for residents of such
area to register, if otherwise qualified, for all future elections. (1977 Code
§ 1.12.020)
   B.   Compliance With State Law: Registration shall be governed by state law.
(1977 Code § 2.50.010)

CHAPTER 1
IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT AND SEWER WARRANTS
SECTION:
3-1-1: Levy Of Assessment And Tax
3-1-2: Improvement Of Sewer District
3-1-3: Improvement District Or Sewer Warrant
3-1-4: Book Of Records
3-1-5: Cancel And Delivery Of Warrants
3-1-6: Form And Issuance Of Warrants
3-1-1: LEVY OF ASSESSMENT AND TAX:
It shall be the duty of the City Council to annually levy an assessment and tax
for the payment of the principal and interest of all special improvement
district and sewer warrants, which may be issued by order of the City Council
on and after the passage and approval of this Chapter. (1977 Code § 3.04.010)
3-1-2: IMPROVEMENT OF SEWER DISTRICT:
   A.   Establish Account: Whenever a special improvement or sewer district is
created by the City for the purpose of constructing sewers, improving the
streets, alleys and highways of said district, or opening, changing or altering
any streets, alleys and highways within the limits of said district, it shall
be the duty of the City Clerk to open an account against the said improvement
or sewer district so created, and said account shall be kept in a book provided
for the purpose. In such account, the Clerk shall charge all cost and expense
connected therewith, as prescribed in the resolution and ordinance creating
said district; and the City Clerk shall issue, by direction of the City
Council, special improvement district or sewer warrants of the kind and
character described in the ordinances relating to the form thereof, and
charging such account with said warrants, and the book of records shall state
the date of such improvement district or sewer warrants, to whom issued and the
amount thereof, to the end that the cost of and the purposes for which said
improvement or sewer district is created, shall be at all times a matter of
public record.
   B.   Warrants Redeemed: When such warrants shall have been redeemed and paid
by the City Treasurer, as hereinafter provided, the respective accounts of said
special improvement and sewer districts shall be properly credited with
warrants so redeemed. (1977 Code § 3.04.020)
3-1-3: IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT OR SEWER WARRANT:
   A.   Presentation For Payment: Whenever a special improvement district or
sewer warrant shall have been issued by the City, and said warrant shall bear
upon its face the regularity of issuance, as prescribed in this Chapter
relating thereto, it shall be presented to the City Clerk for payment.
   B.   No Funds; Register Warrant: If there are no funds to the credit of the
said special improvement district fund sufficient to pay said warrant, it shall
be the duty of the City Clerk to register said special improvement or sewer
warrant in a book to be provided for the purpose, and said registry shall set
forth the number of the special improvement or sewer district, the date of
registration of said warrant and the amount of such warrant, the person to whom
said warrant is issued, and the City Clerk shall endorse upon the face of said
warrant the date of registration of said warrant and shall affix his signature
thereto. (1977 Code § 3.04.030)
3-1-4: BOOK OF RECORDS:
   A.   Preparation Of Book: It shall be the duty of the City Clerk to prepare
a book of records which shall be known as the "Register of Special Improvement
District and Sewer Warrants", and whenever a special improvement or sewer
district is created and designated by proper number, it shall be the duty of
the City Clerk to open in said book of registration, an account with each
special improvement or sewer district, giving such account its proper number
and he shall enter in said book of registration a proper record of all special
improvement district or sewer warrants presented to him for registration or
payment, issued under their respective districts, as in the manner provided in
subsection
3-1-2A of this Chapter.
   B.   Credit Accounts: It is further prescribed as the duty of the City Clerk
to credit each special improvement and sewer district account from time to time
as the same is paid with all taxes and assessments which may be collected by
him on account of special taxes or assessments levied against the respective
special improvement and sewer districts, and he shall apply the fund so
collected in the following manner:
      1.   First: From the monies collected on account of any special
improvement or sewer district, in each year, he shall provide for the payments
of interest on or before January 1, in each year, to that date on any and all
outstanding warrants of each respective special improvement and sewer district,
whereon interest has not ceased, by reason of said warrants being called for
payment, and shall endorse said payment of interest on the reverse side of each
warrant with the interest so paid, or by taking up and cancelling the interest
coupons representing such interest if any such coupons be attached to said
warrants. The first payment of interest shall be computed for the period from
date of registration of each of said warrants to January 1 next succeeding such
date of registration and annually thereafter.
      2.   Second: Out of the remainder of any funds to the credit of such
respective improvement or sewer districts, the City Clerk shall then call in
and pay warrants to the amount of such monies on hand available for the
purpose, so far as such funds will pay and retire the amount that may be due,
with accrued interest, to date of call for redemption and payment, fixing by
notice the date whereon the interest shall cease upon such warrant and it shall
be the duty of the City Clerk to note upon such register the date of call and
to notify the holders of said warrants by letter, if known, or by publication
in a paper of general circulation published in the City, the call for the
redemption of said warrants and the date when interest on said warrants shall
cease. (1977 Code § 3.04.040)
3-1-5: CANCEL AND DELIVERY OF WARRANTS:
It shall be the duty of the City Clerk, at any time after the redemption and
payment of any special improvement or sewer district warrants, as hereinafter
mentioned, to cancel and deliver the same to the City Clerk and take his
receipt therefor, to the end that such warrants when paid and cancelled shall
be properly filed in the office of the City Clerk. (1977 Code § 3.04.050)
3-1-6: FORM AND ISSUANCE OF WARRANTS:
   A.   Form: All special improvement or sewer district warrants from and after
November 27, 1911, and the passage of this Chapter, shall be in form and
language, substantially as follows:
   Special Improvement Or Sewer District Warrants
No.      Amount $             District No.     
   Three Forks, Montana,
                             20**
The City of Three Forks, Montana, will pay to the order of
                        the sum of                Dollars, ($        ), as
authorized by Resolution No.          creating Special Improvement or Sewer
District No.       as therein described, passed provisionally on the        and
finally passed and approved on the                , laws, resolutions and
ordinances relating thereto in payment of the contract in accordance therewith.
This Warrant bears interest at the rate of      per cent annum from the date of
registration of this warrant, as expressed herein, until the date called for
redemption by the City Clerk. The interest on this warrant is payable annually
on the        day of                  in each year unless otherwise paid
previous thereto, and as expressed in the interest coupons hereto attached.
This Warrant is payable from the collection of a special tax or assessment
which is a lien against the real estate within said district, as described in
said resolution hereinbefore referred to.
This warrant is redeemable at the option of the City at any time there are
funds to the credit of said Improvement District Fund, for the redemption
thereof, and in the manner provided for the redemption of the same.
It is hereby certified and recited that all acts and things required to be done
precedent to the issuance of this warrant, have been done, happened and been
performed in the manner prescribed by the laws of the State of Montana, the
resolutions and ordinances of the City of Three Forks, State of Montana,
relating to the issuance thereof.
   City of Three Forks, Montana,
   By

   City Clerk

Montana, this           day of                 20**

   Three Forks, Montana,

   On                20** the City Clerk of the City of Three Forks, Montana,
will at his office in Three Forks, Montana, pay to the bearer, the sum of $
             Dollars, being the interest due on said date of payment on its
Special Improvement or Sewer District Warrant No.       issued on account of
Special Improvement or Sewer District No.      .
 
         Mayor                          
         Clerk                           
 
   (1977 Code § 3.12.010; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Warrants Signed By Mayor: All special improvement or sewer district
warrants shall be signed by the designated officer and the Seal of the City
shall be affixed to each warrant. All interest coupons shall be signed by the
Mayor and City Clerk, or shall bear the printed facsimile signature of the
Mayor and City Clerk thereon. (1977 Code § 3.12.020)
   C.   Warrants In Denomination: Special improvement or sewer district
warrants may be in the denomination of one hundred dollars ($100.00), or
multiple or fractional parts thereof, as the purposes for which said warrants
are issued may require. (1977 Code § 3.12.030)
   D.   Numbering Warrants And Interest Coupons: All special improvement or
sewer district warrants, together with the interest coupons attached, for the
respective districts against which the same are issued, shall be numbered
consecutively beginning with No. 1 for each district and designated on the face
of the warrant the respective district to which such warrants are applicable,
and all warrants in call for payment shall be redeemed in the order of their
registration. (1977 Code § 3.12.040)
CHAPTER 2
REVENUE AND EXPENDITURE FUNDS
SECTION:
3-2-1: General Fund Created
3-2-2: Taxes Collected
3-2-3: Expenses Paid From Various Funds
3-2-1: GENERAL FUND CREATED:
There is hereby created a general fund, in and for the city, for the budgeting
and expenditures of monies for the city. (1977 Code § 3.30.010; amd. 2000 Code)
3-2-2: TAXES COLLECTED:
All taxes collected for city and administrative purposes shall be paid into the
general fund. All monies received from the collection of licenses required by
title 4, chapter 1 of this code, and any amendment thereto, or any ordinance
hereafter enacted by the city council requiring a license to be paid by any
business, occupation and profession or any amendment thereto, and all monies
received from fines imposed for a violation of any ordinance of the city not
otherwise provided for, shall be paid into the general fund. (1977 Code §
3.30.020; amd. 2000 Code)
3-2-3: EXPENSES PAID FROM VARIOUS FUNDS:
   A.   General Fund: All monies in the general fund shall be paid out to
defray expenses incurred for general city or administrative purposes.
   B.   Street And Alley Fund: All monies in the street and alley fund shall be
paid out to defray expenses incurred in maintaining, improving and repairing
the streets and alleys in the city, except where the same may be provided for
by reason of the creation of special improvement districts. (1977 Code §
3.30.030; amd. 2000 Code)
   C.   Three Forks Police Department Fund: All monies in the Three Forks
police department fund shall be paid out to defray the expenses incurred in the
enforcement of the ordinances of the city and the exercise of police powers.
(1977 Code § 3.30.030; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
CHAPTER 3
WATER FUNDS
SECTION:
3-3-1: Water Interest Fund
3-3-2: Water Fund
3-3-3: Water Sinking And Interest Fund
3-3-1: WATER INTEREST FUND:
   A.   Fund Created: There be hereby created a fund to be known as the Water
Interest Fund. (1977 Code § 3.34.010; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Revenues Paid Into Fund: There shall be paid into said Fund during each
year a sufficient amount of the revenues derived from the City water to pay the
interest as it becomes due on the outstanding water bonds. (1977 Code §
3.34.020; amd. 2000 Code)
3-3-2: WATER FUND:
   A.   Fund Created: There be hereby created a fund to be known as the Water
Fund. (1977 Code § 3.34.030; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Excess Monies Transferred: From and after the passage and approval of
this Chapter, annually, at the close of the City's fiscal year, all monies
remaining in the Water Fund, after the payment of maintenance and operating
expenses, and after deducting the interest on all City water bonds not
including improvement district bonds, which shall become due on or before July
1 following, shall be transferred to the Water Sinking and Interest Fund. (1977
Code § 3.34.040; amd. 2000 Code)
3-3-3: WATER SINKING AND INTEREST FUND:
   A.   Fund Created: There be hereby created a fund to be known as the Water
Sinking and Interest Fund. (1977 Code § 3.34.050; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Revenues In Excess: There shall be paid into said Fund all revenues
derived from the City water in excess of the amount necessary to pay operating
and maintenance expenses and interest as it becomes due on the outstanding
Water Sinking and Interest Fund for the purpose of paying the water bonds as
they mature. (1977 Code § 3.34.060; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 4
SEWER MAINTENANCE FUND
SECTION:
3-4-1: Fund Created
3-4-2: Collections Paid Into Fund
3-4-3: Disposition Of Monies
3-4-1: FUND CREATED:
The City Council hereby creates a fund to be known as the Sewer Maintenance
Fund. (1977 Code § 3.36.010)
3-4-2: COLLECTIONS PAID INTO FUND:
There shall be paid into said Fund all monies collected by the City Clerk/
Treasurer under Title 9, Chapter 5 of this Code, relating to the regulation of
sewer connections. (1977 Code § 3.36.020; amd. 2000 Code)
3-4-3: DISPOSITION OF MONIES:
All monies in the Sewer Maintenance Fund shall be used to defray the expenses
of inspection of connections, pumping, cleaning, and other expenses necessary
to the maintenance of the City sewer system. (1977 Code § 3.36.030)
CHAPTER 5
SPECIAL IMPROVEMENT DISTRICT REVOLVING FUND
SECTION:
3-5-1: Fund Created
3-5-2: Warrant Issuance; Insurance
3-5-1: FUND CREATED:
   A.   Statute Authority: There is hereby created and established in the City
a Special Improvement District Revolving Fund as authorized by section 7-12-
4221, Montana Code Annotated, to be maintained for any special improvement
district or districts heretofore or hereafter created for any purpose in order
to secure prompt payment of any special improvement district bonds or warrants,
heretofore or hereafter issued to defray the cost of improvements made therein,
and the interest thereon as it becomes due.
   B.   Transfer Monies: For the purpose of providing funds for such Revolving
Fund, the City Council may in its discretion transfer to the Revolving Fund
from the General Fund of the City such amounts as may be deemed necessary,
which amounts so transferred shall be deemed and considered, and shall be loans
from such General Fund to the Revolving Fund; and shall, in addition to such
transfers from the General Fund, or in lieu thereof, levy and collect for such
Revolving Fund such a tax, hereby declared to be for a public purpose on all
the taxable property in the City as shall be necessary to meet the financial
requirements of such Fund. Such levy, together with such transfer, shall not
exceed in any one year five percent (5%) of the principal amount of the then
outstanding special improvement district bonds and warrants.
   C.   Revolving Fund Loans To District Fund: Whenever any special improvement
district bond or warrant, or any interest thereon, shall hereafter become due
and payable, and there shall then be either no money or insufficient money in
the appropriate district fund with which to pay the same, an amount sufficient
to make up the deficiency may, by order of the City Council, be loaned by the
revolving fund to such District Fund, and thereupon such bond or warrant or
such interest thereon shall be paid from the money so loaned or from the money
so loaned when added to such insufficient amount, as the case may require.
(1977 Code § 3.52.010; amd. 2000 Code)
3-5-2: WARRANT ISSUANCE; INSURANCE:
In connection with the issuance of the special improvement district warrants to
be issued to defray the cost of the improvements in the special improvement
district hereinbefore specifically referred to, the Council hereby undertakes
and agrees to issue orders annually authorizing loans or advances from the
Revolving Fund to the District Fund of said district in amounts sufficient to
make good any deficiency in the principal and interest accounts thereof to the
extent that funds are available, and hereby further undertakes and agrees to
provide funds for such Revolving Fund pursuant to the provisions of sections 7-
12-4222 and 7-12-4223, Montana Code Annotated, by annually making such tax levy
(or, in lieu thereof, such loan from the General Fund) as the City Council
shall determine to be required to provide funds sufficient for the purposes
herein expressed, subject to the maximum limitations imposed by said section 7-
12-4222, Montana Code Annotated. The undertakings and agreements provided for
herein are made pursuant to the provisions of sections 7-12-4223 and 7-12-4224,
Montana Code Annotated. (1977 Code § 3.52.020; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 6
IMPACT FEES FOR PUBLIC FACILITIES
SECTION:
3-6-1: Purpose
3-6-2: Definitions
3-6-3: Applicability
3-6-4: Collection
3-6-5: Limits On Expenditure
3-6-6: Adoption/Revision
3-6-7: Impact Fee Advisory Committee (IFAC)
3-6-8: Accounting
3-6-9: Credits
3-6-10: Unused Impact Fees
3-6-11: Appeals
3-6-12: Savings Clause
3-6-1: PURPOSE:
As authorized by §7-6-1601, et seq, MCA, this chapter provides for the adoption
and administration of impact fees that will help the city pay for the new and
improved public facilities needed to support its growth. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-
2025)
3-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
              A self-contained living unit on the same parcel as a single-family dwelling of
ACCESSORY     greater square footage that includes its own cooking, sleeping, and sanitation
DWELLING      facilities and complies with or is otherwise exempt from any applicable building
UNIT:         code, fire code, and public health and safety regulations adopted pursuant to
              title 50, chapter 2, MCA. For further definition, please see 76-2-345, MCA.
              A geographically bounded portion of the City of Three Forks in which development
BENEFIT AREA: is served by a particular improvement or set of improvements listed in the CIP
              that does not serve other parts of the city. Impact fees will be different in
              different benefit areas.
              Usually shortened to 'improvement' in this chapter, means improvements, land,
CAPITAL       and equipment with a useful life of ten (10) years or more that increase or
IMPROVEMENT:  improve the service capacity of a public facility. The term does not include
              consumable supplies.
CAPITAL       A public document adopted by the city council that evaluates the capacity of the
IMPROVEMENTS  city's public facilities and quantifies the present and anticipated demand for
PLAN (CIP):   those facilities. The CIP compares capacity and demand to identify the need for
              additional or improved facilities and estimates their cost.
              The purposes of section 3-6-3(D) of the Three Forks city code occurs when an
              additional dwelling unit is added to an existing building, or when an existing
              residential building is converted to commercial use, or an existing commercial
              building is converted to residential, or when an existing building, structure,
CHANGE OF     or use is changed to a more intense commercial or residential use. For this
USE:          definition, intensity will be measured by:
              A.   A change in water meter size, if a larger water meter will be installed, it
              is a change in use, or
              B.   Parking. If additional parking spaces must be provided to comply with title
              11, chapter 24 of this code it is a change in use.
COMMERCIAL:   All nonresidential uses.
              Development of land, divisions that create new lots or rights- of-way; grading,
              including clearing, excavation, and fill; the construction, reconstruction,
DEVELOPMENT:  enlargement or relocation of any building or structure; and/or any change in the
              use of a site, building, or structure. Please see title 11, chapter 4 for more
              detail.
              For the purposes of section 3-6-4(D), a building or structure when its area
ENLARGED:     increases by more than fifty percent (50%) or one thousand (1,000) SF, whichever
              is less.
              Consistent with 7-6-1601(5), MCA, a one (1) time charge that helps cover the
IMPACT FEE:   cost of capital improvements needed to serve the development from which the fee
              is collected.
IMPACT FEE    Required by 7-6-1604, MCA. Its purpose is to provide citizen review of the CIP
ADVISORY      and the preparation of service area reports. Based on its reviews, the IFAC
COMMITTEE     makes recommendations to the council.
(IFAC):
              Listed by 7-6-1601(7), MCA, including a water supply production, treatment,
              storage, or distribution facility; a wastewater collection, treatment, or
              disposal facility; a transportation facility, including roads, streets, bridges,
              rights-of-way, traffic signals, and landscaping; a storm water collection,
PUBLIC        retention, detention, treatment, or disposal facility or a flood control
FACILITIES:   facility; a police, emergency medical rescue, or fire protection facility; and
              other facilities for which documentation is prepared as provided in 7-6-1602,
              MCA, that have been approved as part of an impact fee ordinance or resolution by
              a two-thirds (2/3) majority of the governing body of an incorporated city, town,
              or consolidated local government.
SERVICE AREA  Required by 7-6-1602, MCA, which specifies the contents. Service area reports
REPORTS:      are public documents that build on the capital improvements plan to calculate
              trial impact fees for review by the IFAC and action by the council.
STANDARDS FOR Referred to in section 3-6-9(D), is the current version of a detailed set of
DESIGN AND    engineering standards adopted by the city.
CONSTRUCTION:
THIS CODE:    The Three Forks city code.
 
Additional definitions set forth in 7-6-1601, MCA, are included herein as if
fully set forth. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-3: APPLICABILITY:
   A.   Any new or enlargement of principal building, structure, or use, or any
new dwelling unit that is added to an existing building or structure, change in
use for which a zoning permit is required by title 11 of this code must pay the
applicable impact fees adopted in the impact fee resolution that is authorized
by section 3-6-6.
   B.   Accessory buildings, structures, or uses for which a zoning permit is
required by title 11, chapter 4 of this code and that will be connected to city
utilities must pay the applicable impact fees adopted in the impact fee
resolution that is authorized by section 3-6-6.
   C.   Temporary buildings, structures, and uses do not pay impact fees.
   D.   The determination of impact fees for commercial development of up to
four thousand (4,000) square feet (SF) in building area will be made using the
per SF fees calculated in the service area reports. The impact fees for larger
commercial buildings or structures will be determined as provided in E-G,
below.
   E.   The per square foot water and wastewater impact fees for larger
commercial buildings and structures shall be calculated by increasing the per
square foot water and wastewater impact fees in direct proportion to the flow
rate of the meter or meters serving the proposed building or structure. These
higher fees will be applied to the first four thousand (4,000) SF of the
commercial building or structure.
   F.   The impact fee for transportation for larger commercial buildings and
structures shall be the same as adopted in the service area report for the
first four thousand (4,000) SF of building area plus an additional fee for each
additional on-site parking space after the first sixteen (16). That fee will be
specified in the resolution adopting the impact fees.
   G.   The per square foot impact fees for fire protection and municipal
buildings for commercial development shall be as calculated in the service area
reports for the entire area of the building or structure.
   H.   Any applicant for annexation, zoning site plan or subdivision may
present a professionally prepared impact fee study that is consistent with §7-
6-1601, et seq, MCA, and this chapter, as an alternative to the calculations of
D-G, above. That alternative may be accepted by the city council upon a finding
that it more accurately reflects the demands the proposed development will
place on public facilities. Such alternative studies must be reviewed by the
IFAC prior to their consideration by the city council. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-
2025)
3-6-4: COLLECTION:
Impact fees will be collected or credited as provided by section 3-6-9 before
the approval of a zoning permit, site plan or conditional use permit to develop
is finalized. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-5: LIMITS ON EXPENDITURE:
Impact fees may be applied only to the design and construction of capital
improvements listed in the capital improvements plan and the service area
reports. No other use of these fees is permitted. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-6: ADOPTION/REVISION:
   A.   Impact fees may be adopted or revised by a resolution by the council
following a recommendation from the IFAC and a public hearing for which notice
is provided as required by state law.
   B.   Revisions to the resolution adopting or revising impact fees may be
made as often as needed to reflect changes in the CIP, including the completion
of improvements, and the recommendations of the IFAC. IFAC recommendations must
include an updated service area report. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-7: IMPACT FEE ADVISORY COMMITTEE (IFAC):
Pursuant to §7-6-1604, MCA, an IFAC shall be established by the council. The
IFAC's purpose shall be to provide annual citizen review of the CIP, the
service area reports, the impact fees and their administration, then based on
its reviews, make recommendations to the council. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-8: ACCOUNTING:
The city treasurer shall create a separate, interest-bearing fund for each
adopted impact fee, including separate funds for each benefit area. As provided
by section 3-6-5 of this code, these funds may be used only for the design and
construction of capital improvements that are listed in the capital
improvements plan and the applicable service area report. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-
2025)
3-6-9: CREDITS:
   A.   The council may agree to have an applicant construct or install
facilities that the city would, otherwise, build or install using, at least in
part, impact fees.
   B.   Such an agreement will ordinarily be part of the improvements agreement
required for annexation or subdivision in title 11 of this code, but this
chapter does not prohibit a separate contract.
   C.   Where such an agreement is approved by the council, the applicant's
actual costs will be credited against the impact fees that would be owed as
applications for zoning permits are approved. If the actual costs of
construction or installation are expected to exceed the anticipated impact
fees, the agreement required by subsection A., above, will require that the
city pay the difference from specifically identified funds.
   D.   All work performed by an applicant pursuant to this section shall be in
full compliance with the regulations of title 11 of this code, including any
applicable conditions of approval and the improvements agreement as applicable,
and with the city's standards for design and construction, particularly
including the requirements of those standards for inspection, acceptance, and
warranty of the improvements made by the applicant. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-10: UNUSED IMPACT FEES:
   A.   Impact fees that are not collected or used as provided for in the CIP
and service area report shall be returned to the person who owned the property
at the time the fees were collected.
   B.   Impact fees will be retained for the life cycle of the improvement for
which they were assessed before a refund is made. For water and wastewater
impact fees, this will be forty (40) years. For all other improvements, the
cycle shall be calculated based upon current data. (Ord. 406-2025, 8-12-2025)
3-6-11: APPEALS:
   A.   As required by §7-6-1603(8), MCA, anyone who has paid an impact fee who
believes that charge was in error may file an appeal that will be heard before
the council.
   B.   The city council shall establish the appeal fee by resolution. An
applicant who chooses to appeal the assessment or calculation of impact fees,
determination of exemptions, credits, or other decision of city staff, shall
submit an appeal, and payment of a nonrefundable application fee, within thirty
(30) days following the date of decision or determination by city staff. The
application of appeal may stay the collection of the impact fee.
   C.   Appeals will be considered by the city council. The city council shall
consider the appeal in accordance with the rules and regulations of that
governing body. The decision of the city council shall, in all instances, be
the final administrative decision and shall be subject to judicial review in
accordance with applicable law.
