other similar watercraft or snow machines on any of the Three Forks ponds when
powered by any internal combustion engine, fuel powered engine or any other
engine. Battery operated motors propelling watercraft are permitted on the
middle and east ponds. (Ord. 265-2001, 8-13-2001)
5-8-2: OVERNIGHT CAMPING PROHIBITED:
In the developed parking areas and undeveloped areas upon which any vehicle,
trailer, camper or recreational vehicle may be stopped, camping or overnight
parking between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. to five o'clock (5:00)
A.M. is prohibited. (Ord. 367-2016, 10-11-2016)
5-8-3: PENALTY:
Upon a first conviction, the fine shall be no less than one hundred dollars
($100.00) and no more than five hundred dollars ($500.00). Upon each subsequent
conviction within a period of two (2) years, the fine shall be increased one
hundred dollars ($100.00) for each conviction. In addition, upon conviction the
owner or operator so cited shall pay all court costs and other costs associated
with processing the complaint. (Ord. 265-2001, 8-13-2001; amd. Ord. 367-2016,
10-11-2016)
TITLE 6
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE OFFICERS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Arrest For Violations
6-1-2: Examination Of Public Places
6-1-3: Examine Entrances And Exits Of Public Buildings
6-1-1: ARREST FOR VIOLATIONS:
It shall be the duty of police officers to make complaint before the city judge
against all persons known to him to be guilty of a violation of the criminal
laws of the state or ordinances of the city; to arrest and take into custody,
with or without warrant or process, any person who shall be found in any street
or alley or in any other public place, in a state of gross intoxication, or
doing any act in violation of the laws of the state or ordinances of the city;
and to bring such person before the city judge, or place him or her in the
county jail, to be dealt with according to law; to execute all orders or
processes issued to him by the mayor, city court or city council, or other
officer having power to issue the same and make due return thereof. (1977 Code
§ 2.28.010; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
6-1-2: EXAMINATION OF PUBLIC PLACES:
It shall be the duty of police officers in and for the city at all times, when
on duty, to enter all public places of business when open to the general public
and make a thorough and complete search and examination thereof for the purpose
of determining whether there is any violation of the ordinance prohibiting
nuisances, of the ordinance regulating the storage of explosives, kerosene,
coal oil, petroleum and dynamite and all other ordinances providing for the
protection and preservation of the public health, public morals and guarding
the public safety. (1977 Code § 2.28.020; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-
10-2009)
6-1-3: EXAMINE ENTRANCES AND EXITS OF PUBLIC BUILDINGS:
It shall be the duty of police officers at all times, when on duty, to make a
careful examination of the front and rear entrances to all public places of
businesses after the closing hour of business for the day and when closed at
any other time to the general public, and determine from said examination
whether said entrances are securely locked, bolted and fastened, and to examine
all windows in said public places of businesses that can be reached from the
street by extending hand. (1977 Code § 2.28.030; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-
10, 11-10-2009)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
6-2-1: Disturbing Peace And Quiet
6-2-2: Permitting Any Disturbances
6-2-3: Public Safety; Bonfires, Fireworks, Guns
6-2-4: Bows And Arrows; Other Projectiles
6-2-5: Abandoned Refrigerators, Iceboxes
6-2-6: Penalty
6-2-7: Urination Or Defecation In Public Prohibited
6-2-1: DISTURBING PEACE AND QUIET:
No person within the city, or within three (3) miles of the city limits shall
knowingly disturb the peace and quiet of any streets, neighborhood, family or
person, by loud, tumultuous noise, or by tumultuous or offensive conduct, or by
using offensively loud radio or television sets, or by threatening, quarreling,
scolding, hallooing, hollering, challenging to fight or fighting, or by
cursing, swearing, uttering obscene, profane vulgar or indecent language in the
presence of any person, or by committing any obscene, vulgar, indecent or lewd
act in any public place, or in view of any person. (1977 Code § 9.16.010; amd.
2000 Code)
6-2-2: PERMITTING ANY DISTURBANCES:
Any person knowingly permitting any disturbance described in the foregoing
section, upon premises owned or occupied by him or her, shall be deemed guilty
of a misdemeanor. (1977 Code § 9.16.020; amd. 2000 Code)
6-2-3: PUBLIC SAFETY; BONFIRES, FIREWORKS, GUNS:
   A.   Bonfires 1 ; Fireworks Permit: It shall be unlawful within the
corporate limits of the city for any person to build bonfires in any public
street, square, or on any vacant lot, or explode, set off or fire, within said
limits, any firecrackers, rockets, torpedoes, toy pistols, or any fireworks and
explosives whatever, without special permit therefor from the mayor. The mayor
permits legal (state and federal) fireworks on a yearly basis. (1977 Code §
9.12.010)
   B.   Guns Fired Within Corporate Limits:
      1.   Prohibition: No person shall hereafter wilfully shoot or fire off a
gun, pistol or any firearm within the corporate limits of the city, except as
provided in subsection B2 of this section. (1977 Code § 9.12.020)
      2.   Exception: Nothing in this subsection shall be construed to embrace
the firing of a gun, pistol or other firearm when done in the lawful defense of
the person, property or family, or in the necessary enforcement of the law.
(1977 Code § 9.12.030)
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 5, chapter 3 of this code.
6-2-4: BOWS AND ARROWS; OTHER PROJECTILES:
No person shall hereafter wilfully shoot any arrow or other dangerous
projectile through the use of any weapon unless such arrow or other projectile
is shot at a target with a backstop of sufficient density to stop the arrow or
projectile. The minimum dimensions of the backstop shall be four feet (4') in
width and four feet (4') in length. (Ord. 205, 6-11-1985; amd. 2000 Code)
6-2-5: ABANDONED REFRIGERATORS, ICEBOXES:
   A.   Leaving Appliances Outside: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm
or corporation to leave outside of any building or dwelling in a place
accessible to children any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox,
refrigerator or any other container of any kind which has an airtight door or
lock which may not be released for opening from the inside of said icebox,
refrigerator or container. (1977 Code § 7.12.010)
   B.   Removing Snap Locks Or Doors: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm
or corporation to leave outside of any building or dwelling in a place
accessible to children any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox,
refrigerator or any other container of any kind which has an airtight snap lock
or other device thereon without first removing the said snap lock or other
doors from said icebox, refrigerator or container. (1977 Code § 7.12.020)
6-2-6: PENALTY:
Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (2000 Code)
6-2-7: URINATION OR DEFECATION IN PUBLIC PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to urinate or defecate on public property
or public right of way, or on private property open to public view, except in
restrooms and facilities provided for such purpose. The penalty for any person
violating these provisions is described in section
6-2-6 of this chapter. (Ord. 273, 6-8-2003)
CHAPTER 3
CURFEW FOR MINORS
SECTION:
6-3-1: Short Title
6-3-2: Purpose
6-3-3: Scope
6-3-4: Definitions
6-3-5: Curfew For Minors
6-3-6: Exceptions
6-3-7: Curfew Hours
6-3-8: Parental Responsibility
6-3-9: Law Enforcement Officers, Duty
6-3-10: Penalties
6-3-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known and may be cited as the CURFEW ORDINANCE. (Ord.
234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-2: PURPOSE:
   A.   Establish Restrictions: The purpose of this chapter is to establish
reasonable restrictions upon the time of day during which minors shall be
allowed on any of the streets or other public places of the city. Such
restrictions are enacted to further the general welfare of the community and
specifically to further the following community interests:
      1.   The protection of the younger children in the city from each other
and from other persons on the street during the nighttime hours;
      2.   The enforcement of parental control of and responsibility for their
children;
      3.   The protection of the public from nocturnal mischief by minors;
      4.   The reduction in the incidence of juvenile criminal activity; and
      5.   Prevent exposure to and the possibility of being led into
involvement with crimes of violence, destruction and/or self- destruction.
   B.   General Police Powers: These restrictions are enacted pursuant to the
general police and other powers granted to self-government power local
governments. (Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-3: SCOPE:
The provisions of this chapter are intended to apply to all minors under the
age of eighteen (18) years and to any parent of any minor person under the age
of eighteen (18) years. (Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-4: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following definitions shall apply:
   CITY: The local government of the city of Three Forks, Montana, and all of
the area located within its geographical boundaries, and also the pond area and
publicly owned property outside the city limits.
   CURFEW: A regulation establishing restrictions upon the time of day during
which minor persons may appear on any of the streets or public places of the
city of Three Forks, Montana.
   LAW ENFORCEMENT FACILITY: The offices of the city of Three Forks police
department at 206 Main Street, Three Forks, Montana.
   MASCULINE GENDER: Shall include the feminine gender.
   MINOR: Any person who has not attained the age of eighteen (18) years.
   PARENT: Any person having legal custody of a minor: a) as a natural or
adoptive parent; b) as a legal guardian; or c) as a person to whom legal
custody has been given by order of court.
   PERSON: Any human being, male or female.
   PUBLIC PLACE: Any park, playground, schoolyard, pond area, or other publicly
owned property within or outside the city limits.
   SINGULAR NUMBER: Shall include the plural number.
   STREET: Any public street, highway, sidewalk, alley, or other public way
within the city of Three Forks, Montana. (Ord. 234, 10-10-1995; amd. 2000 Code;
Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
6-3-5: CURFEW FOR MINORS:
A curfew restricting the time of day during which minor persons may appear on
any of the streets or in any of the public places of the city is hereby
established. No minor, as specified in section
6-3-7 of this chapter, shall be in or upon any street or public place within
the city during the hours provided in section
6-3-7 of this chapter. (Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-6: EXCEPTIONS:
In the following exceptional cases, a minor in or upon any street or public
place within the city during the hours provided in section
 6-3-7 of this chapter shall not be considered in violation of this chapter
when:
   A.   Accompanied by a parent of such minor.
   B.   Accompanied by a person over eighteen (18) years of age who is
authorized by a parent of such minor to take said parent's place in
accompanying said minor for a designated period of time and purpose within a
specified area.
   C.   In the performance of an errand or duty directed by a parent of such
minor.
   D.   Attending a school or religious activity. This exception will apply for
one-half (1/2) hour after the completion of such activity.
   E.   Engaged in legally recognized employment. This exception will apply for
the period from one-half (1/2) hour before to one-half (1/2) hour after work.
(Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-7: CURFEW HOURS:
Minors who have not reached their eighteenth birthday shall not be in or upon
any street or public place between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and
five o'clock (5:00) A.M. except on Friday or Saturday nights when such hours
shall be between twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M.;
provided, however, that on any weekday night preceding a holiday recognized by
the United States Of America, state of Montana, or the city, the hours shall be
between twelve o'clock (12:00) midnight and five o'clock (5:00) A.M. In
addition, during the period of time that the state is operating under daylight
saving time, the aforementioned hours shall be extended by one-half (1/2) hour.
(Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-8: PARENTAL RESPONSIBILITY:
   A.   It is a violation of this chapter for any parent, guardian or other
person having the care, custody or control of a minor under the age of eighteen
(18) years to allow such minor, either expressly or by neglect to duly exercise
such care, custody or control, to wander, play, loiter on the public streets,
highways, parks and playgrounds after the hour prescribed in section
6-3-7 of this chapter.
   B.   The burden for proving the exception noted in this chapter is on the
defendant.
   C.   In any prosecution under this section, it shall not constitute a
defense that the parent, guardian or other adult person having the care,
custody or control of such minor does not have knowledge that such minor did
wander, stroll or play in the public places during the hours of the curfew.
(Ord. 323-11, 6-14-2011)
6-3-9: LAW ENFORCEMENT OFFICERS, DUTY:
   A.   Ascertain Name Of Minor Violator And Parent: Upon finding a minor in or
upon any street or public place within the city in violation of any of the
provisions of this chapter, it shall be the duty of the attending law
enforcement officer of the city to take the name of such minor and the name and
address of the minor's "parent" as defined in section
 6-3-4 of this chapter.
   B.   Notify Parent Or Guardian: The law enforcement officer shall
immediately notify the parent or guardian of the minor in violation of the
curfew, and the parent or guardian shall immediately appear to take charge of
such minor.
   C.   Entrust Minor To Parent Or Guardian: When a minor is apprehended for
violation of the provisions of this chapter, the law enforcement officer shall
turn the minor over to the minor's parent or parents. If a parent cannot be
located, or fails to take charge of the minor, said minor may be entrusted to a
relative, neighbor, or other person who will, on behalf of the parent, assume
responsibility of caring for the minor pending the availability or the arrival
of the parent. (Ord. 234, 10-10-1995)
6-3-10: PENALTIES:
   A.   Fines Imposed: Upon the first incident or violation of this chapter, a
written notice or warning shall be given to a parent or guardian of the minor
who is in violation of this chapter. Subsequent violation and conviction under
this chapter shall result in a fine of one hundred dollars ($100.00) for a
second offense, two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for a third offense and
five hundred dollars ($500.00) for a fourth offense. Subsequent offenses shall
have a five hundred dollar ($500.00) fine imposed each time and the court may
consider heavier financial or other penalties. (Ord. 316-09-10, 11-10-2009)
   B.   Youth Court: "Minors", as defined in section
 6-3-4 of this chapter, may be cited into youth court upon violation of this
chapter at the discretion of the law enforcement officer. (Ord. 234, 10-10-
1995)
CHAPTER 4
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A. DOGS
SECTION:
6-4A-1: Definitions
6-4A-2: Dog Licensing Requirements
6-4A-3: Additional Dog(s) Permit
6-4A-4: Tag And Collar
6-4A-5: Running At Large Prohibited
6-4A-6: Impoundment
6-4A-7: Nuisance Dogs
6-4A-8: Suspected Rabies
6-4A-9: Dangerous Dogs
6-4A-10: Penalty
6-4A-1: DEFINITIONS:
   ADDITIONAL DOG(S) PERMIT: A permit obtained by an occupant of a residential
dwelling, after approval by the City Council, for when one harbors more than
three (3), but not more than four (4) dogs.
   CURRENT VACCINATION CERTIFICATE: A vaccination certificate against rabies
which shall be dated within three (3) years from the date that the application
for a dog license is made.
   DANGEROUS DOG: Any dog which bites or attempts to bite any human being
without provocation, or which harasses, chases, bites, or attempts to bite any
other animal.
   DOG: Includes male and female.
   DOGGY DAY CARE: A business which keeps/cares for animals for pet owners
throughout the day, but not overnight which is not allowed in the city limits.
   HARBOR: A person who habitually lets or permits a dog to remain or be in or
about his or her house or premises.
   KENNEL: A commercial business in which one keeps animals for pet owners
which includes overnight stays, typically with an exterior fenced property (to
prevent dogs getting loose off the property), and interior fenced individual
dog runs which may be indoor and/or outdoor, and a larger exercise area. This
includes "doggy day cares" which do not house animals overnight which is not
allowed in the city limits.
   OWNER: Any person or persons, firm, association, or corporation owning,
keeping, or harboring a dog.
   POUND: The place provided by the city and maintained by the Three Forks
police department for the impounding of dogs.
   RUNNING AT LARGE: A dog which is off the owned or leased premises of the dog
owner, unless he shall be under leash and under the control of a competent
person.
   VACCINATE: The inoculation of a dog with an antirabies vaccine under the
administration of the county health officer or by any licensed veterinarian,
the cost of said vaccination to be borne by the owner of the dog.
(1977 Code § 8.04.010; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009; Ord. 320-10,
10-12-2010; Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-2: DOG LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required; Fee; Time For Registration: Every dog over five (5)
months of age in the city limits is required to have a license. The annual
license fee shall be set via resolution adopted by the city council. The fee
shall be for each dog and each dog shall be registered for the calendar year on
or before April 15 of each year at the office of the city clerk.
   B.   Application For License: The owner shall state at the time application
is made for such license, his/her name, address, phone number, the dog's name,
breed, color, sex, altered status (spay/neuter), and current rabies vaccination
certificate or like proof, and no license shall be is-sued by the clerk without
such current rabies vaccination certificate.
   C.   Term Of Registration: Any dog brought into the city after April 15 and
prior to the following April 15, or any dog attaining the age of five (5)
months after such date and prior to such date in the succeeding year shall pay
the fee and register the dog as provided herein. Such registrations shall
expire on December 31 annually.
   D.   Exceptions: The provisions of this section shall not apply to dogs
whose owners are nonresidents, temporarily within the city, nor to dogs brought
into the city for the purpose of participating in any dog show, nor to "seeing
eye" dogs or "hearing impaired" guide dogs, properly trained to assist a blind
person or hearing impaired person, when such dogs are actually being used by a
blind person or a hearing impaired person for the purpose of aiding them in
going from place to place.
(1977 Code § 8.04.020; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 359-15, 7-28-2015; Ord. 402-2024,
1-9-2024)
6-4A-3: ADDITIONAL DOG(S) PERMIT:
   A.   Limit On Number Of Dogs; Application And Hearing:
      1.   It is unlawful for any person, family or group of persons in the
same dwelling to keep, harbor, or maintain any number more than three (3) dogs
over five (5) months of age in or upon any property. (Ord. 244, 1997; amd. 2000
Code). It is unlawful for any person, family or group of persons in the same
dwelling to keep, harbor, or maintain more than four (4) dogs of any age with
or without an issued permit in or upon any property.
      2.   Any person, family or group of person in the same dwelling in or
upon any property may apply for a permit authorizing the keeping of four (4)
dogs. The application form shall be provided by the City and must be
accompanied by the applicable fee to be set via resolution adopted by the city
council. Submittal of a complete, signed application is an agreement between
the applicant and the city to perform an inspection prior to any decision. If
the applicant is not the property owner, the application shall include the
property owner's signature.
         a.   Said application fee will be used to cover the cost of staff to
create and mail notice to the property owners within three hundred feet (300' -
the equivalent of one city block), excluding streets and alleys, in any
direction from the applicant's property, of the hearing scheduled before the
city council to decide on the Additional Dog Permit application. This fee is
nonrefundable.
      3.   This section shall not apply to licensed veterinarian hospitals. It
is intended to apply to keeping or maintaining a commercial dog kennel or doggy
day cares, and breeding dogs, which are hereby declared to be nuisances, unless
an additional dog permit is granted by the city council after application and
hearing.
      4.   Upon receipt of a complete application, the clerk shall schedule the
decision at a public meeting before the city council. Such hearing shall be
held after investigation of the premises by a city employee or law enforcement,
who shall inspect the space the animals will be housed. Such inspection report
shall include at a minimum the care/health of the animals, access to outdoor
space, whether or not the outside space is fenced, if there are any odors or
excess of animal waste, and any dog-related complaints associated with the
applicant. The employee/officer may make a recommendation of approval, approval
with conditions, or denial to the city council.
   B.   Permit Required; Fee: An additional dog permit shall be required where
the applicant owns, harbors, or keeps more than three (3) dogs, which
application shall be authorized or denied based upon the information in the
application, provided during the application process and including, but not
limited to public comment presented to the city council. The license fee shall
be set via resolution adopted by the city council and is good for the calendar
year, or any part thereof, expiring on December 31, unless sooner revoked. A
permit holder must adhere to any conditions imposed by the city council, and
agrees to inspections by law enforcement upon any complaint(s) received, or
upon renewal.
   C.   Annual Renewal: Upon approval of an additional dog permit, said permit
must be renewed each calendar year no later than April 15. Such renewal shall
include a fee set via resolution adopted by the city council.
   D.   Revocation Of License: Upon complaint being made and substantiated that
an additional dog permit is being operated in an improper manner or violates
any of the conditions imposed, the city council may revoke the permit after a
proper hearing and notice to the permittee. In the event the permit is revoked,
the dog owner shall then have no more than thirty (30) days to remove the
animals in excess of the number allowed by law.
   E.   Violation, Fines: It is unlawful to have more than three (3) dogs
harbored or maintained on a premises without a current permit. If, after ninety
(90) days of notice of violation of this subsection, more than three (3) dogs
remain on the premises, the fine doubles for each dog over the allowance.
(Ord. 244, 1997; amd. Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-4: TAG AND COLLAR:
   A.   Issuance Of Tag: Upon payment of the license fee, the city clerk shall
issue to the owner a license certificate and a metallic tag for each dog
licensed. The shape of the tag shall change every year and shall have stamped
thereon the year for which it was issued.
   B.   Collar Required: Every owner shall provide each dog with a collar to
which the license tag must be affixed, and see that the collar and tag are
constantly worn; provided, however, that it shall be lawful to remove such
collar and license tag when such dog is under the immediate control of its
owner or his/her agent.
   C.   Duplicate Tag; Fee: In case the tag is lost or destroyed, a duplicate
will be issued by the clerk upon payment as set via resolution by the city
council. Tags shall not be transferable from one dog to another.
(1977 Code § 8.04.030; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-5: RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED 1 :
   No owner of any dog shall permit such dog to run at large at any time.
(1977 Code § 8.04.040)
 
Notes
1 1. See also article C of this chapter.
6-4A-6: IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Authority to Impound: It shall be the duty of any city employee or law
enforcement to ap-prehend any dog running at large, or unlicensed, or without
collar and license tag, in violation of any one or more of sections
6-4A-1 through this section to impound such dog at the animal shelter for the
county, or other location designated by the city council.
   B.   Registry Required: Police officers, upon impounding any dog, shall make
or cause to be made a complete registry, entering the apparent breed, color,
sex and whether licensed. If licensed, he shall enter the name and address of
the owner and the number of the license tag.
   C.   Supervision Of City Employees: Any person employed by the city for the
purpose of enforcing sections
6-4A-2 through
6-4A-10 of this article shall be under the supervision and authority of police
officers.
   D.   Use Of Tranquilizer Gun Or Similar Device: No person, including police
officers, or members of the Three Forks police department shall, in the
enforcement of sections
6-4A-8 through
6-4A-10 of this article, use a "tranquilizer gun" or any similar mechanized
device which causes paralysis or unconsciousness in a dog, except if the dog is
a "dangerous dog" as defined in section
6-4A-1 of this article. However, nothing herein shall preclude the use of such
a tranquilizer gun or similar device in the hands of a licensed veterinarian or
a member of the Three Forks police department or other city employee who is
certified in writing by a licensed veterinarian as competent to use such a
tranquilizer gun or similar device.
(1977 Code § 8.04.050; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009; Ord. 320-10,
10-12-2010; Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-7: NUISANCE DOGS:
   No owner shall keep a dog, whether running at large or not, which shall
cause annoyance or disturbance by prolonged or repeating barking, howling, or
yelping, by chasing motor vehicles or human beings, or repeatedly damaging or
destroying the flowers, plants, lawn, shrubbery, or trees of a neighborhood or
of a citizen. Any owner keeping such a nuisance dog in violation of this
section shall be punished as set forth in section the PENALTY section of this
article.
(Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-8: SUSPECTED RABIES:
Any dog suspected of having rabies shall be seized by a police officer and
impounded for a period of ten (10) days. The county health officer shall be
notified at once of such impounding and the dog may be disposed of only under
his direction.
(1977 Code § 8.04.080; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009; Ord. 402-
2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-9: DANGEROUS DOGS:
   A.   Relinquish Dangerous Dog To Authorities: Whenever a written complaint
is made before a police officer or city judge, that a "dangerous dog", as
defined in section
6-4A-1 of this article, has bitten or attempted to bite any human being without
provocation, or which harasses, chases, bites, or attempts to bite any other
animal, the police officer shall issue an order allowing the police officer to
seize the dog which is the subject of the complaint for a period up to seventy
two (72) hours. The animal would be kept until the police officer has completed
the investigation of the charge or seventy two (72) hours whichever is less.
   B.   Failure To Relinquish Dangerous Dog: The owner or possessor who shall
refuse or neglect to turn over said dog to the police officer within twelve
(12) hours of receiving such order described in subsection A of this section
shall be in violation of this article and punished as hereinafter provided.
   C.   Dangerous Dog Retention: Upon the expiration of seventy two (72) hours
after relinquishment of the dog described in subsection A of this section, if
the investigation supports, in the opinion of the Three Forks police
department, the dog should be retained as evidence until the case is
adjudicated, the Three Forks police department may apply to the city court for
an order allowing the dog to remain in the custody of the Three Forks police
department pending file adjudication of the charge. Upon conviction, in
addition to any other penalty, the party so convicted shall be assessed all
costs and fees for the keeping of the dog.
(Ord. 320-10, 10-12-2010; amd. Ord. 331-12, 4-10-2012; Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
6-4A-10: PENALTY:
   A.   Dangerous Dogs: Any owner or possessor of a dangerous dog upon
violating the provisions of this article by owning or possessing a dangerous
dog shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof, shall be
fined no less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00) but not exceeding one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00) and/or six (6) months' imprisonment for a first
offense. Upon conviction of a second offense for the same dangerous dog, the
fine shall be no less than five hundred dollars ($500.00) or alternatively the
court may order the euthanization of the dangerous dog. Upon conviction of a
third or subsequent offense for the same dangerous dog, the fine shall be no
less than one thousand dollars ($1,000.00) or in the alternative the court may
order the euthanization of the dangerous dog.
   In addition to the fine, an owner or possessor who is found guilty of
violating this provision shall pay restitution to the city for all costs and
expenses of boarding the dangerous dog. If the dog is euthanized, the owner or
possessor who is found guilty of violating the provision shall pay as
restitution to the city all costs and expenses of euthanizing the dog.
   Any owner found violating the provision for failure to relinquish to a
police officer, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be fined no less than one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00), but not
exceeding five hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or six (6) months' imprisonment
for each offense.
   B.   Nuisance Dogs: Any owner found violating any provision of this article
shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be fined
not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) but not exceeding five hundred
dollars ($500.00) and/or six (6) months' imprisonment.
   C.   Licensing Penalties: Any owner found violating any provision of the
licensing provisions of this article shall, upon conviction, be guilty of a
misdemeanor and may be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code.
(Ord. 329-12, 2-14-2012; amd. Ord. 332-12, 4-10-2012; Ord. 363-2015, 1-12-2016;
Ord. 402-2024, 1-9-2024)
ARTICLE B. LIVESTOCK AND FOWL
SECTION:
6-4B-1: Hoofed Animals At Large
6-4B-2: Animals And Fowl At Large
6-4B-2-1: Chickens
6-4B-3: Prohibition Of Pastures
6-4B-4: Exceptions
6-4B-5: Fines Collected
6-4B-6: Penalty
6-4B-1: HOOFED ANIMALS AT LARGE:
The herding or running at large of hoofed animals upon the City streets,
avenues, alleys, parks, or public places or grounds within the City, excluding
the Buttelman land west of the Jefferson River while it is zoned agricultural,
is hereby prohibited and declared to be a nuisance. (Ord. 226, 1993)
6-4B-2: ANIMALS AND FOWL AT LARGE:
It is hereby made and declared unlawful and a nuisance for any hoofed animals
(i.e., hogs, horses, cattle, sheep, swine, and goats) and fowl (i.e., chickens,
turkeys, ducks, and geese) excepting those chickens allowed to be kept by City
ordinance and those animals in times of rodeos and parades, to be kept within
the corporate limits of the City for more than forty eight (48) hours, and such
animals or fowl so kept within the City longer than said allowed time are
hereby declared to be a nuisance and a violation of this article and the
continuance of the same shall be regarded as a separate offense to be punished
as such separate offense. Roosters are strictly prohibited within the City
limits and the presence of the same shall be hereby declared to be a nuisance
and a violation of this article and the continuance of the same shall be
regarded as a separate offense to be punished as such separate offense. (Ord.
354-15, 2-24-2015)
6-4B-2-1: CHICKENS:
   A.   Permits Required/Inspections/Renewal Fee: The maximum number of permits
issued shall be established by the City Council and adopted by resolution. Each
permit, if approved, will be issued on a first come, first served basis
providing all requirements of this section are met. The acceptance by an
application of a permit as described herein is a representation by the
applicant that so long as a permit is held, the inspection described in this
sec-tion is consented to by the applicant. An annual renewal and inspection
shall be done within twelve (12)-months of the initial permit issuance date, at
a fee determined by the City Council via resolution.
      1.   Prior to the keeping of any chickens, a party seeking to keep
chickens shall obtain a permit from the City. A permit fee may be established
by resolution of the City Council and may be revised from time to time. Only
one permit shall be issued per lot. Issuance of a permit is a discretionary
act, based on a complete application being provided and all requirements being
met.
      2.   The owner of the chickens shall keep a copy of all signed City
approval documents for inspection upon request by law enforcement, animal
control officer or Zoning Code official.
      3.   A permit for chickens under this section does not relieve any party
from any requirement to obtain any other permit or other necessary approvals
for any structure, fence, lighting, heat source, etc., as required by this Code
or State of Montana Code.
      4.   A party wishing to keep chickens shall submit an application to the
Three Forks City office.
      5.   The application shall contain the following:
         a.   A sketch identifying the property boundaries, the location of all
structures on the property and distances between said structure and between the
property boundaries. The sketch must also indicate the location of the chicken
enclosure and henhouse.
         b.   A description of cubic footage of the henhouse.
         c.   The name, address, and signed statement of the property owner, if
different from the applicant, consenting to the keeping of the applied for
number of chickens on the property.
         d.   A sworn statement that all statements contained in the
application are true and that the permit holder shall keep the chicken in
compliance with the terms of the permit, application and this section.
   B.   Roosters: No roosters shall be kept or maintained within the City.
   C.   Number Of Chickens: The number of chickens authorized per permit shall
comply with the following, subject to all other standards in this article:
      1.   For each residential parcel, up to six (6) chickens.
      2.   For parcels with multiple households the physical area used for
determining the maximum number of allowed hens is exclusive to each permit and
may not overlap. This may restrict the number of permits issued on a given
parcel.
   D.   General Regulations For Keeping Chickens:
      1.   No chickens may run at large within the corporate limits of the
City. All chickens must be contained within the permittee's property boundary.
      2.   The permittee shall provide the chickens with a cover, predatorproof
henhouse that is thoroughly ventilated, of sufficient size to admit free
movement of the chickens. The henhouse must be adjacent to and provide free
access to the chicken enclosure. Any heat source or electrical facilities
installed in a chicken house must comply with all adopted Building and
Electrical Codes of the State of Montana.
      3.   Chickens shall be secured within the enclosure from sunset to
sunrise.
      4.   Chicken enclosures and houses must be kept in a neat and sanitary
condition at all times, and must be cleaned on a regular basis so as to prevent
offensive odors.
      5.   Storage of chicken manure must be in a fully enclosed bin/container
as to prevent offensive odors.
      6.   Chickens shall have continuous access to adequate food and water.
      7.   Store feed must be kept in rodent and predator proof containers.
      8.   Chickens shall be maintained in a healthy condition. Ill chickens
shall either receive appropriate medical care or be culled.
      9.   No henhouse shall be located closer than twenty feet (20') to any
structure inhabited by someone other than the chicken owner, custodian or
keeper, and not closer than ten feet (10') to any property line. Henhouses may
be movable but must comply with all standards of this section.
      10.   Henhouses will not be permitted in any front yard.
      11.   No chickens shall be slaughtered within the public view.
   E.   Compliance With Investigator: If during any inspection by any of those
listed above, the investigator determines changes are to be made to the
enclosure, henhouse, or the number of chickens to be kept, or require
mitigation for the impact to adjacent properties, such as fencing or other
screening, the applicant/permit holder shall comply with the order of the
investigator. A person aggrieved by a decision of the investigator may appeal
to the City of Three Forks' Variance Board, who shall review all applicable
information and issue a decision on the appeal. Appeals on the Variance Board's
decision may be made to the City Council. At the time of the final approval by
the initial investigator, the investigator/officer shall indicate final
approval on the permit and keep a record of final approval.
   F.   Permit Specific To Permit Holder: A permit to keep chickens is specific
to the permit holder and the location of the permit. A person wishing to move
chickens to a different property shall obtain a new permit. A new resident of a
property who intends to keep chickens shall obtain a new permit regardless of
whether chickens were kept on the property or continue to be kept on the
property.
   G.   Changes In Standards: Changes to the standards contained in this
section shall require any permit holder to comply with any new standard,
regulation, or condition and no notice to a permit holder is required prior to
enforcement of any new standard beyond that required for adoption of a new or
revised ordinance.
   H.   Zoning Permit Issuance: Any enclosure, building, structure or henhouse
that exists, or will be built or brought onto the residential property for the
use of raising chickens must apply for and be issued a zoning permit and where
applicable a floodplain permit. If the permittee is adding a structure of any
kind which will be located within the floodplain, the permittee must comply
with all ordinances regarding floodproofing of the structure. (Ord. 348-14, 2-
25-2014; amd. Ord. 372-2017, 6-27-2017; Ord. 400-2023, 3-14-2023)
6-4B-3: PROHIBITION OF PASTURES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or pasture any hoofed animals and
fowl within the City limits excepting chickens allowed to be kept by City
ordinance, and those animals in times of rodeos and parades. (Ord. 344-13, 11-
26-2013)
6-4B-4: EXCEPTIONS:
This article will not apply nor will it be enforced against any property or
animals located on property within the City limits that lies west of the
Jefferson River. (Ord. 226, 1993)
6-4B-5: FINES COLLECTED:
All fees, fines and forfeitures collected hereunder shall be deposited in the
General Fund of the City and dispensed as the City Council may provide. (Ord.
226, 1993)
6-4B-6: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of violating any provision of this article shall be
subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code, including revocation of the permit. "Offense" is defined as
each animal for each day. (Ord. 372-2017, 6-27-2017)
   6-4C ()CHAPTER 4
   ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE C. ANIMALS RUNNING AT LARGE
SECTION:
6-4C-1: Definitions
6-4C-2: Owner's Duty
6-4C-3: Violation; Fines Imposed
6-4C-1: DEFINITIONS:
   ANIMAL: Includes both male and female.
   OWNER: Any person or persons, firm, association, or corporation owning,
keeping, or harboring an animal.
   RUNNING AT LARGE: An animal is defined as "running at large" which is off
the owned or leased premises of the animal's owner, unless he shall be under
leash and under the control of a competent person. (Ord. 209, 12-9-1986)
6-4C-2: OWNER'S DUTY:
The owner or keeper of any animal within the City limits shall at all times
prohibit and prevent said animal from being at large. (Ord. 209, 12-9-1986)
6-4C-3: VIOLATION; FINES IMPOSED:
   A.   Fines Imposed: Any person violating the provisions of this Article
shall be guilty of a public offense and shall be fined as follows:
      1.   Upon a first conviction, a fine of twenty five dollars ($25.00)
shall be imposed.
      2.   Upon a second conviction within one year from the date of the first
conviction, the fine shall be twice the amount of the fine for the first
conviction.
      3.   Upon a third conviction within one year from date of the first
conviction, the fine shall be four (4) times the amount of the fine for the
first conviction.
      4.   Upon a fourth conviction within one year from the date of the first
conviction, the fine shall be eight (8) times the amount of the fine for the
first conviction.
   B.   Jail Sentence: In addition to the fines set forth above, any one
conviction may include sentence in the Gallatin County jail for a period of not
more than ten (10) days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. (Ord. 209, 12-
9-1986)
TITLE 7
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC REGULATIONS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Adoption Of State Regulations
7-1-2: Definitions
7-1-3: Mayor And Police Officers; Enforcement
7-1-4: Government Vehicles
7-1-5: Authorized Emergency Vehicles; Exemptions
7-1-6: Pushcarts, Bicycles, Animals
7-1-7: Traffic Signs And Signals
7-1-8: Crosswalks For Pedestrians
7-1-9: Lanes For Traffic
7-1-10: Bicycles, Skateboards And Vehicles On Sidewalks
7-1-11: Air Compression Brakes
7-1-1: ADOPTION OF STATE REGULATIONS:
   A.   Adoption: All ordinances of the City relating to the regulation of
traffic within the City are hereby revised and recodified by the adoption of
the Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways as set forth in title 61,
chapters 8 and 9, Montana Code Annotated, and as amended from time to time.
   B.   Copy On File: One full printed copy of the Act is on file in the Office
of the City Clerk. The aforesaid Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways is
hereby adopted by reference and made a part of this chapter as fully, for all
intents and purposes, as though set forth herein at length. (2000 Code)
7-1-2: DEFINITIONS:
All words and phrases used in this chapter, the definitions of which are not
herein given, shall be given the ordinary meanings. Whenever in this chapter
the following terms are used, they shall have the meanings respectively
ascribed to them in this section:
   ARTERIAL HIGHWAYS: That portion of Montana State Highway 10 within the
limits of the City of Three Forks, Montana; all of Main Street in the City of
Three Forks, Montana; and all those streets and avenues which may be hereafter
designated by the Council as arterial highways.
   AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLE: Vehicles of the Fire Department, police
vehicles and such ambulances and emergency vehicles of City departments as are
designated or authorized by the Mayor.
   BUSINESS DISTRICT: All that part or those parts of Three Forks on Main
Street and that portion or those portions of Montana State Highway 10 within
the limits of the City of Three Forks, Montana.
   CAMPING, PRIVATE NON-COMMERCIAL: The use of temporary living accommodations
such as tents, tepees, yurts, and recreation vehicles such as motor homes,
campers, or trailers or any other vehicle or structure not permitted.
   COUNCIL: The City Council.
   CROSSWALK: That portion of a street or roadway ordinarily included within
the prolongation of curb and property lines at intersections, or any other
portion of a street or roadway clearly indicated for pedestrian crossing by
lines or other markings on the surface.
   INTERSECTION: The area embraced within the prolongation of the lateral curb
lines, or, if none, then, the lateral boundary lines of two (2) or more streets
or highways which join one another at an angle, whether or not one such street
or highway crosses the other.
   MAYOR: The Mayor of the City.
   MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle as herein defined, which is self- propelled.
   OFFICIAL TRAFFIC SIGNS: All signs, markings and devices, other than signals,
not inconsistent with this chapter, placed or erected by authority of the Mayor
or other official having jurisdiction, for the purpose of guiding, directing,
warning or regulating traffic.
   OPERATOR: Any person who is in actual physical control of a vehicle.
   PARKING: The standing of a vehicle, whether occupied or not, upon a street
or roadway, otherwise than temporarily for the purpose of and while actually
engaged in loading or unloading, or in obedience to traffic regulations or
traffic signs or signals.
   PEDESTRIAN: Any person afoot.
   POLICE OFFICER: Every police officer or any officer authorized to direct or
regulate traffic or to make arrests for violations of traffic regulations.
   PRIVATE ROAD OR DRIVEWAY: Every road or driveway not open to the use of the
public for purposes of vehicular travel.
   RESIDENCE DISTRICT: All that part or those parts of Three Forks not included
in the business district.
   RIGHT-OF-WAY: The privilege of the immediate use of a street, roadway or
highway.
   ROADWAY: That portion of a street, avenue or alley between the regularly
established curb lines, and, where there are no curbs, that part devoted to
vehicular traffic.
   SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between the curb lines and the adjacent
property lines.
   STREET: "Avenue" and "alley".
   TRAFFIC: Pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles and other
conveyances, either singly or together, while using any street, roadway or
highway for purposes of travel.
   TRAFFIC CONTROL SIGNAL: Any device using colored lights, or words, or any
combination thereof, whether manually, electrically or mechanically operated,
by which traffic is alternately directed to stop and to proceed. It also
includes stationary "stop" signs.
   VEHICLE: Every machine in, upon or by which a person or objects may be
transported or drawn upon a street or roadway, whether currently operable or
not, except devices moved by human power or used exclusively upon stationary
rails or tracks. (1977 Code § 10.16.010; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-
2009; Ord. 376-2017, 10-10-2017)
7-1-3: MAYOR AND POLICE OFFICERS; ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Enforcement Authority: It shall be the duty of the Mayor and police
officers of the City to enforce the provisions of this chapter. The police
officers are hereby authorized to direct all traffic, either in person or by
means of visible or audible signal in conformance with the provisions of this
chapter; provided, that in the event of a fire or other emergency, or to
expedite traffic or safeguard pedestrians, the police officers or Fire
Department may direct traffic, as conditions may require, notwithstanding the
provisions of this chapter. (1977 Code § 10.16.020; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-
09-10, 11-10-2009)
   B.   Noncompliance: It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse or fail to
comply with any lawful order, signal or direction of the police officers with
reference to "traffic" as defined in section
7-1-2 of this chapter. (1977 Code § 10.16.030; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10,
11-10-2009)
7-1-4: GOVERNMENT VEHICLES:
The provisions of this chapter shall apply to the operator of any vehicle owned
by or used in the service of the United States government, the State, the
County, or the City, and it shall be unlawful for any said operator to violate
any of the provisions of this chapter, except as otherwise herein provided.
(1977 Code § 10.16.040)
7-1-5: AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES; EXEMPTIONS:
The provisions of this chapter regulating the movement, parking and standing of
vehicles shall not apply to "authorized emergency vehicles" as defined in this
chapter while the driver of such vehicle is operating the same in an emergency
in the necessary performance of public duties. This exemption shall not,
however, protect the driver of any such vehicle from the consequence of a
reckless disregard of the safety of others. (1977 Code § 10.16.050)
7-1-6: PUSHCARTS, BICYCLES, ANIMALS:
Every person propelling any pushcart or riding a bicycle or an animal upon a
roadway, and every person driving any animal, shall be subject to the
provisions of this chapter applicable to the operator of any vehicle, except
those provisions of this chapter with reference to the equipment of vehicles
and except those provisions which by their very nature can have no application.
(1977 Code § 10.16.060)
7-1-7: TRAFFIC SIGNS AND SIGNALS:
   A.   Placement And Enforcement:
      1.   The Mayor shall determine and designate the character or type of all
official traffic signs and signals, and it shall be his duty to place and
maintain, or cause to be placed and maintained, all official traffic signs and
signals required hereunder.
      2.   No provision of this chapter for which signs are required shall be
enforceable against an alleged violator, if, at the time and place of the
alleged violation, the sign herein required is not in proper position and
sufficiently legible to be seen in the exercise of ordinary care and caution.
Whenever a particular section does not state that signs are required, such
section shall be effective without signs being erected to give notice thereof.
(1977 Code § 10.16.070)
   B.   Disobeying: It shall be unlawful for any operator to disobey the
instructions of any official traffic sign or signal placed in accordance with
the provisions of this chapter, unless otherwise directed by a police officer.
(1977 Code § 10.16.080; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
   C.   Unofficial Signs And Signals:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or maintain or to
display upon or in view of any street any unofficial sign, signal or device
which purports to be or is an imitation of or resembles an official traffic
sign or signal, or which attempts to direct the movement of traffic or which
hides from view any official traffic sign or signal.
      2.   Every such prohibited sign, signal or device is hereby declared to
be a public nuisance, and the Mayor is hereby empowered to remove the same, or
cause it to be removed, without notice. (1977 Code § 10.16.090)
   D.   Defacing Signs Or Signals: It shall be unlawful for any person to
wilfully deface, injure, move, obstruct or interfere with any official traffic
sign or signal or barricade. (1977 Code § 10.16.100)
7-1-8: CROSSWALKS FOR PEDESTRIANS:
The Mayor is hereby authorized to establish and to designate and shall
thereafter maintain, or cause to be maintained, by appropriate devices, marks
or lines upon the surface of the street, roadway or highway, crosswalks at
intersections where, in his opinion, there is particular danger to pedestrians
crossing the street, roadway or highway, and at such other places as he may
deem necessary. (1977 Code § 10.16.110)
7-1-9: LANES FOR TRAFFIC:
The Mayor is hereby authorized to mark or cause to be marked lanes for traffic
on street pavements at such places as he may deem advisable, consistent with
the provisions of this chapter. (1977 Code § 10.16.120)
7-1-10: BICYCLES, SKATEBOARDS AND VEHICLES ON SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Unlawful Use Of Sidewalks: No person shall make unlawful, unauthorized
or improper use of the sidewalks upon any of the streets in the City; nor ride,
drive or use thereon any bicycle, velocipede, skateboard, scooter, motorcycle,
motor vehicle, or any riding machine/device of any kind.
   B.   Exemptions: Handicap use of motorized mobility; riders learning to ride
or using training wheels; motorized use of snow removal equipment during
inclement weather conditions.
   C.   Penalty: Any person who violates any of the provisions of this section
shall, upon conviction, be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 338-13, 9-10-2013)
7-1-11: AIR COMPRESSION BRAKES:
   A.   Use Prohibited; Exception: The use of air compression brakes generally
known as "jake brakes" is hereby prohibited within the City limits. An
exception shall be if, in an emergency situation, the use of air compression
brakes is necessary to prevent accident or injury to persons or property.
   B.   Penalty: Any person who violates any provision of this section shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 258-99, 6-8-1999; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Definition
7-2-2: Power Of The Mayor
7-2-3: Removal, Impounding, Return Of Motor Vehicles
7-2-4: Fines And Penalties
7-2-5: General Parking Regulations
7-2-6: Parking Prohibited In Specific Places
7-2-7: No Parking Of Certain Vehicles
7-2-8: Responsibility For Charges
7-2-9: Parking Near Driveways Entering Main Street
7-2-10: Angle Parking
7-2-11: Handicapped Parking
7-2-12: U-Turns
7-2-13: Restricted Parking
7-2-14: Residential Parking Restrictions
7-2-15: School Area Parking Restrictions
7-2-1: DEFINITION:
For the purpose of this chapter, a "motor vehicle" includes all kinds of
vehicles, any kind of trailer, camper, recreational vehicles, boats, trucks and
semitrucks with or without trailers. (Ord. 310-09, 5-12-2009)
7-2-2: POWER OF THE MAYOR:
The Mayor of the City of Three Forks is empowered to designate areas of
parking, limitations on parking, no parking, standing or stopping. He/she is
hereby authorized and empowered to designate areas or zones of parking, no
parking, restricted or limited parking such as handicapped parking, standing or
stopping, and may provide for the erection of suitable signs and/or designate
such zones by providing for the painting of the curb a color recognized by the
Department of Transportation to designate a specific zone. Any person stopping,
standing or parking in such zones as the Mayor may designate hereunder, that
does not have proper permitting, shall be subject to the punitive provision of
this chapter. (Ord. 373-2017, 7-11-2017)
7-2-3: REMOVAL, IMPOUNDING, RETURN OF MOTOR VEHICLES:
Motor vehicles parked in violation of any section of this chapter may be
removed or impounded by any police officer or highway patrolman in accordance
with this Code at owner's expense. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-4: FINES AND PENALTIES:
See section
1-4-1, "General Penalty", of this Code. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-5: GENERAL PARKING REGULATIONS:
   A.   No person shall park any vehicle, or trailer, boat, camper or
motorcycle upon any street, roadway, thoroughfare or alley; or on and in any
other public place for the principal purpose of:
      1.   Displaying such vehicle or motor vehicle for sale.
      2.   Greasing, maintaining or repairing such vehicle, except repairs that
are necessitated by an emergency rendering vehicle inoperable. (Ord. 268, 2-11-
2003)
   B.   When a vehicle is loading or unloading within a public alley, ten feet
(10') of the width of the alleyway shall be available at all times for the free
movement of vehicular traffic. When such a vehicle is loading or unloading in
an alley, the same shall not be parked in such a position as to block the
driveway or entrance of any abutting property, except for in Central Business
District. (Ord. 376-2017, 10-10-2017)
   C.   City streets are not to be used as storage areas. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
   D.   Except as otherwise provided, a vehicle parked upon a public street or
thoroughfare shall be parked or stopped parallel to the travelled way facing
the same direction as the traffic flow upon such street or thoroughfare.
Further, parking or stopping shall be of such a distance as to not block,
inhibit or impair the travelled way in any manner, including but not limited to
opening doors shall not interfere or cross the plane of the travelled way.
   E.   Camping, private non-commercial is prohibited within the Municipal
limits, except in authorized and permitted campgrounds.
   F.   No vehicle, inoperable or unlicensed vehicle, inoperable or unlicensed
trailer, inoperable or unlicensed camper or inoperable or unlicensed
recreational vehicle may remain standing or parked on one side of the public
street within any one block for more than seventy two (72) hours. After seventy
two (72) hours, any vehicle and any inoperable or unlicensed vehicle,
inoperable or unlicensed trailer, inoperable or unlicensed camper or inoperable
or unlicensed recreational vehicle may be declared abandoned and a five (5) day
notice of intent to remove and impound may be placed on the vehicle, trailer,
camper or recreational vehicle by the City or law enforcement. The cost of
towing and impoundment storage is the responsibility of the owner. (Ord. 376-
2017, 10-10-2017)
7-2-6: PARKING PROHIBITED IN SPECIFIC PLACES:
No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid
conflict with other traffic, or in compliance with the directions of a police
or traffic control officer or highway patrolman in any of the following places:
   A.   On a sidewalk, walkways and trails.
   B.   In front of a public or private driveway.
   C.   Within an intersection or within fifteen feet (15') of an intersection.
   D.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
   E.   On a crosswalk, or within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk when marked
by painted lines and designated by a sign.
   F.   Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk at an intersection.
   G.   Within twenty feet (20') of the approach to any traffic signal, stop
sign or other traffic control device located at the side of a roadway.
   H.   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or construction when
stopping or parking would obstruct the flow of traffic; or leave less than
twenty feet (20') of available roadway from the free movement of traffic.
   I.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge of a
curb, roadway or street.
   J.   Upon any bridge or elevated structure within the City.
   K.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping. (Ord. 268, 2-11-
2003)
7-2-7: NO PARKING OF CERTAIN VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful at any time to park a motor vehicle giving off an
offensive or disagreeable odor, or any tank truck, tank trailer or like vehicle
containing or used for the transportation of gasoline, butane, fuel oil or
other highly toxic flammable substance to be parked on any street, alley, park
or other public place or upon any private property in the City where it would
create a hazard to life or adjacent property for a period longer than thirty
(30) minutes; however, this restriction shall not be construed to prevent the
delivery of such liquid to retail gas stations or to private residence or
business or business property, but only for so long as is reasonably necessary
to complete such delivery. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-8: RESPONSIBILITY FOR CHARGES:
The owner of a vehicle, which has been removed or impounded, will be
responsible for moving and storage expenses arising from the transportation of
said vehicle. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-9: PARKING NEAR DRIVEWAYS ENTERING MAIN STREET:
   A.   East Side: It shall be illegal for any person to park any motor vehicle
within fourteen feet (14') of the north side and four feet (4') on the south
side of any driveway entering upon the east side of Main Street located in the
City.
   B.   West Side: It shall be illegal for any person to park any motor vehicle
within fourteen feet (14') of the south side and four feet (4') of the north
side of any driveway entering upon the west side of Main Street located in the
City. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-10: ANGLE PARKING:
Upon those streets which have been marked or signed for angle parking, vehicles
shall be parked wholly within, or between, two (2) such adjacent marks or
signs. In the Business District, all vehicles must be parked on, and by turning
the same to, the right side of the street in the direction which such vehicles
are facing. No left turns into parking spaces. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-11: HANDICAPPED PARKING:
   A.   Definition: For the purpose of this section, "physically handicapped"
means a physical disability, in firmness, malformation or disfigurement which
is caused by bodily injury, birth defects or illness. It includes, without
limitation, any degree of paralysis, amputation, lack of physical coordination,
dependence upon a wheelchair or any other remedial appliance or device.
   B.   Reserved Handicapped Parking: Whenever a particular parking space has
been designated and reserved for the handicapped, no person shall park in said
space unless he/she has visibly displayed on his/her vehicle a valid
handicapped parking permit or license plate issued by a municipality, the State
of Montana or any other state, or the Veterans' Administration. (Ord. 268, 2-
11-2003)
   C.   Designated Handicapped Parking: A parking space reserved for a person
with a disability must be designated by a sign showing the international symbol
of accessibility, indicating that a permit is required, and stating the penalty
for a violation. Violators will pay a one hundred dollar ($100.00) fine. (Ord.
374-2017, 7-11-2017)
7-2-12: U-TURNS:
Main Street: It shall be unlawful for the operator of any motor vehicle to make
a U-turn for parking or any other purpose on Main Street or in the business
district of the City. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003)
7-2-13: RESTRICTED PARKING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to park on Main Street between Ash Street
and Date Street from three o'clock (3:00) A.M. to five o'clock (5:00) A.M. any
vehicle. (Ord. 278-03-04, 4-13-2004)
7-2-14: RESIDENTIAL PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Within the borders of an officially designated residential district or
on the side of any street which borders or is within the borders of an
officially designated residential district, no person shall allow a motor
vehicle that is licensed for highway use, while such vehicle is parked or
standing to: (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003; amd. Ord. 376-2017, 10-10-2017)
      1.   Operate its refrigeration and/or generator unit;
      2.   Allow its engine to run more than thirty (30) minutes in any twelve
(12) hour period, or allow its generator to run more than sixty (60) minutes in
any twelve (12) hour period except when temperature is ten degrees (10°) below
zero Fahrenheit; (Ord. 376-2017, 10-10-2017)
      3.   Hold a load of live animals or offensively odorous material for more
than one hour in any twelve (12) hour period. (Ord. 268, 2-11-2003; amd. Ord.
376-2017, 10-10-2017)
7-2-15: SCHOOL AREA PARKING RESTRICTIONS:
Exclusive of adjacent lot owners who will be issued a City permit to exceed the
one (1) hour parking, and School-issued parking permits for School-maintained
property, parking shall be restricted in the City right-of-way as follows:
   A.   Year round:
      1.   East Oak Street - between North 5th Avenue East and North 4th Avenue
East:
         a.   One-way traffic flow pattern traveling east to west from North
5th Avenue to North 4th Avenue East;
         b.   North half of this block has designated angled parking spaces;
         c.   South half of East Oak Street is designated "No Parking".
      2.   North 4th Avenue East - from East Oak Street to East Neal Street:
         a.   One-way traffic flow pattern traveling from north to south;
      3.   East Oak Street - between North 2nd Avenue East and MT Hwy-2/
Frontage Road:
         a.   North half of East Oak Street "No Parking".
   B.   Commencing on roughly August 20 of each year and continuing through
roughly June 6 of the next calendar year (as the school dates change from year
to year), from the hours of seven thirty o’clock (7:30) A.M. to four o’clock
(4:00) P.M. Monday through Thursday, parking and stopping of any vehicles as
defined in section
7-2-1 of this Title and Chapter shall be restricted as follows. (Refer to
Section E of this Title and Chapter for outside school dates.)
      1.   North 4th Avenue East - from East Oak Street to East Neal Street:
         a.   Easterly side one (1) hour parking;
         b.   Westerly side Student loading/unloading and handicap spaces.
      2.   North 4th Avenue East - from East Neal Street to East Ash Street
(both sides of street):
         a.   One (1) hour parking.
      3.   North 3rd Avenue East - from East Neal Street to East Ash Street
(both sides of street):
         a.   One (1) hour parking.
      4.   North 2nd Avenue East - from MT Hwy-2/Frontage Road to East Oak
Street:
         a.   Both sides are all day parking, maximum seventy-two (72) hours
(refer to section
7-2-5(F) of this Title).
      5.   North 2nd Avenue East - from East Oak Street to East Neal Street:
         a.   Easterly side is all day parking, maximum seventy-two (72) hours
(refer to section
7-2-5(F) of this Title);
         b.   Westerly side only one (1) hour parking.
      6.   North 2nd Avenue East - from East Neal Street to East Ash Street:
         a.   North half of Easterly side is all day parking, maximum seventy-
two (72) hours (refer to section
7-2-5(F) of this Title);
         b.   South half of Easterly side one (1) hour parking;
         c.   Westerly side one (1) hour parking.
      7.   East Oak Street - between North 2nd Avenue East and MT Hwy-2/
Frontage Road:
         a.   South half one (1) hour parking.
      8.   East Neal Street - between North 2nd and North 4th Avenues East:
         a.   North half is designated (from west to east) as student drop off/
pick up, followed by Emergency Services parking, then delivery and/or supply
loading and unloading, and finally handicap parking spaces.
         b.   South half (from west to east):
         (1)   Adjacent to the parking lot is all day parking, maximum seventy-
two (72) hours (refer to section
7-2-5(F) of this Title);
         (2)   From the alley between North 2nd and 3rd Avenues East all the
way to North 4th Avenue East is one (1) hour parking.
   C.   The City shall issue parking permit(s) exempting the adjacent lot owner
(s) from the one (1) hour parking area restrictions and authorizing adjacent
lot owner(s) permission to park vehicles in the one (1) hour parking area for
longer than the restricted time so long as the City-issued parking permit is
displayed in the windshield. The parking permit does not authorize the holder
to park in any other parking restricted area(s) of the City, nor park longer
than seventy-two (72) hours (refer to section
7-2-5(F) of this Title).
   D.   Three Forks School District shall issue parking permits for the school
employees/students parking lots, which are outside of the City's rights-of-way,
and administer the permits as it sees fit.
   E.   Any time outside of the dates and hours listed in section
7-2-15(B) are exempt from these provisions, as are special events held at the
School (i.e. sports, programs, open houses) which draw larger crowds than
normal daily activities. (Ord. 362-15, 8-25-2015; amd. Ord. 403-2024, 11-12-
2024)
CHAPTER 3
SNOWMOBILES 1
SECTION:
7-3-1: Use Of Streets And Highways Within City
7-3-2: Operation Of Snowmobiles
7-3-3: Excessive Noise
7-3-4: Headlights And Taillights
7-3-5: Fluorescent Flag
7-3-6: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 5, chapter 8 of this code.
7-3-1: USE OF STREETS AND HIGHWAYS WITHIN CITY:
   A.   Streets: The streets within the city shall be used only as a method of
transportation and not as a means of recreation. Streets shall only be used to
get in and out of the city, and for other necessary travel. (1977 Code §
10.12.010)
   B.   Highways: Highways cannot be used within the city limits, except for a
ninety degree (90°) angle crossing. (1977 Code § 10.12.050)
7-3-2: OPERATION OF SNOWMOBILES:
   A.   Stop At Intersections: Full stops shall be made at all intersections.
(1977 Code § 10.12.020)
   B.   Single File; Speed: Snowmobiles will travel only in single file on the
right side of streets, at a speed of fifteen (15) miles per hour or less. (1977
Code § 10.12.030)
   C.   Operating On Private Property: Snowmobiles will not be operated on
private property without the permission of the owner, and at no time shall they
be operated on sidewalks or posted areas. (1977 Code § 10.12.040)
   D.   Nighttime Snowmobiling: No snowmobiling shall be done after the hour of
ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. within the city except in going to, or returning from
an evening ride. (1977 Code § 10.12.060)
7-3-3: EXCESSIVE NOISE:
Excessive noise shall be considered disturbing the peace. (1977 Code §
10.12.070)
7-3-4: HEADLIGHTS AND TAILLIGHTS:
Headlights and taillights shall be on at all times while operating on the
streets. (1977 Code § 10.12.080)
7-3-5: FLUORESCENT FLAG:
A snowmobile shall at all times display a fluorescent flag at least five feet
(5') from surface level. (1977 Code § 10.12.090)
7-3-6: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon
conviction, be subject to penalty as provided in section
 1-4-1 of this code. (1977 Code § 10.12.100; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GOLF CARTS
SECTION:
7-4-1: Use Of Streets And Highways Within City
7-4-2: Operation Of Golf Carts
7-4-3: Excessive Noise
7-4-4: Penalty
7-4-1: USE OF STREETS AND HIGHWAYS WITHIN CITY:
   A.   Streets: The streets within the city shall be used only as a method of
transportation and not as a means of recreation. Golf carts shall use the
streets only to get in and out of the city, and for other necessary travel.
(Ord. 210, 7-14-1987)
   B.   Highways: Highways cannot be used within the city limits, except for
crossing. (Ord. 322-11, 6-14-2011)
7-4-2: OPERATION OF GOLF CARTS:
   A.   Stop At Intersections: Golf carts shall make a full stop at all
intersections where stop signs are located and otherwise shall follow all the
rules of the road. (Ord. 210, 7-14-1987)
   B.   Single File; Speed: (Rep. by Ord. 322-11, 6-14-2011)
   C.   Operation On Private Property: Golf carts will not be operated on
private property without the permission of the owner, and at no time shall they
be operated on sidewalks or posted areas. (Ord. 210, 7-14-1987)
   D.   Nighttime Use Of Golf Carts: No golf cart shall be operated one hour
after sunset or before sunrise within the city and only when the cart is
equipped with proper lighting equipment comparable to lighting equipment for
motor vehicles. (Ord. 322-11, 6-14-2011)
7-4-3: EXCESSIVE NOISE:
Excessive noise shall be considered disturbing the peace. (Ord. 210, 7-14-1987)
7-4-4: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter shall, upon
conviction, be subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (Ord. 210, 7-14-1987; amd. 2000 Code)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
EXCAVATIONS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Excavations In Public Streets
8-1-2: Excavations For Poles
8-1-1: EXCAVATIONS IN PUBLIC STREETS:
   A.   Removal Of Natural Soil; Permit Required: It shall be unlawful, within
the corporate limits of the City, for any person to make any excavation in any
of the public streets and alleys, and to disturb and remove from the surface of
said streets and alleys any of the natural soil, dirt and earth belonging
thereon, except as provided in this Section, and without first obtaining a
license as provided for in Section
8-1-2 of this Chapter. (1977 Code § 12.02.010; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Improving Streets: Nothing in this Section shall be construed to
prevent or to prohibit the use, working, grading and improving said streets and
alleys as may be authorized by law, and ordinances of the City. (1977 Code §
12.02.020)
   C.   Penalty: Any person violating any of the provisions of this Section
shall, upon conviction for each and every offense, be subject to penalty as
provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1977 Code § 12.02.030; amd. 2000 Code)
8-1-2: EXCAVATIONS FOR POLES:
   A.   Application For Permit: It shall hereafter be unlawful for any person,
association, corporation or company to make or cause to be made, any excavation
in any of the streets, avenues, alleys or other public grounds within the
corporate limits of the City for the purpose of erecting or placing any
telephone, telegraph, electric light or other like poles, or pole used or to be
used for any like purpose, or to erect any poles therein without first making
application to the Street Superintendent for a permit to do the same, and
obtaining from said Superintendent a permit in writing to make such excavation
and erect such poles.
   B.   Contents Of Application; Pole Location: Such application shall show the
location of such poles when erected, but such location may be changed by the
City Council so as to conform to existing conditions and the ordinances of the
City; and the location of such poles, when determined, shall be, in all cases,
done under the supervision of the Street Superintendent acting under the advice
and direction of the City Council. (1977 Code § 12.16.010; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 2
SIDEWALK CONSTRUCTION
SECTION:
8-2-1: Sidewalk Specifications And Grade On Main Street
8-2-2: Construction Requirements For Sidewalks On Main Street
8-2-3: Property Owner To Build Or Repair
8-2-4: Repair Of Deteriorated Sidewalks; Lien For Costs
8-2-5: Construction Of New Sidewalks
8-2-6: Obstructing Streets During Construction Or Repair
8-2-7: Width Of Sidewalks
8-2-8: Penalty
8-2-1: SIDEWALK SPECIFICATIONS AND GRADE ON MAIN STREET:
   A.   Supervision: All sidewalks constructed and laid upon either side of
Main Street in the City between the south line of Blocks 47 and 48 to its
intersection with the east line of Railway Avenue shall be constructed of
cement or concrete material, and shall be constructed and laid under the
direction and supervision of the City Engineer and according to the provisions
of this Chapter, the surveys and profiles of Main Street now on file in the
office of the City Clerk, and the plans and specifications prepared and adopted
by the City Council. (1977 Code § 12.04.010; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Specifications:
      1.   Sidewalks: The sidewalk on either side of Main Street shall be
fourteen feet (14') in width; the curb or sidewalk grade at edge nearest the
carriageway shall be four inches (4") higher than grade line of center of
street; the elevations of line "A" or top of sidewalk along the property line
shall be as follows at block corners; the figures used are in excess of four
thousand feet (4,000'):
South end Blocks               47 and 48 67.71
North end Blocks               47 and 48 67.41
South end Blocks               28 and 29 67.35
North end Blocks               28 and 29 67.05
South end Blocks               24 and 25 66.98
North end Blocks               24 and 25 66.68
South end Blocks               16 and 17 66.62
North end Blocks               16 and 17 66.32
South end Blocks               13 and 14 66.25
North end Blocks               13 and 14 65.95
South end Blocks               5 and 6   65.88
North end Blocks               5 and 6   65.58
Southwest Corner Block 4                 65.52
West line Block 4 in East line           65.39
of Railway Avenue
 
      2.   Gutters: The gutter shall be one and one-third feet (11/3') in depth
below top of curb; that grade of Main Street shall be six inches (6") lower
than line "A". (1977 Code § 12.04.020)
   C.   Grades: The grade of all sidewalks and improvements thereof made on
Main Street shall conform to the grade fixed by this Section and the surveys
and profiles having reference to Main Street, reported to and approved by the
City Council, and on file in the office of the City Clerk. (1977 Code §
12.04.030)
   D.   Penalty: All persons convicted of violating any of the provisions of
this Section shall be subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1977 Code § 12.04.040; amd. 2000 Code)
8-2-2: CONSTRUCTION REQUIREMENTS FOR SIDEWALKS ON MAIN STREET:
All sidewalks hereafter built on Main Street in the City shall be built
according to the provisions of Section
8-2-1 of this Chapter and shall be constructed as follows:
   A.   First or filler shall be gravel or cinders, and shall be well tamped in
layers four inches (4") thick.
   B.   Second or concrete shall be five inches (5") thick consisting of gravel
and sand to be mixed as follows: five (5) parts of gravel, three (3) parts of
sand to one part of cement.
   C.   Third or top coat shall be not less than one inch (1") thick and mixed
as follows: two (2) parts of sand to one part of cement.
   D.   The concrete shall be cut through into blocks not over five feet (5')
square and the cut shall extend through the concrete and either building paper
or sand inserted in the cut made in the concrete.
   E.   Top coat shall be cut through to the concrete and into blocks not over
five feet (5') square. The cut through the top coat for each block shall match
as nearly as possible the cut made in the concrete.
   F.   Curb shall be faced one inch (1") thick as built and shall be mixed two
(2) parts of sand to one part of cement. (1977 Code § 12.08.010)
8-2-3: PROPERTY OWNER TO BUILD OR REPAIR:
   A.   Requirement; Time Limit: All persons owning real property, a lot or
lots, abutting on Main Street between the south line of Blocks 47 and 48 and
its intersection with the east line of Railway Avenue in the City where there
are no sidewalks, or where the same are, for any reason, dangerous and unsafe
for public use and convenience, shall build, rebuild and repair the sidewalks
along and in front of such abutting property, and in conformity to the
provisions of the ordinances of the City relating to the grade and construction
of sidewalks on each side of Main Street and of this Chapter, within thirty
(30) days after this Chapter shall go into effect and be operative. (1977 Code
§ 12.08.020)
   B.   Council Resolution: At the expiration of the said thirty (30) days
mentioned in subsection A of this Section, the City Council shall, by
resolution, designate and describe the lot and block in front of which a
sidewalk shall be newly constructed and built, or rebuilt and repaired as
provided for in this Chapter. (1977 Code § 12.08.030)
   C.   Notice To Property Owner: At the expiration of thirty (30) days from
the date of the adoption and passage of the resolution mentioned in subsection
B of this Chapter, the Street Superintendent shall immediately give twenty (20)
days' notice, in writing, to the owner of the property abutting such sidewalk,
or his agent, lessee or tenant, either by mailing or delivering the same, and
if neither can be found or their address is unknown, then by posting a copy of
said notice near the front line of the lot in front of which the sidewalk is
ordered constructed or repaired, fully describing therein the termini, course,
width and character of the sidewalk ordered; during which the said parties so
desiring may construct or repair the sidewalk abutting their property, and
further providing that all such sidewalks so ordered, remaining unbuilt or not
