repaired at the expiration of said twenty (20) days from the date of said
notice, shall be built by the City Council at the expense of said property
owner as in this Chapter provided for. (1977 Code § 12.08.040; amd. 2000 Code)
8-2-4: REPAIR OF DETERIORATED SIDEWALKS; LIEN FOR COSTS:
   A.   Order Repair By Owner: Whenever any sidewalk which is now or which may
by reason of natural deterioration or decay, or by reason of unevenness, or for
any cause whatever, become unfit or unsafe for public travel, or dangerous to
the public safety, the Street Superintendent shall require the owner of the
premises abutting such sidewalk, or his agent, to immediately repair the same.
   B.   Failure Of Owner To Repair; Action By City: In case of his refusal or
neglect to comply with such requisition, or in case no one can be found upon
whom to serve such notice to repair such sidewalk, such sidewalk shall be
immediately removed, remodeled, rebuilt, paved, cleaned, repaired or newly
built under the direction of the Street Superintendent, or such other form of
relief as may be required to make the same fit for public travel, as in his
judgment may be most expedient.
   C.   Lien For Costs: The costs thereof shall be a lien upon the lot or lots
abutting upon such sidewalk, and may be enforced or the amount may be recovered
against the owner by a suit before a competent jurisdiction, or may be assessed
and collected as a special tax against such lot or lots as in other cases.
(1977 Code § 12.08.050; amd. 2000 Code)
   D.   Compliance With Document: All sidewalks in need of repair or replacing,
excluding Main Street, shall follow the Montana Code Annotated public works
document concerning Municipal sidewalks. (2000 Code)
8-2-5: CONSTRUCTION OF NEW SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Requirement; Notice; Lien For Costs:
      1.   The construction of all new sidewalks ordered, or that shall be
removed, remodeled, rebuilt, paved, cleaned, repaired or newly rebuilt as by
this Chapter required, shall be under the supervision and to the satisfaction
of the Street Superintendent.
      2.   The total cost of all sidewalks constructed by the City, or that may
be constructed or repaired by the Street Superintendent, in accordance with the
provisions of this Chapter, or in the maintenance of sidewalks, which total
costs shall include that of the sidewalk proper as well as that of any notice,
establishment of the grade and all other necessary expenditures, shall be
certified by the Street Superintendent to the City Treasurer, who shall
transmit forthwith a copy thereof to the owner of the property immediately
abutting upon said sidewalk, or to his agent, lessee or tenant, either by
mailing or delivering the same, which total cost of construction, repairing or
rebuilding must be paid within one month from the date thereof, and if not paid
within the said time, the same shall become a lien or tax against the lots
abutting upon such sidewalks and shall bear interest at the rate of one percent
(1%) per month until paid, and shall be collected at the same time and in the
same manner as other taxes affected by such charge. (1977 Code § 12.08.060;
amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Time Limit: At the expiration of twenty (20) days from the date of the
notice, as aforesaid, the Street Superintendent must cause to be built, such
portions of the sidewalks ordered that may not yet be built within twenty (20)
days from the date thereof, as may be ordered by the City Council. (1977 Code §
12.08.070; amd. 2000 Code)
8-2-6: OBSTRUCTING STREETS DURING CONSTRUCTION OR REPAIR:
   A.   Permit Required: None of the duties or privileges imposed or conferred
by this Chapter shall in any way be deemed to authorize or allow the
obstruction of any street either during or after any work upon any sidewalk,
except such as may be absolutely necessary to make such improvement, without a
permit therefor.
   B.   Granting Of Permit: No material removed from any sidewalk shall be
placed upon any portion of any adjacent street, alley or place unless a permit
therefor be granted. (1977 Code § 12.08.080)
   C.   Time Limit For Removal Of Debris: All refuse lumber and debris
remaining after the completion of any sidewalk, repairs or renewals of
sidewalk, shall be removed from the street forthwith, and any owner, lessee or
tenant of abutting property who shall fail to remove any such obstruction from
any street, alley or place within forty eight (48) hours after being notified
by the Street Superintendent so to do, shall be deemed guilty of maintaining a
public nuisance and shall be subject to the penalties prescribed for the
violation of any of the provisions of this Chapter.
   D.   Failure To Remove; Lien For Costs: In case of such failure to remove
obstructions after such notice, the Street Superintendent shall cause the same
to be removed and shall charge the full costs of such removal to such owner,
lessee or tenant and the said charge shall become a lien upon said abutting
property and shall be collected as hereinbefore provided for the collection of
cost of construction or repair of sidewalks. (1977 Code § 12.08.080; amd. 2000
Code)
8-2-7: WIDTH OF SIDEWALKS:
   A.   Width Specified: All sidewalks on both sides of all streets crossing
Main Street in the City for the distance of one block from each side of said
Main Street shall be eight feet (8') wide. (1977 Code § 12.12.010)
   B.   Uniformity Of Width; Grade: All sidewalks provided for in this Section
shall be uniform in width, built on grade established by ordinance and
according to specifications prescribed by ordinance. (1977 Code § 12.12.020)
8-2-8: PENALTY:
Unless otherwise provided, any person violating any of the provisions of this
Chapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof,
shall be subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1977 Code § 12.08.090; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 3
STREET AND AVENUE DESIGNATIONS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Datum Line Or Base
8-3-2: Benchmark
8-3-3: Grade Of Center Line
8-3-4: Elevations Of Crossings
8-3-5: Improvements
8-3-6: Penalty
8-3-1: DATUM LINE OR BASE:
The datum line or base from which the grades of the several streets and avenues
of Three Forks shall be determined, defined, fixed, and designated, shall be by
reference to the following described benchmarks: first, the top of the cement
work at the bottom of the small hole cut in the surface of the sidewalk at the
northeast corner of the square formed by the intersection of Main and Cedar
Streets, is sixty six and twenty five one- hundredths feet (66.25') above datum
and in line A of diagram. Datum is still further fixed by reference to the top
of the square stone set on the south side of the track of the N.P.R.Y. near the
present station for Three Forks, State of Montana, in the SW1/4 of Section 30,
in Township 2N Range 2E, the elevation of which is four thousand sixty one feet
(4,061') above sea level as published by authority of the U.S. Geological
Survey in the bulletin entitled "A Dictionary of Altitudes in the United
States". The elevation of the point on the datum or base line is, therefore,
referenced to sea level and is four thousand sixty six and twenty five one-
hundredths feet (4,066.25'), and for convenience in the use of the figures
referring to the elevations of points on the datum or base line for Main
Street, the figures in excess of four thousand feet (4,000') are used. (1977
Code § 10.02.010)
8-3-2: BENCHMARK:
A second benchmark shall be at the surface of the northeast corner of the
cement work around the "City pump" near the intersection of the east line of
Railway Avenue with the north line of Cedar Street; elevation above sea level,
four thousand sixty six and sixty eight one-hundredths feet (4,066.68'). (1977
Code § 10.02.020)
8-3-3: GRADE OF CENTER LINE:
The grade of center line of Main Street, from the south line of Blocks 47 and
48 to its intersection with the east line of Railway Avenue, in the Original
Townsite of Three Forks, shall be a uniform grade of one foot (1') in a
thousand, or elevation 67.21 to elevation 64.97. (1977 Code § 10.02.030)
8-3-4: ELEVATIONS OF CROSSINGS:
The elevations of crossings of center lines of streets with line "B" or grade
of center line of Main Street, in feet above Datum, shall be as follows, using
figures in excess of four thousand feet (4,000'):
Center of Main St in line with S. line of Blocks 47 and 48   67.21
Fir Street                                                     66.88
Elm Street                                                     66.51
Date Street                                                    66.15
Cedar Street                                                   65.75
Birch Street                                                   65.41
Ash Street                                                     65.05
Main Street and line Railway Avenue                            64.97
 
(1977 Code § 10.02.040)
8-3-5: IMPROVEMENTS:
All improvements hereafter made on Main Street shall conform to this Chapter
and the rules and regulations promulgated by the City Council, then reported to
and approved by the City Council and filed in the office of the City Clerk.
(1977 Code § 10.02.050)
8-3-6: PENALTY:
All persons convicted of violating any of the provisions of this Chapter shall
be subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this Code. (1977 Code § 10.02.060; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 4
STREET OBSTRUCTIONS
SECTION:
8-4-1: Obstructing Streets And Grounds Prohibited
8-4-2: Builders And Contractors Obstructing Streets
8-4-3: Unloading Of Materials
8-4-4: Fence Around Excavation Area
8-4-5: Wagons, Sleighs, Or Carriages On Streets
8-4-6: Deposit Of Boxes, Barrels
8-4-7: Playing Ball In Streets
8-4-8: Obstructions During Excavation
8-4-9: Stands, Booths On Streets
8-4-10: Owner Responsibility
8-4-11: Neglecting To Remove Obstructions
8-4-12: Penalty
8-4-1: OBSTRUCTING STREETS AND GROUNDS PROHIBITED:
The streets, avenues, alleys and other public grounds in the city shall be kept
free and clear of all obstructions, encumbrances and "encroachments of every
kind" and character whatsoever for the use of the public, and shall not be used
or occupied in any other way than is provided by law and the ordinances of the
city. (1977 Code § 10.04.010)
8-4-2: BUILDERS AND CONTRACTORS OBSTRUCTING STREETS:
It shall be unlawful hereafter for any builder, contractor, person, company or
corporation to build, erect, place or locate, or cause to be built, erected,
placed or located any building, fence, or obstruction, encumbrance or
encroachment of any kind or character whatsoever, in whole or in part, upon any
street, avenue, alley or other public grounds within the corporate limits of
the city. (1977 Code § 10.04.020; amd. 2000 Code)
8-4-3: UNLOADING OF MATERIALS:
It shall be unlawful for any builder, contractor, person, company or
corporation to encumber or obstruct, or make any encroachments upon, or cause
to be encumbered or obstructed, or cause to be made any "encroachments, in any
manner" whatever, upon any street, avenue, alley or other public grounds in the
city, by unloading, depositing or placing therein or thereon any building
material of whatever kind, or any article or thing whatever, tending to
obstruct, encumber or encroach thereon, without first having obtained written
permission therefor as provided in this chapter. (1977 Code § 10.04.030; amd.
2000 Code)
8-4-4: FENCE AROUND EXCAVATION AREA:
No city officer, builder, contractor, person, company or corporation shall make
any excavation, or dig any shaft, hole, drain or ditch in any street, avenue,
alley or other public grounds of the city without providing, during the
continuance of such excavation, shaft, hole, drain or ditch, a temporary fence
around or in front of the same, and also hanging red lights about said fence
and deposits of materials, from dark to daylight of each day, so as to be
plainly seen from every direction of public approach, and so long as said
excavation or obstruction shall continue in the sidewalk, street or avenue, in
order to prevent persons, animals or vehicles from falling or being driven into
the same. (1977 Code § 10.04.070; amd. 2000 Code)
8-4-5: WAGONS, SLEIGHS, OR CARRIAGES ON STREETS:
   A.   Prohibition: No wagon, sleigh, sled, carriage, or nonmotorized vehicle
of any kind or description, without horses or other beasts of burden, shall be
permitted to remain or stand in any street, avenue, alley, or on any public
grounds within the limits of the city, except for the purpose of being
repaired, and then only in front of the premises of the person so repairing,
and within twenty feet (20') of the property line of said premises. (1977 Code
§ 10.04.040; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Removal Authorized: Any such wagon, sleigh, sled, carriage, or other
vehicle, or any part of the same may be removed by a police officer; provided,
however, that the provisions of this section shall not apply to automobiles or
motorcycles when in use and left standing temporarily. (1977 Code § 10.04.040;
amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
8-4-6: DEPOSIT OF BOXES, BARRELS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or deposit empty boxes of any kind
whatever, barrels, straw, dirt, filth, chips, shavings, paper or other rubbish
in any street, avenue, alley or on any public grounds in the city. (1977 Code §
10.04.080; amd. 2000 Code)
8-4-7: PLAYING BALL IN STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to engage in any game of ball, or throw or
bat any ball, or to play at or engage in any other games in or upon any street
or avenue of the city, or engage in or upon any street or avenue of the city in
any sport or act or pastime having a tendency to frighten horses or damage any
property upon or along said streets or avenues. (1977 Code § 10.04.090; amd.
2000 Code)
8-4-8: OBSTRUCTIONS DURING EXCAVATION:
   A.   Permit Required; Restrictions: Any builder, contractor, person, company
or corporation who shall desire to occupy or obstruct any part of any sidewalk,
street or avenue during the excavation for any building, or for the storage of
building materials for the construction, repair, or removal of any building
may, after having first procured a permit therefor from the city council,
occupy and obstruct for such purpose not more than one-third (1/3) of the width
of such street or avenue, including the sidewalk; and that portion of the
sidewalk, or street, so to be used, shall be only that portion directly in
front of the property to be improved, and no material shall be stored, placed
or piled upon the street or avenue, except such as is to be immediately used in
such improvement or construction.
   B.   Removal Of Rubbish: No rubbish removed from any excavation of a
building shall be allowed to be stored upon the street or avenue, but the same
shall be removed from day to day, and the permission hereby given shall
terminate with the completion of the intended improvement, and all obstructions
and materials shall be immediately removed therefrom. (1977 Code § 10.04.100;
amd. 2000 Code)
8-4-9: STANDS, BOOTHS ON STREETS:
No person, traveling merchant, hawker, peddler or any itinerant vendor of
goods, wares or merchandise, patent medicines, drugs, notions, or other
articles of commerce shall erect, build, keep or maintain in any manner
whatever a stand, place, booth or any arrangement or device whatever on Main
Street in the city, for the purpose of vending, selling, advertising, or
otherwise disposing of goods, wares or merchandise, patent medicines, drugs,
notions or other articles of commerce, nor for any commercial or amusement
purposes whatsoever without a special permit therefor from the mayor; provided,
however, that when a license is issued or granted to any of the persons for any
of the businesses or occupations as above specified in this section, they may
occupy any of the streets or avenues intersecting and crossing said Main Street
and far enough removed from the corner of said streets and avenues so as not to
interfere with the free passing to and from of vehicles and pedestrians on said
Main Street and the street crossings thereof. (1977 Code § 10.04.110; amd. 2000
Code)
8-4-10: OWNER RESPONSIBILITY:
The owner or person in control of any building, fence, porch, steps, building
materials, gravel and sand for building purposes, or for any purpose whatever,
or any other obstructions, encumbrances and encroachments of every kind and
character now standing and being, or which may hereafter be standing, built,
erected or placed in or upon any street, avenue, alley, or other public grounds
within the city, or which may be left standing upon any new street, avenue,
alley, or other public grounds that has been, or may hereafter be opened, shall
remove the same within such reasonable time not exceeding thirty (30) days nor
less than five (5) days, as he shall be required so to do by a written notice
signed and served by a police officer. (1977 Code § 10.04.050; amd. 2000 Code;
Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009)
8-4-11: NEGLECTING TO REMOVE OBSTRUCTIONS:
   A.   Nuisance Declared: Whenever the owner or person in control of any
building, fence, porch, steps, building materials, gravel and sand to be used
for building purposes, or for any purpose whatever, or other obstructions,
encumbrances and encroachments of every kind and character now standing and
being, or which may hereafter be standing, built, erected or placed in or upon
any street, avenue, alley, or public grounds in the city as specified in this
chapter, shall refuse or neglect to remove the same, after notice given as
prescribed in section
 8-4-10 of this chapter or, if the owner or person in control of the same
cannot be found for the purpose of such notice, the same shall be deemed a
nuisance. (1977 Code § 10.04.060; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Removal By City; Cost Assessed To Owner: It shall be lawful for a
police officer and it is hereby made his duty to cause the same to be removed
or taken down, in his discretion, and the expense thereof shall be recoverable
from the owner. (1977 Code § 10.04.060; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-
2009)
8-4-12: PENALTY:
Any person who shall violate the provisions of this chapter shall be subject to
penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code. (2000 Code)
CHAPTER 5
NORTHWESTERN ENERGY CORPORATION
SECTION:
8-5-1: Franchise Granted; Term
8-5-2: Extend Gas Mains
8-5-3: Provide Sufficient Quantity Of Gas
8-5-4: Disturbing System
8-5-5: Work Done In Workmanlike Manner
8-5-6: Hold Harmless Agreement
8-5-7: Right To Make Assignments
8-5-8: Exclusive Rights Or Privileges
8-5-9: City Authority
8-5-10: Failure To Comply
8-5-1: FRANCHISE GRANTED; TERM:
There is hereby granted to the Montana Power Company, a corporation, its
successors and assigns, the right, privilege and franchise for the full period
of fifty (50) years from October 14, 1980, and thereafter until and unless
otherwise provided by ordinance to construct, equip, lay, maintain and operate
in, under, upon, over and across the streets, avenues, alleys, highways,
bridges, easements and other public places in the city, as now or hereafter
constituted, mains, pipes, conduits, manholes, reducing and regulating stations
and all other appurtenances and accessories for the purpose of transporting,
conveying, distributing, supplying and selling natural gas or artificial gas,
or a mixture of natural and artificial gas for light, heat, power and other
purposes, at rates fixed and allowed by the public service commission of
Montana. NorthWestern Energy Corporation (hereinafter called the "grantee") is
a successor in interest to Montana Power Company. Grantee agrees to file with
the city clerk the schedule of rates thus fixed and allowed. (Ord. 355-15, 2-
24-2015)
8-5-2: EXTEND GAS MAINS:
The grantee shall extend its gas mains and pipes to such parties of the city as
the consumption of gas shall justify. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-3: PROVIDE SUFFICIENT QUANTITY OF GAS:
The grantee, at all times during the existence of this franchise, shall use its
best efforts to obtain and supply a continuous, sufficient and adequate
quantity of gas for use by the city and its inhabitants; provided, however,
that the grantee shall in nowise be liable to the city or to its inhabitants
because of the interruption or discontinuance of the supply of gas by causes
beyond the reasonable control of the grantee. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-4: DISTURBING SYSTEM:
The grantee shall not discontinue the distribution of gas through its
distributing system, or any portion thereof, for an unreasonable length of time
for the purpose of making repairs and extensions, but the grantee shall not be
liable to the city or to any consumers for damages caused by such temporary
discontinuance or interruption of the delivery of gas, provided that such
repairs and extensions are made with reasonable diligence. (Ord. 195, 8-11-
1980)
8-5-5: WORK DONE IN WORKMANLIKE MANNER:
   A.   Performance In Workmanlike Manner: All work done in, under, upon, over
and across the present and future streets, avenues, alleys, highways, bridges,
easements and other public places in the city by the grantee for the purpose of
carrying out the provisions of this franchise shall be done and performed in a
good and workmanlike manner.
   B.   Restoration Of Street: When any street, alley, or other public place in
the city is excavated or damaged by the grantee by reason of such work, the
grantee shall restore such street, alley or public place to its former
condition as early as practicable.
   C.   Grade Or Plan Change: If at any time a change in the grade or plan of
any street, alley or public place shall be made by order of the proper city
officials, the grantee shall, without expense to the city, make such changes in
the location of its pipes and facilities as the change of the grade or plan of
the street, alley or public place makes necessary, which said changes shall be
made as soon as possible after the grantee shall have received notice from the
proper city official having the same in charge. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-6: HOLD HARMLESS AGREEMENT:
The grantee shall hold the City harmless from all costs and damages which shall
or may accrue to the City by reason of the neglect, default or misconduct of
the grantee in connection with the exercise of its rights hereunder. (Ord. 195,
8-11-1980)
8-5-7: RIGHT TO MAKE ASSIGNMENTS:
The grantee is hereby given the right and authority to make assignments of this
right, privilege or franchise, and its rights hereunder, all assignees to be
bound to the same extent as the original grantee. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-8: EXCLUSIVE RIGHTS OR PRIVILEGES:
Nothing in this Chapter contained shall be held or construed to grant any
exclusive rights or privileges, but the City reserves to itself the right at
any time to make such other grants or extend such other privileges to any other
person, company or corporation for the use of its streets, alleys or other
public places, or any thereof, for the purposes in this Chapter expressed, or
for any other valid purpose as the City Council may by ordinance from time to
time determine. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-9: CITY AUTHORITY:
The City shall pass all ordinances necessary or suitable to protect the
property and rights of the grantee and to enable the grantee to enforce any of
its reasonable rules and regulations for the management, operation and control
of the service hereunder, and shall pass any reasonable ordinance that may be
necessary or suitable in order fully to confirm to the grantee the rights
herein or hereby granted or intended so to be. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
8-5-10: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
Failure on the part of the grantee to comply in any substantial respect with
any of the provisions of this franchise shall be grounds for a forfeiture
thereof; but no such forfeiture shall take effect if the reasonableness or the
propriety thereof is protested by the grantee until and unless a court of
competent jurisdiction (with right of appeal in either party) shall have found
that the grantee has failed to comply in a substantial respect with any of the
provisions of this franchise, and grantee shall have six (6) months after the
final determination of said question to make good the default before a
forfeiture shall result, with the right in the City Council, at its discretion,
to grant such additional time to the grantee for compliance, as necessities in
the case may require. (Ord. 195, 8-11-1980)
CHAPTER 6
PARKS
SECTION:
8-6-1: Purpose
8-6-2: Definitions
8-6-3: Park Property; Regulations Authorized
8-6-4: Hours Of Operation Of Parks
8-6-5: Park Prohibitions
8-6-6: Park And Recreational Facility Reservations
8-6-7: Park And Recreational Facility Reservation Permits; Application Process
8-6-8: Fees
8-6-9: Enforcement
8-6-10: Revocation Of Permit
8-6-11: Penalty
8-6-1: PURPOSE:
The provisions of this section shall apply to all park lands in the city,
whether dedicated, deeded, or otherwise acquired for park purposes, and to all
facilities designated for city recreational purposes. Each application for use
of a park or recreational facility shall be reviewed on a case-by-case basis.
This section seeks to impose reasonable time, place and conduct controls in an
appropriate and limited manner upon events and facility uses for which
reservations are required. This section shall be administered in a manner that
seeks to allow for expression, assembly, and the exercise of religious rights
in accordance with applicable constitutional and statutory limits and controls.
(Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018)
8-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
 
FIREWORKS:             The meaning stated in
                       6-2-3.
                       A park, playground, recreation facility, pond areas, or
PARK:                  any other area in the city, developed or undeveloped,
                       owned or used by the city, and devoted to active or
                       passive recreation.
                       Any meeting, march, demonstration, picket line, race/
                       marathon, rally, or gathering of more than 75 persons
                       for a common purpose as a result of prior planning that
PUBLIC ASSEMBLY:       affects or may reasonably be expected to affect the
                       normal flow or regulation of pedestrian or vehicular
                       traffic within a park or recreational facility, or
                       occupies any park or recreational facility in a place
                       open to the general public.
RECREATIONAL FACILITY: A building, structure, place or other location within a
                       park or under the management of the city.
                       Any group or organization that is given use of a park
USER GROUP:            for an extended period of time through a park
                       reservation.(Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-
                       2018, 8-28-2018)
 
8-6-3: PARK PROPERTY; REGULATIONS AUTHORIZED:
The City Council shall have the right to adopt reasonable regulations governing
the use of the public parks in the city, and no person shall violate any of
such regulations. The Council appoints the Mayor, or his/her designee, to
administer the general provisions of this section. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018;
amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-4: HOURS OF OPERATION OF PARKS:
   A.   Hours: All parks shall be open to the public every day of the year
subject to the exceptions established herein. Anyone under the age of eighteen
(18) must adhere to the laws defined in Title
6-3-7 &
6-3-8.
   B.   General Closure: Any section or part of any park may be closed to the
public by the Mayor. Notice of closing shall be posted in a conspicuous manner.
   C.   Night Closure: No person without written permission of the Mayor shall
be physically present within the boundaries of any park between the hours of
10:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-
2018)
8-6-5: PARK PROHIBITIONS:
   A.   It is unlawful for any person in a park or adjacent to a recreational
facility to:
      1.   Mark, deface, disfigure, injure, tamper with or displace or remove
any buildings, bridges, tables, benches, grills, railings, paving or paving
material, water lines, equipment, signs, drinking fountains, swimming or wading
pools or other park or recreational facility property, improvements or
appurtenances whatsoever, real or personal;
      2.   Fail to cooperate in maintaining restrooms and washrooms in a neat
and sanitary condition.
      3.   Dump dirt, grass and tree clippings or dig, remove, plant or deposit
any soil, rock, sand, stones, trees, shrubs or plants or other wood or
materials, or make any excavation by tool, equipment or other means or agency
except as authorized by the Mayor.
      4.   Construct or erect any building or structure of whatever kind,
whether permanent or temporary, or run or string any public utility into, upon
or across park or recreational facility property, except on special written
permit issued hereunder.
      5.   Damage, cut, carve, mark, transplant or remove any plant, or injure
the bark, dig in or otherwise disturb grass areas, or in any other way injure
the natural beauty or usefulness of any area.
      6.   Attach any rope, cable, structure, device or other contrivance to
any tree, fence, railing, bridge, bench, building or other structure unless
otherwise posted. This prohibition does not include locking bicycles to the
foregoing mentioned structures as long as no damage is done to the structure
and so long as the bicycle does not interfere with the use and enjoyment of the
park by others.
      7.   Litter or fail to refuse to deposit litter in provided garbage
receptacles. Where receptacles are not provided, all such rubbish or waste
shall be carried away from the park by the person responsible for its presence
and properly disposed of elsewhere.
      8.   Break glass objects and then fail to remove broken glass and safely
dispose of the broken glass in such fashion so as not to cause injury to
persons or property.
      9.   Cause or permit any domestic animal to run loose, or fail to keep
such animal under restraint as per Title 6-4C, in any park or other open space
area designated by the City Council as an area requiring restraint as per Title
6-4A. The above provision shall not apply to service animals authorized under
the Americans with Disabilities Act. Further, every owner or person having
custody of said dog or other animal shall remove and properly dispose of the
animal's solid waste (fecal material).
      10.   Pasture or pen any animal, domesticated or wild.
      11.   Hunt, molest, harm, frighten, kill, trap, pursue, chase, tease,
shoot or throw missiles at any animal, nor remove from the park or have in his
possession any animal, or the eggs or nest, or young of any animal. An
exception to the foregoing is made in that snakes known to be poisonous may be
killed on sight. An exception is further made to fishing where allowed by the
state department of fish, wildlife and parks. This regulation does not apply to
officers of state or local government duly acting within the course and scope
of their duties.
      12.   Start a fire except in facilities installed and provided for such
purpose, or to fail to completely extinguish a fire upon leaving the park.
      13.   Camp overnight as per Titles
5-8-2 and
7-2-5-E.
      14.   Display, offer to sell, or sell any article or service without
first obtaining permission by the City Council pursuant to this chapter,
exception of the Three Forks Chamber of Commerce's Farmer's Market.
      15.   Operate a skateboard, roller skate, inline skate, ride a bike or
similar recreational device with wheels on any tennis court, basketball court,
or in any drained swimming pool.
      16.   Operate a skateboard, rollerskate, inline skate, or ride a bike or
similar recreational device with wheels on or against any city-owned table,
bench, structure, tennis court, bike rack, parking stop, retaining wall,
fountain, statue, railing, stage, or other improvement which may suffer damage
by such use.
      17.   Operate a skateboard, rollerskate, inline skate, or ride a bike or
similar recreational device with wheels on or in any pavilion.
      18.   Practice golf with real golf balls in any park.
      19.   Drive, operate or park any vehicle or trailer on park lands or
trails, except as authorized by the Mayor.
   B.   The Mayor may create additional prohibitions which may be applicable to
one or more parks or recreation facilities. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd.
Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-6: PARK AND RECREATIONAL FACILITY RESERVATIONS:
The following standards apply to the use, including the reserved use, of all
parks and recreational facilities:
   A.   Reservation Priority: Unless reserved according to the park reservation
procedure, established herein, the use of the park or portion thereof by the
public shall be on a first-come, first-served basis.
   B.   Scope: Only parks and recreational facilities designated within the
City of Three Forks' fee schedule resolution may be reserved for exclusive use.
   C.   Tents, canopies, inflatable structures: Approval must be granted by the
Mayor for the use of, and prior to the assembly of, any tents, canopies, shade
structures, inflatable toys, etc., within a park.
   D.   Public address or sound systems: Public address and/or sound systems
may be used within parks with the approval of the Mayor. The sound system
cannot be used for more than three consecutive hours in any park. The use of
amplified sound shall be limited to the hours between 12:00 p.m. (noon) and 9:
00 p.m.
   E.   Marking the grounds: Only water-based turf paint shall be used on any
turf. Only chalk shall be used on impervious surfaces such as sidewalks and
asphalt.
   F.   Park user group agreements: The Mayor may enter into agreements with
various park user groups, with the fee for such agreements as established by
the City Council.
      1.   Admission fees may be charged for events held in conjunction with a
park user group agreement if approved by the Mayor and listed in the agreement.
      2.   Articles, food, beverages or service may be sold for events held in
conjunction with a park user group agreement, if so noted in the agreement.
   G.   Parking: Parking spaces at a park or recreational facility are not
reserved with a park reservation permit, and all parking is on a first-come,
first-served basis. Issuance of park reservation permit does not provide
guarantee of parking to the permittee or invitees.
   H.   Portable toilet facilities: The Mayor may require a person holding a
reservation permit to provide portable toilet facilities. The Mayor shall
determine how many such facilities are needed and the timeframe in which they
must be present. If the facilities are not removed within the timeframe
established, the city may remove them and all costs associated with removal
shall be charged to the applicant.
   I.   Litter removal: A person holding a reservation permit shall pick up and
properly dispose of all types of litter within the recreational facility,
buildings and/or grounds.
   J.   Additional rules: The Mayor and/or Council may establish additional
rules governing the use of a park or recreational facility by the public or a
person holding a reserved use permit. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-
2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-7: PARK AND RECREATIONAL FACILITY RESERVATION PERMITS; APPLICATION PROCESS:
   A.   A person seeking a park or recreational facility reservation permit
shall file an application with the City Clerk on forms provided by the City and
shall include all information the City deems relevant to the requested event.
Applicants must be at least 18 years of age.
   B.   An application for a reservation permit shall be filed with the City no
less than five (5) working days prior to the event.
      1.   Exception: The City will allow reservations with fewer than five (5)
working days notice if the event anticipates a small number of participants and
would have minimal impact to the neighboring community and minimal disturbance
of other public to use the rest of the park.
   C.   Standards of issuance of reservation permit:
      1.   The Mayor shall issue a permit, subject to any conditions deemed
necessary and reasonable, as provided for herein when, from consideration of
the application and such other information as may otherwise be obtained, the
Mayor finds:
         a.   The application is complete and sets forth accurately and in
sufficient detail the information required for consideration;
         b.   The conduct of the event will not unduly inconvenience either the
public in using adjacent public areas normally open for general public use or
the city in the conduct of governmental operations;
         c.   The possibility of the event causing any noise which unreasonably
disturbs, injures, or endangers the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of
reasonable persons of ordinary sensitivity.
      2.   The conduct of the event will not require law enforcement's presence
to properly police the event as to prevent normal protection of the city;
      3.   The conduct of the event is not reasonably likely to cause injury to
persons or property;
      4.   Adequate sanitation and other required health facilities (park
latrines or "port-a-potties") are or will be made available;
      5.   There is sufficient parking near the site of the event, or other
arrangements made for transportation, to accommodate the number of vehicles
reasonably expected;
      6.   Such event is not for the primary purpose of advertising any
product, goods, or event that is primarily for private profit.
      7.   A reservation for public assembly permit for the same time and
general location is already granted or has been received and will be granted;
      8.   The conduct of a past event for the same purpose or by the same
organizer and/or organization.
      9.   The permittee obtain insurance which names the City of Three Forks
as an additional insured without limitation in the amounts set by the City.
   D.   An event may be limited as to the number of participants in the
interest of adequacy of facilities.
   E.   Unless otherwise agreed by the applicant, the Mayor shall act on an
application within 1 business day after determining that the application is
complete. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-8: FEES:
A nonrefundable fee shall be paid to cover administrative costs of processing
permits. The fee under this article shall be set by City Council resolution.
(Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-9: ENFORCEMENT:
This chapter may be enforced by the Mayor, or his/her designee, law
enforcement, or the fire chief. In addition this article may be enforced by
injunction, restraining order, declaratory relief, or such other order as may
be imposed by a court with appropriate jurisdiction. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018;
amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-10: REVOCATION OF PERMIT:
The Mayor, or his/her designee, law enforcement, or the fire chief shall each
have independent authority to instantly revoke or suspend any permit issued
under this article:
   A.   Upon a violation of the conditions imposed in the permit;
   B.   Upon violation of this article or any other provision of law;
   C.   When a public emergency arises where the municipal resources required
for that emergency are so great that deployment of municipal personnel,
equipment or services required for the permit would have an immediate and
adverse effect upon the welfare and safety of persons or property.
   D.   Such revocation shall take effect immediately, and the Mayor, law
enforcement, or fire chief shall promptly notify the permittee of revocation.
After revocation, the permittee may not conduct the event, or if the event has
commenced, shall immediately cause the event to be terminated in a safe, proper
manner.  (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
8-6-11: PENALTY:
Any person violating the provisions of this chapter will be deemed guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be subject to penalty as
provided in Section
1-4-1  of this code. (Ord. 382-2018, 9-11-2018; amd. Ord. 382-2018, 8-28-2018)
TITLE 9
WATER AND SEWER
CHAPTER 1
DELINQUENT UTILITY BILLS 1
SECTION:
9-1-1: Interest
9-1-2: Service Charge
9-1-3: Tenants Receiving Disconnect Notice
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  9-2-3, rule 4, of this title.
9-1-1: INTEREST:
The city council does hereby assess an interest rate of one and one-half
percent (11/2%) a month on all utility bills that remain unpaid on the twenty
first day of each month. Payment is due the twentieth day of each month and the
interest shall commence on the first day after payment is due. (Ord. 295-06-07,
10-10-2006)
9-1-2: SERVICE CHARGE:
A service charge of ten dollars ($10.00) will be assessed on every utility bill
not paid by the twentieth day of each month to recover for the city the cost of
personnel and materials in notifying utility customers of their delinquent
obligations. (Ord. 294-06-07, 10-10-2006)
9-1-3: TENANTS RECEIVING DISCONNECT NOTICE:
   A.   Tenants who receive a disconnect notice two (2) times within their
residency on the landowner's property will no longer have the water and/or
sewer account in their own name; the account will be placed in the landowner's
name and become the responsibility of the landowner.
   B.   Any utility customer that receives a disconnect notice will be required
to pay the account balance in full by the disconnect date or the water and/or
sewer service will be turned off. (Ord. 300-07-08, 8-11-2008)
CHAPTER 2
WATER SYSTEM REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-2-1: City Clerk, Duties
9-2-2: Water/Wastewater Operator

9-2-9: Connection With City Water System Required

9-2-11: Penalties
