9-2-13: Consent To Annexation For Continued Service
9-2-1: CITY CLERK, DUTIES:
The city clerk shall be the custodian of all books, records and papers
pertaining to the water system and shall keep a correct account of all receipts
and disbursements with reference thereto, and shall issue all bills for water
rents and materials furnished to commercial relations with consumers, and make
all reports required by law. All receipts from the operation of the water
system shall be kept in a separate fund to be known as the water fund 1 . (1977
Code § 2.34.010; amd. 2000 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 3, chapter 3 of this code.
9-2-2: WATER/WASTEWATER OPERATOR:
   A.   Appointment; Salary; Term: The mayor shall at the first regular meeting
of the city council each fiscal year, or as soon thereafter as possible,
appoint, subject to the confirmation of the council, a water/wastewater
operator. The council shall fix his salary or compensation, and he shall
perform all the duties prescribed and defined as herein provided. He shall
serve until removed by the council, or until his successor is appointed and
qualified. (1977 Code § 2.34.020; amd. 2000 Code)
   B.   Duties And Responsibilities:
      1.   Management Of Waterworks Plant: The water/wastewater operator shall
be the general executive officer of the waterworks plant and shall have
immediate control and management of all things pertaining to said plant,
subject to the approval and confirmation of the council. (1977 Code § 2.34.030;
amd. 2000 Code)
      2.   Charge Of Employees: The water/wastewater operator shall have charge
of all employees and property pertaining to the system. He shall give written
orders for all supplies and materials, furnishing a copy of each to the city
clerk for record. He shall have charge of all contracts and shall see that they
are faithfully executed, and shall have charge of the erection, alteration, and
repair of all buildings, engines, pumps, fixtures, wells, reservoirs and
grounds. He shall determine the location and size of all water mains, service
connections, valves, hydrants and specials.
      3.   Records: He shall furnish promptly to the city clerk a report of all
physical changes in items which are a matter of record in said clerk's office.
He shall submit all bills, payrolls and accounts to the council for approval.
      4.   Tapping Mains: Upon notification of the city clerk of the issuance
of a permit to a consumer for service connection, the water/wastewater operator
shall furnish to the consumer any material specified by the city clerk and
shall tap the main and inspect the service installation.
      5.   Reports: The water/wastewater operator shall furnish to the mayor or
city council any regular or specific reports concerning his work upon demand of
the council.
      6.   Pump Record: The water/wastewater operator shall maintain a daily
pump record of each pump, the pressure maintained and the number of gallons
pumped, submitting regularly, to the city clerk such of this information as may
be required by the clerk.
      7.   Gates And Hydrants: The water/wastewater operator shall see that all
gates and hydrants are restored to their proper condition after use by the fire
department, attending promptly to any necessary repairs. It shall be his duty
also to test and flush the fire hydrants of the city whenever such testing and
flushing seems essential to service.
      8.   Inspection: Whenever in the judgment of the water/wastewater
operator, as he deems it necessary, he may cause an inspection of the pipes and
water fixtures of any consumer, and the refusal of any consumer to permit such
inspection at a reasonable time shall be sufficient cause for refusing service.
The water/wastewater operator shall be vigilant to detect and eliminate all
abuses, whether from waste or improper use of water.
      9.   Meters: The water/wastewater operator shall cause all meters to be
read and inspected monthly and shall furnish to the city clerk a copy of these
readings together with a record of all changes in installations. It shall be
the duty of the water/wastewater operator to cause the prompt repair of all
meters suspected of inaccurate measurement and he shall report to the city
clerk all items used in the repair of meters and the amounts to be charged the
consumer for these items.
      10.   Service Control: The water/wastewater operator shall cause
consumer's services to be turned on or off promptly at the request of the city
clerk, giving a report of the work when done and shall not at any time except
in case of emergency, open or close any consumer's service line without the
knowledge and consent of the clerk. (1977 Code § 2.34.040; amd. 2000 Code)
9-2-3: WATER SYSTEM RULES:
In the interest of control and protection of the water system, the following
rules shall be considered a part of the contract with every person who accepts
water service as supplied by the City, and all persons accepting said service
shall be bound by these rules:
   Rule 1. Applications; Payment of Fee: Applications for new connections to
the mains or alterations in old connections must be made at the City Clerk’s
office on the printed form furnished for that purpose. The application must be
made by the owner or agent for the property to be served and must be
accompanied by the connection fee before connection will be authorized. This
fee shall be established by the City Council and include the cost of certain
standardized items of material that will be furnished to the applicant for use
in the service line and connection. The use of the furnished items is
mandatory.
   Rule 2. Additional Service; Permit For Extensions: Should the owner of the
property or his agent desire additional service or desire to apply water for a
purpose not intended in the original application, a permit must be obtained
before extensions are made.
   Rule 3. Termination Of Service By Consumer: Upon payment of service charges
to date of notice and presentation of written notice to the city clerk,
consumers may at any time terminate service. Water rentals will be charged
until such notice is filed. No charge will be made for turning water off or on
when the account is not in arrears but no remission of the minimum charge will
be made for less than one calendar month.
   Rule 4. Consumer Payments: Service charges must be paid monthly. Accounts
not paid by the twentieth of the month following notification of the consumer
are presumed to have been received by the person for whom they were intended.
Accounts which have been terminated because of delinquency in payment must be
paid in full together with a service charge of forty dollars ($40.00) before
service will be restored. All persons not in the employ of the city water
department are forbidden to open, close or in any manner change or disturb the
curb valve or any consumer’s service line.
   Rule 5. Location of Service Pipes: No permits shall be issued for service
connections when said services are to run across adjacent property or through
buildings on the same property. Service pipes must be laid at least six-and-
one-half feet (6.5') below the surface and not in the same trench with the
sewer pipes. Service pipes may enter the building at any point designated by
the owner of the property or his agent and all risk due to freezing of such
pipes and meters shall be assumed by the said property owner.
   Rule 6. Connected Premises: Two (2) or more premises of different ownership
shall not be supplied by the same connection (see Rule 1 of this Section)
unless the services are so installed that each is controlled by a separate curb
valve. In all cases, the owner of the property served shall be responsible for
all water used either by himself or any others to whom the water is accessible.
   Rule 7. Stop And Waste: Immediately ahead of every meter, a stop and waste
valve must be installed and in service lines entering basement, this valve
should be located immediately beyond the point of entry. These valves must be
provided with handles or wrenches for their operation and when not supplied by
the City, shall be of a form and quality specified by the Water/Wastewater
Operator. It shall be the duty of owners and occupants to familiarize
themselves with the uses and purposes of these valves and to report any fault
in their operation. No responsibility for damage will be assumed by the City
through failure of the owner or occupant of the premises to use the stop and
waste valve in stopping leaks or draining pipes and meters to prevent freezing.
   Rule 8. Ball Valves: Immediately ahead of every meter a ball valve must be
installed. These valves must be provided with handles for their operation and
when not supplied by the City, shall be of a form and quality specified by the
Water Superintendent. It shall be the duty of owners and occupants to
familiarize themselves with the uses and purposes of these valves and to report
any fault in their operation. No responsibility for damage will be assumed by
the City through failure of the owner or occupant of the premises to use the
ball valve in stopping leaks or draining pipes and meters to prevent freezing.
   Rule 9. Private Hydrants: No private hydrants shall be located within the
street lines or in any place easy of access to the public unless the same is
metered and then only by special permit.
   Rule 10. Responsibility For Service Pipes And Fixtures: The City will not be
responsible for service pipes and fixtures. Owners, at their own expense, must
keep service pipes and fixtures from the mains in good working order and
properly protected from frost and other dangers. No claim shall be made against
the City on account of failure of any service pipe or fixture or for the
accidental failure in the supply of water. No reductions from the regular rates
will be made for any time that service pipes or fixtures are out of commission
due to frost.
   Rule 11. Special Permit; Large Quantities Of Water: A special permit must be
obtained from the Water/Wastewater Operator before water meters or other
service requiring larger quantities of water are installed.
   Rule 12. Hose For Sprinkling: Hose used for sprinkling purposes must not be
more than three-fourths inch (3/4") inside diameter and the inside diameter of
the orifice or the nozzle of the same must not be more than one-half inch (½")
in diameter.
   Rule 13. Unnecessary Use Of Water: Consumers shall prevent the unnecessary
waste of water in lawn or garden sprinkling, washing of vehicles or other
similar uses of hose, and shall keep all water outlets closed when not in
actual use. Hydrants, basins, urinals, water closets, bathtubs or any other
openings must not be left running to prevent water freezing in pipes, or for
any other unnecessary waste, and when consumers persist in a wasteful use of
water, the City reserves the right to cut off the supply, and repeated
violation of this rule will subject the offender to prosecution as hereinafter
provided.
   Rule 14. Alarm Of Fire: During alarms of fire the use of hose, yard
fountains and all other outlets where a constant flow of water is maintained is
forbidden. This rule will be strictly enforced and will subject offenders to
prosecution.
   Rule 15. Water For Building Purposes: Contractors, builders or others
desiring water for building purposes must make application to the Water/
Wastewater Operator, who will issue a permit therefor, and all consumers are
warned not to allow them to use their fixtures. Water will not be turned on in
any new building until all water used in construction thereof has been paid
for. Owners are recommended to require contractors to show a receipt in full
for water used for building purposes before making final settlement, as the
property is held for such rental.
   Rule 16. Authorized Employees: No person other than authorized employee of
the Water Department shall make any tap or connection with any main or mains or
with any distributing pipe of the water system.
   Rule 17. Accidents From Boilers And Pressure: The City will not be
responsible for accidents resulting from insecure boilers or for variation of
water pressure, or the ram from water in the mains, or collapse from any cause
whatever.
   Rule 18. Shutting Off Of Water In Mains: The City reserves the right at any
time to shut the water off in the mains for the purpose of making repairs or
extensions or for any other needful purpose and consumers will be so notified,
but no claim shall be made against the City on account of the breakage of any
service pipe or service cock or for any other damage that may result from
shutting off water for necessary repairs, laying or relaying mains, hydrants or
other connections.
   Rule 19. Meters; Regulations and Charges: Meters will be placed on all
services as directed by the Water/Wastewater Operator. Each metered consumer is
subject to the minimum charge for such class of service as he receives. In
Residential Zoning Districts, and in all mobile home parks, multi-family
structures which have one meter shall be subject to the minimum water charge
for each residential unit, regardless of meter status. Rates for additional
water are shown in Section
9-2-6 of this Chapter. In all cases where a meter is installed, the consumer
must furnish proper protection from frost or other damage, and the meter must
be located where it is easily accessible for reading purposes and repairs.
Where necessary for protection, a standard form of meter box will be required
by the Water Department. The actual cost of the same shall be paid by the
consumer. After such receptacle is placed, the Water Department will furnish
and connect the meter and maintain the same in good condition under ordinary
wear and tear. When a meter is installed at the request of a consumer, its
installation shall be permanent unless the consumer elects to have same removed
and pays all expenses incident to the installation and removal of same or
discontinues service entirely. Service on a meter for a shorter period than six
(6) months will be considered temporary and in such cases, the consumer will be
required to reimburse the Water Department for the actual cost of the labor in
connection with the installation and removal of the meter.
   Rule 20. Replacing And Testing: The Water Department may replace any meter
at such time as it may see fit and shall be the judge of the size and make of
any meter installed. In case of a dispute as to the accuracy of a meter, the
customer, upon depositing the estimated cost of making a test, may demand that
the meter be removed and tested as to accuracy in his presence. In case the
meter is found to be registering correctly or in favor of the consumer, the
cost of such testing and replacing of the meter shall be borne by the consumer.
In case the meter is found to be registering incorrectly and against the
consumer, the amount deposited by the consumer will be refunded and a
reasonable adjustment made for overcharges, for a period not exceeding sixty
(60) days previous to the demand of the consumer for a test to be made. In case
a meter is found stopped for any reason, so that it is not correctly recording
the consumption of water, the Water Department may average the amount due for
the current month, using the past two (2) months as a basis of average.
   Rule 21. Interference With Meters: Water consumers are not permitted to
interfere in any way with the meter after it has been set in place. In case the
meter seal is broken or the working parts of the meter have been tampered with
or the meter damaged, the Water Department may render a bill for the current
month, based on the average of the past two (2) months, together with the full
cost of such damages as have been done to the meter, and may refuse to furnish
water until the account is paid in full.
   Rule 22. Placing of Meters: Where practicable, meters may be placed in a
location with easy access for reading and maintenance. In Residential Zoning
Districts all new multifamily residential structures shall have a meter
installed on each unit. The meter must be placed so as to be of easy access to
the officers of the Water Department, and must be carefully protected from
freezing and from other dangers. Before setting any meter, the pipes must be
blown out, and the meter must be set without the use of red lead or any other
substance for packing in the fitting. The meter must be set level and made
firm, suitable supports being provided when necessary. All new water hookups
shall have a double check-valve backflow prevention assembly installed
downstream of the water meter.
   Rule 23. Meters Outside of Buildings: When meters must be located on the
outside of buildings, they need to be placed in an approved meter pit or
structure approved by the Water/Wastewater Operator. The approved meter pit or
structure shall have a cover with easy access.
   Rule 24. Check Valves On Meters: In all cases, if meters are placed on pipes
connected to boilers or other hot-water apparatus, a check valve must be placed
between said meter and such boiler, or other hot-water apparatus, to protect
the meter from back pressure of steam or hot water.
   Rule 25. Rules Regulating Plumbing: Rules regulating plumbing work upon any
of the water mains, connections or appliances in any way pertaining to the
water system of the City are set forth in Section
9-2-4 of this Chapter. (1977 Code § 2.34.050; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 293-06-07,
10-10-2006; Ord. 390-2021, 8-10-2021; Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-2022)
9-2-4: RULES REGULATING PLUMBING:
The following rules shall be strictly adhered to by all persons performing any
plumbing work in and upon any of the mains, connections or appliances
appertaining to the waterworks system of Three Forks.
   Rule 1. Refilling Of Trenches: All trenches shall be refilled in a careful
and workmanlike manner, tamped (thoroughly wet down when weather conditions
will permit) so as to replace as nearly as possible all material excavated and
leave the surface of the street in as good condition as before commencing work.
Special care shall be observed with trenches within the street lines and all
surplus material must be removed when work is completed, and any refilling
necessary to maintain the highway in as good condition as before commencing
work for a period of three (3) months shall be done by the person causing the
excavation.
   Rule 2. Tapping Done By Water Department: No person other than an authorized
employee of the Water Department, acting under the orders of the Water/
Wastewater Operator, shall tap or make any perforation or opening of any kind
in any water main.
   Rule 3. Materials Supplied by Water Department: The Water Department
recommends that the owner and/or contractor supply all the materials for
installation according to City standards. If necessary, the Water Department
can supply the materials. There will be an additional charge for all materials
supplied. All connections will be performed by City Personnel, or authorized
agent, of the Water Department to the City main.
   Rule 4. Depth of Service Pipes: All service pipes must be laid at least six
and one-half (6 ½') feet below the surface of the ground. The general rules and
regulations respecting the kind and quality of material to be used and the
manner and the location of setting shut-off and curb boxes shall govern.
   Rule 5. Barricades And Danger Signals: Excavations within the street lines
shall be made in such manner as to impede traffic as little as possible, and
the Water/Wastewater Operator may determine and limit the time such excavations
may remain open and if unnecessarily delayed, he may direct that the force be
increased to such an extent as will hasten the work to completion. Red light
must be maintained upon all unfinished work from sundown to sunrise, and
sufficient barricades must be in place at all times until the work is
completed.
   Rule 6. Alterations, Additions And Disconnections: No alteration, addition
or disconnection in or about any water pipes or fixtures shall be made without
written permission to do such work being granted by the Water/Wastewater
Operator.
   Rule 7. Written Report: Within twenty four (24) hours after completion of
any work in connection with the water supply of any consumer, either for new
work, extensions, additional fixtures or repairs, a written report shall be
completed by the person doing the work and returned to the Water/Wastewater
Operator upon blanks furnished for that purpose, covering all improvements made
under the permit therefor.
   Rule 8. Excavations: Excavations underneath the sidewalk or areaways shall
not be made until after the tap at the main has been made, in order that the
highway may not be obstructed any longer than is absolutely necessary.
   Rule 9. Time of Tapping: The Water Department will require forty-eight (48)
hours’ notice before tapping mains, and in no case will taps be made on
Saturdays, Sundays or holidays.
   Rule 10. Leaks Or Accidents: In case of leaks and other accidents to pipes
or fixtures, the water may be shut off to make necessary repairs, and a report
of the same shall be made and filed as provided in Rule 7 of this Section. In
all cases where repairs to pipes or fixtures are made on any premises, the
water shall be left turned on or off as it was before such repairs were made.
   Rule 11. Pipe Joints: Where iron pipes are to be joined together, either
brass soldering nipple or brass soldering union must be used. Wiped joints will
not be permitted on iron pipes or iron connections.
   Rule 12. Testing New Work: In no case after the completion and test of work,
if it be the first introduction of service pipe, shall the water be left turned
on at the premises, but the stopcock shall be immediately closed.
   Rule 13. Water/Wastewater Operator’s Control: The water/wastewater operator,
under the direction of the city council, shall have absolute control of the
entire waterworks system and all buildings and property pertaining to the
system.
   Rule 14. Extensions From One Street Number To Another: Service pipes shall
not be extended from one street number to another without special permission
therefor.
   Rule 15. Water And Sewer Pipes In Same Trench: Water pipes shall not be laid
in the same trench with the sewer pipes, but an entirely separate trench must
in all cases be provided for their accommodation.
   Rule 16. Separate Service Pipes: In piping buildings where various floors or
apartments are to be supplied from a separate service, the plans shall first be
submitted to the water/wastewater operator and approved by him.
   Rule 17. Ball valves: In all cases where water pipes enter a building, such
pipes must be supplied with a ball valve with handle or wrench fixed thereto as
provided in Rule 19 of this section.
   Rule 18. Setting Of Meters: The setting of meters will be governed by
section
9-2-3, rules 25, 26, and 27 of this chapter.
   Rule 19. Curb Box Lids: The opening of curb box lids by any other means than
a proper wrench is strictly forbidden and anyone violating this rule will be
held responsible for all damages occasioned thereby.
   Rule 20. Master Plumbers: Master plumbers will be held responsible for their
workmen and for each and every violation of any of the rules and regulations of
this chapter and shall be subject to the penalties prescribed herein.
   Rule 21. Inspection: The Water/Wastewater Operator may adopt such rules and
regulations as deemed necessary to provide and ensure proper inspection of the
work and no material shall be used until same has been approved. No pipe shall
be covered until such inspection and approval has been made. The Water/
Wastewater Operator must be given forty-eight (48) hours notice when work will
be ready for inspection, and when same has been inspected and approved. (1977
Code § 2.34.060; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-2022)
9-2-5: COUNCIL REVIEW AND CONTROL:
In all cases, wherein by these rules and regulations discretion is vested in
the water/wastewater operator, such discretion shall be subject to review and
control of the city council. (1977 Code § 2.34.070; amd. 2000 Code)
9-2-6: WATER RATES AND CHARGES:
   A.   Water Rates; Metered Water:
      1.   The rates, charges and rentals for the services and facilities
provided by the city water system shall be fixed and established by resolution
of the city council.
      2.   The monthly water use rate shall be fixed and established by
resolution of the city council.
   B.   Water Hookup Fees:
      1.   Hookup Fee: The fee for water hookups shall be the cost of all
materials, valves and parts and labor necessary to properly complete
construction of service. A fee for new water customers signing up for existing
services shall be fixed and established by resolution of the city council.
      2.   Request for Hookup: Any request for water hookup shall be made to
the City Clerk, in writing on the application form provided by the City, at
least forty-eight (48) hours prior to commencement of installation. Utility
hookup will not occur during weekends, evenings, holidays or other time when
city personnel are unavailable for inspection.
      3.   Authorized Installers: Only those contractors, persons, firms, and
corporations who are bonded by a surety, authorized to conduct business within
the City and State are authorized to install the utility service. (Ord. 334-13,
4-9-2013; amd. Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-2022)
9-2-7: FIRE HYDRANTS AND VALVES:
No person, other than an authorized employee of the water department, members
of the fire department (when in discharge of their duties), or other person in
authority, shall open, close, turn or interfere with any fire hydrant, valve,
or curb stop belonging to the water works system. (1977 Code § 2.34.080; amd.
Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-2022)
9-2-8: ENFORCEMENT; DUTIES OF LAW ENFORCEMENT:
   A.    It shall be the duty of law enforcement officers to give vigilant aid
to the water/wastewater operator in the enforcement of all rules and
regulations and to this end they shall report all violations thereof which may
come to their attention.
   B.    The law enforcement officers shall work with the City Attorney at the
direction of the Mayor on enforcement issues. (1977 Code § 2.34.090; amd. 2000
Code; Ord. 313-09-10, 11-10-2009; Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-2-9: CONNECTION WITH CITY WATER SYSTEM REQUIRED:
   A.   Requirement: All occupants, residents and owners of real property
located within the city which real property abuts or is adjacent to any water
transmission line of the city or any water line utilized by the city for
transmitting city water shall connect said real property and utilize the water
system as potable water for any structures located on said real property.
   B.   Existing Water Wells; Exception: Subsection A of this section shall not
apply to existing water well systems utilized by existing structures; however,
should the existing well fail or need substantial repair, then said water
system shall be attached to the city's water system.
   C.   Disconnection From Water System; Consent Required: It shall be unlawful
for any person to disconnect any water system from the present city water
system without the consent of the city. (Ord. 212, 8-10-1987)
   D.   Penalty: Any violation of this section shall be punishable by a fine as
provided for in section
 1-4-1 of this code per day for each day said section is violated and shall be
cause, under the zoning code 1 , for the issuance by the water/wastewater
operator of an order restricting or terminating the habitability of the
structure located on the described premises. (Ord. 212, 8-10-1987; amd. 2000
Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 11 of this code.
9-2-10: SAND POINT WELL CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Prohibition: It shall be illegal and unlawful for any owner or occupant
of any real estate lot within the city to install a sand point well or any
other device which utilizes subterranean water in such a manner that the sand
point well or water system will be connected at any point to the water system
of the city or the individual water system of any occupant of real estate
within the city.
   B.   Disconnection of System by City: In addition to the penalty herein, the
City may disconnect, at the curb stop, the individual water system from the
central water system of the City.
   C.   Penalty: A violation of this section shall be punishable by a fine as
provided for in section
1-4-1 of this code for each violation. Under the provisions of this section,
each twenty four (24) hour period in which the sand point well or other device
is connected to the water system shall constitute a separate violation. (Ord.
211, 8-10-1987; amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-2022)
9-2-11: PENALTIES:
Unless otherwise provided, any person, firm, corporation, architect, plumber or
contractor, or other person who shall be found guilty of violating any of the
rules and regulations of this chapter, or who shall fail or neglect to comply
with the provisions contained therein, shall, upon conviction thereof, be
subject to penalty as provided in section
1-4-1 of this code; provided, however, that when the offense is one which
relates to rentals, leakage or illegal use of water, the water/wastewater
operator may cause the supply to be shut off and the offender shall forfeit all
payments that may have been made for same. When the water has been turned off
for violation of this chapter, it shall not be turned on again until all
amounts due have been paid and a charge of forty dollars ($40.00) will be added
to cover the cost of turning the water off and on 1 . (1977 Code § 2.34.150;
amd. 2000 Code; Ord. 293-06-07, 10-10-2006)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  9-2-3, rule 4 of this chapter.
9-2-12: TEMPORARY SUSPENSION OF WATER AND UTILITY SERVICES:
   A.   Any request for the activation or turning on, or the suspension or
turning off of water services after four o’clock (4:00) P.M. or on weekends
shall not occur unless the fee, established via resolution by the City Council,
has been paid.
   B.   Any request for the activation or turning on of water at a location
where suspension of service has occurred due to nonpayment by the user shall
not occur unless the entire past due bill and a reconnection fee, established
via resolution by the City Council, has been paid. This reconnection fee is in
addition to the after four o’clock (4:00) P.M. or weekend fee.
   C.   City staff may, after appropriate investigation based upon need and
hardship, waive all or a portion of the fees assessed in this section with the
consent and approval of the Mayor.
   D.   If a customer or property owner desires to have their water service
turned off, either temporarily (“snowbird”) or permanently, they must sign and
submit this request on the forms prepared and approved by the City. Failure to
sign and submit such request will mean that the utility service will remain in
existence and the minimum monthly charge will be assessed.
   E.   Should a property owner or customer request water only service during
construction, such service will only be provided after execution and submission
to the city of Three Forks on forms approved by the city of such service
accompanied by the applicable fee, if any.
   F.   Only employees of the city of Three Forks are authorized to access,
turn on or turn off water. No exceptions.
   G.   The cost of any repairs of a faulty curb box valve are the sole
responsibility of the customer or property owner and shall be assessed on the
utility bill.
   H.   Absolutely no extensions or changes to these rules and regulations may
be granted except by a majority vote of the Three Forks city council at a duly
called council meeting. (Ord. 275-2003, 8-11-2003; amd. Ord. 393-2022, 5-24-
2022)
9-2-13: CONSENT TO ANNEXATION FOR CONTINUED SERVICE:
The city may, at any time, require a property owner's consent to annexation as
a condition of continued sewer and/or water service. When the city determines
to require such consent from a particular property owner, the city may notify
the property owner, in writing, that the city seeks such consent, and that if
such consent is not given, the city will require that the property owner
discontinue receiving sewer and water service. The property owner may notify
the city in writing of his or her consent to annexation. If within ten (10)
days of the property owner's receipt of such notice, the property owner
contacts the city and makes firm arrangements, in writing, to discontinue sewer
and water service, then the city shall not further pursue obtaining the
property owner's consent. If, however, the property owner has not, within ten
(10) days, made firm written arrangements to discontinue sewer and water
service, then the city shall be entitled to treat the property owner as having
consented to annexation of his or her property upon the expiration of such ten
(10) day period. The failure by the property owner to respond in writing within
ten (10) days shall entitle the city to treat the property owner as having
consented upon the expiration of such ten (10) day period.
If the property owner consents to annexation under any of the methods described
above, the property owner may not thereafter withdraw his or her consent to any
proposed annexation of his or her property. If the property owner consents to
annexation under any of the methods described above, then the city shall be
entitled to disregard any protest that such property owner makes to a proposed
annexation of his or her property. Nothing herein shall prevent the city from
seeking consent even if the city has previously obtained a waiver of protest
from such property owner or from his or her predecessor in interest. (Ord. 292-
05-06, 3-28-2006)
CHAPTER 3
WELLHEAD PROTECTION
SECTION:
9-3-1: Short Title
9-3-2: Intent
9-3-3: Definitions
9-3-4: Regulated Substances
9-3-5: Prohibited Activities
9-3-6: Restrictions Within Wellhead Protection Areas
9-3-7: Required Permits
9-3-8: Exhibit A, Regulated Substances List
9-3-1: SHORT TITLE:
This Chapter will be known as the THREE FORKS WELLHEAD PROTECTION ORDINANCE.
The provisions of this Chapter will be effective within the City and the Mayor
is hereby vested with the power to enforce the terms of this Chapter. This
Chapter will establish prohibitions and restrictions to prevent public water
supply contamination by hazardous or toxic substances. This Chapter shall be
liberally construed to effect its purpose. (Ord. 225, 1993)
9-3-2: INTENT:
In order to protect existing and future water supply wells serving the City,
the City Council declares that the storage, handling, use, production, or
disposal of hazardous or toxic substances in the zone of contribution to public
water supply wells is potentially harmful to the drinking water of the City and
that certain activities are prohibited and regulated within certain defined
wellhead protection areas. (Ord. 225, 1993)
9-3-3: DEFINITIONS:
The following definitions apply within this Chapter:
   ADMINISTERING AGENCY: City building office as supervised by the Mayor.
   AQUIFER: A ground water bearing geologic formation or formations that
contain enough saturated, permeable material to yield significant quantities of
water.
   CONTAMINATION: The presence of any harmful or deleterious substances in the
drinking supply.
   DRINKING WATER: Water that is satisfactory for drinking, for culinary and
domestic purposes, and that meets current State and Federal drinking water
standards.
   GROUND WATER: Water that fills all the unblocked pores of underlying
material below the water table which is the upper limit of saturation, or water
which is held in the unsaturated zone by capillarity.
   HANDLE: To use, generate, process, produce, package, treat, store, emit,
discharge, or dispose of a regulated substance.
   REGULATED SUBSTANCE: A hazardous or toxic substance regulated under Section
9-3-4 of this Chapter.
   THREE FORKS AQUIFER: The aquifer underlying the City of Three Forks which
supplies the area with water.
   WELLHEAD: The physical structure, facility, or device at the land surface
from or through which ground water flows or is pumped from subsurface, water-
bearing formations.
   WELLHEAD PROTECTION AREA: The surface and subsurface area surrounding a
water well or well field supplying a public water system, through which
contaminants are reasonably likely to move toward and reach such water well or
well field which is determined to have a one hundred foot (100') radius from
the well.
   ZONE OF CONTRIBUTION: The area surrounding a pumping well that encompasses
all areas or features that supply ground water recharge to the well. (Ord. 225,
1993)
9-3-4: REGULATED SUBSTANCES:
   A.   Hazardous And Toxic Substances: The substances to be regulated include
certain known hazardous or toxic substances which may cause contamination of
the Three Forks aquifer.
   B.   List Of Substances; Periodic Review: The substances to be regulated are
those set forth on, or referred to in, the list entitled "Exhibit A, Regulated
Substances", Section
9-3-8 of this Chapter. The list will be reviewed and revised as necessary by
formal amendment of this Chapter. A mixture shall be deemed a regulated
substance if it contains more than one percent (1%) by volume of any regulated
substance.
   C.   Exceptions: This Chapter shall not apply to regulated substances that:
      1.   Are handled in a quantity less than or equal to the household
quantity listed for that substance in Exhibit A, Section
9-3-8 of this Chapter;
      2.   Are contained in consumer products packaged for distribution to, and
use by, the general public for personal or household purposes;
      3.   Are contained in commercial office supplies used by a business not
engaged in commercial printing or reproduction;
      4.   Are contained in a vehicle fuel tank. (Ord. 225, 1993)
9-3-5: PROHIBITED ACTIVITIES:
The following activities are prohibited within wellhead protection areas:
   A.   The drilling of private water wells, for any purpose;
   B.   The drilling of injection wells;
   C.   The establishment or creation of dumps or landfills. (Ord. 225, 1993)
9-3-6: RESTRICTIONS WITHIN WELLHEAD PROTECTION AREAS:
   A.   Permit Required: Any person who engages in an activity involving the
handling of regulated substances within a wellhead protection area after the
date of adoption of this Chapter may do so only after obtaining a ground water
noncompliance permit. Such continuing activity shall be referred to as "legal
noncomplying activity". No person shall engage in any new activity involving
the handling of regulated substances within a wellhead protection area without
a permit.
   B.   Conditions Of Permit: Legal noncomplying activities may be continued
and maintained as long as the person engaged in such activity maintains a
ground water noncompliance permit, subject to the following conditions:
      1.   No legal noncomplying activity may be enlarged or increased or
expanded or altered so as to substantially increase the risk of contamination
from such activity in the judgment of the administering agency;
      2.   Any legal noncomplying activity that is discontinued or abandoned or
ceases for a period of six (6) months shall not be considered a legal
noncomplying activity, and thereafter may not be resumed; (Ord. 225, 1993)
      3.   In the event a facility which houses a legal noncomplying activity
is destroyed or damaged by any means to an extent of fifty percent (50%) or
more (as determined by a State building inspector), the activity involving the
handling of regulated substances shall not thereafter be considered a legal
noncomplying activity and may not thereafter be resumed or continued. (Ord.
225, 1993; amd. 2000 Code)
9-3-7: REQUIRED PERMITS:
   A.   Ground Water Noncompliance Permit:
      1.   Obtaining Permit: All persons required to obtain a ground water
noncompliance permit within a wellhead protection area shall obtain that permit
within one month after the adoption of this Chapter.
      2.   Duration Of Permits: Ground water noncompliance permits must be
renewed every three (3) years. Permits shall expire on December 31 of the third
year.
      3.   Permit Application: All applications for ground water noncompliance
permits must be filed with the administering agency prior to the deadline for
obtaining an initial permit or expiration of an existing permit. All
applications shall contain a completed ground water noncompliance permit
application form, which shall be available from the administering agency.
      4.   Fees: The application fee for a ground water noncompliance permit
shall be fifty dollars ($50.00). This fee must be received by the administering
agency at the time of the application.
      5.   Permit Issuance: The administering agency shall issue a ground water
noncompliance permit upon finding that:
         a.   The permit application is complete; and
         b.   All applicable fees have been paid.
   B.   Permit Specifications: The ground water noncompliance permit shall
authorize the applicant to handle regulated substances identified in the
application in quantities not to exceed those specified therein. The acceptance
of a ground water noncompliance permit shall authorize an agent of the City to
enter and inspect the facility subject to the permit. (Ord. 225, 1993)
9-3-8: EXHIBIT A, REGULATED SUBSTANCES LIST:

CHAPTER 4
SEWER SERVICE RATES AND CHARGES
SECTION:
9-4-1: Basic Sewer Rates
9-4-2: Connection With City Wastewater (Sewer) System Required
9-4-3: Residential And Travel-Trailer Park Sewer Rates
9-4-4: Sewer Hookup Fees
9-4-5: Collection Of Rates
9-4-6: Exception To Nonindustrial User Rates
9-4-7: User Charge System Review And Revision
9-4-8: Wastewater Treatment Services; Notice Of Rate
9-4-9: Service To Imerys (A Corporation, Or Its Successors)
9-4-10: Enforcement; Duties Of Law Enforcement
9-4-11: Penalties
9-4-1: BASIC SEWER RATES:
Sewer Rates: All owners of buildings connected to the public sewer system are
liable for sewage rates. In Residential Zoning Districts, and in all mobile
home parks, multi-family structures shall be subject to the minimum sewer
charge for each dwelling unit. The rate shall be fixed and established by
resolution of the city council. From initial sign up until an average rate is
reached, customers will be set up on a household size basis as defined below.
The average sewer rate is based upon the water usage for the months of
December, January, February and March of the preceding year. The rates are
computed each fiscal year and the new rate to be in effect July of each year.
If water was not used during the month(s) of December, January, February or
March, the sewer rate computation would be made on the basis of any four (4)
months of use in the year. A utility customer may petition the city council to
amend the determination of the household size/average sewer rate and present
evidence in support of the customer's petition. It shall be the duty of each
customer to notify the city when circumstances have arisen which result in a
change in the designated household size/average sewer rate.
   A.   Customers Receiving Water And Sewer Utility Service:
      1.   First Four Hundred Cubic Feet: The base rate for the first four
hundred (400) cubic feet of water flow and usage shall be fixed and established
by resolution of the city council.
      2.   Over Four Hundred Cubic Feet: All water flow and usage that exceeds
four hundred (400) cubic feet shall be fixed and established by resolution of
the city council.
      3.   Household Size Defined: "Household size" is defined as the number of
human beings six (6) years or older living in and utilizing the sewage
connections, including sinks and toilets, within a unit. Every two (2) human
beings under the age of six (6) will constitute one person in determining
household size. Household size shall be used to establish rates for commercial
and nonresidential rates.
   B.   Customers Receiving Sewer Utility Service Only:
      1.   Fixed Rate: Monthly sewer rate for customers not receiving water
utility services shall be fixed and established by resolution of the city
council.
      2.   Household Size Defined: "Household size" is defined as the number of
human beings six (6) years or older living in and utilizing the sewage
connections, including sinks and toilets, within a unit. Every two (2) human
beings under the age of six (6) will constitute one person in determining
household size. Household size shall be used to establish rates for commercial
and nonresidential rates.
      3.   Determination And Notification Of Household Size: The city clerk
shall notify each present sewer utility customer of the prescribed sewer charge
and the number of the household size as determined by the clerk. The clerk's
determination shall be binding upon the utility customer and shall be the basis
for the future utility assessment unless and until a sewer customer receives a
new determination from the city council.
   C.    Travel-trailer parks will be charged the minimum sewer connection
charge, as determined by resolution adopted by the City Council,    per sewer
connection ordinances in place. If the travel-trailer park is seasonal, which
means connected to the system and shut off for use during a portion of the
year, the owner is obligated to pay for no less than one inactive service
connection for the travel-trailer park.(Ord. 356-15, 2-24-2015; amd. Ord. 385-
2019, 10-8-2019; Ord. 389-2021, 8-10-2021)
9-4-2: CONNECTION WITH CITY WASTEWATER (SEWER) SYSTEM REQUIRED:
   A.    Every building which produces gray water, sewage or discharge of any
type is required, in a manner authorized by the laws of the State of Montana,
laws, rules and regulations of Gallatin County and the City of Three Forks, to
be connected to the City of Three Forks’ public sewer system.
   B.    Septic Tanks: In no instances shall septic tanks, cesspools, privies,
privy vaults, or other facilities be used for the disposal of sewage, except
where approved in writing by the City Engineer, Water/Wastewater Operator, and
County Sanitarian, and a public sewer is not available. (Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-
2019)
9-4-3: RESIDENTIAL AND TRAVEL-TRAILER PARK SEWER RATES
See section
9-4-1 of this chapter.
(Ord. 335-13, 4-9-2013; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-4: SEWER HOOKUP FEES:
   A.    Fee Imposed: The fee for sewer hookups shall be the actual cost of all
materials, valves and parts and labor necessary to properly complete
installation of service.
   B.    Request For Hookup: Any request for sewer hookup shall be made to the
city clerk, in writing, at least twenty four (24) hours prior to commencement
of installation. Utility hookup will not occur during weekends, evenings,
holidays, or other times when city personnel are not available for inspection.
   C.    Authorized Installers: Only those contractors, persons, firms and
corporations who are bonded by a surety authorized to conduct business within
the state are authorized to install the utility service. (Ord. 228, 7-26-1994;
amd. 318-09-10, 11-24-2009; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-5: COLLECTION OF RATES:
Each user of the sewage utility will be deemed to have contracted and agreed to
pay the sewage charges hereby imposed, and such charges may be collected by
action at law whenever the same are more than thirty (30) days overdue and
shall bear interest, at the highest rate allowed by law for contract
indebtedness, from and after the twentieth day of the month when the charge
becomes due and payable. (Ord. 192, 8-13-1980; amd. Ord. 231, 1995; amd. Ord.
385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-6: EXCEPTION TO NONINDUSTRIAL USER RATES:
Nonindustrial users with above normal domestic waste strength shall be liable
for an industrial sewer rate based on the formula described in section
9-5-6 of this title. (Ord. 192, 8-13-1980; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-7: USER CHARGE SYSTEM REVIEW AND REVISION:
The city shall review the user charge system not less than every two (2) years
and shall revise the system as necessary to assure equality of the system and
to assure that sufficient funds will be collected to adequately operate and
maintain the system. (Ord. 192, 8-13-1980; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-8: WASTEWATER TREATMENT SERVICES; NOTICE OF RATE:
The user will be notified at least annually, in conjunction with a regular
bill, of the rate and that portion of the user's charges which are attributed
to wastewater treatment services. (Ord. 192, 8-13-1980; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-
8-2019)
9-4-9: SERVICE TO IMERYS (A CORPORATION, OR ITS SUCCESSORS):
The city will provide water and sewer services to Imerys, as per agreement
dated March 27, 2001, for a period of twenty (20) years without requiring
annexation into the city. In pertinent part, the agreement provides that Imerys
will pay the city for water and sewer services, on a monthly basis, based on
the amount of flow through the sewer line, and on the applicable rates
described in the city's water and sewer ordinances. The city shall review rates
for water and sewer service provided outside of the city limits and
specifically under the agreement and set the rate by separate resolution. (Ord.
360-15, 7-28-2015; amd. Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-10: ENFORCEMENT; DUTIES OF LAW ENFORCEMENT:
   A.    It shall be the duty of law enforcement officers to give vigilant aid
to the water/wastewater operator in the enforcement of all rules and
regulations and to this end they shall report all violations thereof which may
come to their attention.
   B.    The law enforcement officers shall work with the City Attorney at the
direction of the Mayor on enforcement issues. (Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)
9-4-11: PENALTIES:
Unless otherwise provided, any person, firm, corporation, architect, plumber or
contractor, or other person who shall be found guilty of violating any of the
rules and regulations of this chapter, or who shall fail or neglect to comply
with the provisions contained therein, shall, upon conviction thereof, be
subject to penalty as provided in Section
1-4-1 of this code; provided, however, that when the offense is one which
relates to rentals, leakage or illegal use of wastewater, the water/wastewater
operator may cause the water supply to be shut off and the offender shall
forfeit all payments that may have been made for same. When the water has been
turned off for violation of this chapter, it shall not be turned on again until
connections are repaired and approved by the water/wastewater operator, city
engineer, county sanitarian and all amounts due have been paid, including the
fee to turn on/off as per
9-2-11 of this title. (Ord. 385-2019, 10-8-2019)

PASS THROUGH:  other sources, is a cause of a violation of any requirement of the City of Three

               Any individual, partnership, co-partnership, firm, company, corporation,

               The reduction of the amount of pollutants, the elimination of pollutants, or the

PRETREATMENT:  of, a discharge of such pollutants into the POTW. This reduction or alteration can
